## P0 (10 items)

### P0.1 [vimmi-mi] pmm=TRUE with defaults yields identical multiple imputations (zero between-variance) and the safeguard warning is explicitly bypassed
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

For MI, PMM must be stochastic. But vimpute's pmm defaults are deterministic: map_pmm_k sets k=1 when pmm=TRUE and pmm_k=NULL (helper_vimpute.R:669 'out[[v]] <- if (isTRUE(pmm[[v]])) 1L else NULL'), and pmm_k_method defaults to "mean" (vimpute.R:160), so even k>1 aggregates deterministically (mean of donors is not a draw — invalid PMM even for single imputation). With no boot the fitted model is fixed, so the nearest donor is fixed, so all m imputations are identical and mice::pool gets B=0 (SEs collapse to complete-data SEs). Worse, the m>1 safeguard at vimpute.R:339-343 skips the warning precisely when has_any_pmm is TRUE (vimpute.R:333, 340), so the user gets silently invalid MI. Verified: vimpute(sleep, method="robust", pmm=TRUE, m=3, nseq=2) → imp$NonD and imp$Dream literally identical across all 3 imputations (SD of column means = 0), no warning emitted (the residual variation in Sleep/Span/Gest came only from lmrob's internal subsampling RNG, not from any MI mechanism). Fix: for m>1 require stochastic PMM (default pmm_k>=5 with pmm_k_method="random", ideally combined with boot=TRUE for parameter uncertainty, as mice does via Bayesian beta draws), or at minimum extend the vimpute.R:340 warning to fire when PMM is deterministic (k==1 or agg != "random") and boot=FALSE. Repro: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/t1_pmm.R

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:333 (has_any_pmm), 339-343 (warning condition '!has_any_pmm'), 160 (pmm_k_method="mean" default); helper_vimpute.R:669 (k=1 default). Empirical: sleep, method=robust, pmm=TRUE, m=3 → NonD/Dream imputations identical across m, no warning.

**Verifier:** Code reading verifies every cited location: helper_vimpute.R:669 defaults pmm_k to 1L when pmm=TRUE and pmm_k=NULL; vimpute.R:160 defaults pmm_k_method="mean"; the PMM donor step (helper_vimpute.R:2101-2126) computes order(abs(score_obs-s))[1:k] and aggregates with mean()/median() — no RNG for k=1 or agg="mean" (verified: pmm_donor_selection with k=5/"mean" returns identical values under different seeds). The m>1 safeguard at vimpute.R:339-343 is conditioned on !has_any_pmm (vimpute.R:333,340), so pmm=TRUE suppresses it exactly as claimed. Empirical repro: (a) exact claimed setup vimpute(sleep, method="robust", pmm=TRUE, m=3, nseq=2) -> NonD and Dream bitwise identical across all 3 imputations (between-imputation SD of means = 0), no MI warning emitted; Sleep/Span/Gest varied only via lmrob's internal subsampling RNG (incidental learner noise, not an MI mechanism — consistent with the claim's own caveat). (b) Sharper: with the deterministic learner method="xgboost", pmm=TRUE, m=3 -> ALL five variables bitwise identical across the 3 imputations and no warning, i.e. a vimmi object with exactly zero between-imputation variance delivered silently. (c) Control: same call without pmm correctly fires the 'all imputations will be identical' warning, proving the bypass is specifically the has_any_pmm exclusion. (d) Internal mappers confirm defaults resolve to k=1/"mean" per variable. The methodological point also stands: mean-of-k-donors is a deterministic aggregate, not a random draw, so even pmm_k>1 with the default pmm_k_method="mean" provides no between-imputation variability.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/v1_pmm.R — output: robust run NonD/Dream identical (between-SD 0), no warning; xgboost run ALL variables identical across m=3, no warning; control without pmm fires the warning; default mapping k=1/"mean" confirmed; k=5+"mean" seed-invariant.

### P0.2 [vimmi-mi] boot=TRUE with uncert="none" (and uncert-only without boot) silently produces improper MI; nothing enforces that proper MI needs both parameter draws and residual noise
*kind: method-gap | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Between-imputation variability in the m>1 loop (vimpute.R:419-457, independent re-runs) comes from (a) bootstrap refit of the learner (vimpute.R:1940-1972, parameter uncertainty, analogous to mice norm.boot) and/or (b) inject_uncertainty noise (helper_vimpute.R:1761-1818, residual uncertainty). Proper MI (posterior-predictive draws) requires BOTH. With boot=TRUE, uncert="none" the imputations are conditional means from bootstrap-perturbed models: within-imputation residual variability of the missing values is absent, attenuating variances and covariances. Verified by simulation (n=300, y=2+1.5x+N(0,2), 30% MCAR on y, method="regularized", m=5): pooled SE(beta_x)=0.1054 vs mice norm.boot 0.1709 and even complete-case 0.1475 — a ~40% SE underestimate that will inflate type-I error. Conversely uncert alone without boot lacks parameter uncertainty (theoretically improper, though in this simulation the pooled SE happened to be near-correct at 0.172). The safeguard at vimpute.R:339-343 only fires when ALL sources are absent, and the docs (vimpute.R:89-104) never state that boot and uncert must be combined; only the example at vimpute.R:131-134 happens to show the proper combination. Fix: when m>1, warn (or upgrade defaults) unless boot=TRUE AND (uncert in normalerror/resid OR stochastic PMM); document the properness requirement in @param m and the vimmi help page. Repro: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/t3_improper.R

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:339-343 (warning only when !boot && uncert==none && !pmm); vimpute.R:1940-1978; helper_vimpute.R:1761-1818. Simulation: pooled SE(beta_x) 0.105 (boot+none) vs 0.171 (mice norm.boot) vs 0.148 (complete-case).

**Verifier:** Code: with boot=TRUE the learner is refit on a bootstrap resample (vimpute.R:1940-1972) but predictions for missing rows remain point predictions — inject_uncertainty(method="none") returns preds unchanged (helper_vimpute.R:1777), so imputations are conditional means of bootstrap-perturbed models with no residual draw. The only safeguard (vimpute.R:339-343) fires solely when boot=FALSE AND uncert=="none" AND no pmm; the @param docs (vimpute.R:89-105) and the vignette section on boot/robustboot/uncert (vignettes/vimpute.Rmd:386-407) never state that proper MI requires combining parameter uncertainty (boot) with residual/PMM noise (uncert) — only the examples happen to show good combinations. Independent empirical reproduction (n=300, y=2+1.5x+N(0,2), 30% MCAR on y, method="regularized", m=5): pooled SE(beta_x)=0.1054 with boot=TRUE/uncert="none" (0.1044 under a second seed — stable), versus complete-case SE 0.1475, vimpute boot+normalerror 0.1481, vimpute normalerror-only 0.1720, mice norm.boot 0.1709. Since y is MCAR with no auxiliary variables, MI cannot legitimately beat the complete-case SE, so 0.105 is a ~29% SE underestimate (anti-conservative inference). Mechanism visible in the imputations: within-imputation SD of imputed y is 2.03 (spread of fitted values only) vs 2.8-3.1 for the proper variants, confirming the missing residual component (true residual sd=2). Note the existing warning text would even be wrong to extend verbatim here — boot alone DOES produce distinct imputations (between-imputation SD 0.109 > 0); the defect is statistical improperness that the API neither prevents nor documents, exactly as claimed (method-gap, not a coding bug).

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/v2_improper.R — pooled SEs: 0.1054 (boot+none, 0.1044 seed 12345) < 0.1475 (complete case) vs 0.1481 (boot+normalerror), 0.1720 (normalerror only), 0.1709 (mice norm.boot).

### P0.3 [cellwise] cellIRWLS multiplies raw design values by cell weights, making cellIRMI/cellM/cellMCD imputations worse than median imputation even on clean data
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/cellwise_utils.R*

R/cellwise_utils.R:498 builds X_tilde <- sqrt_w_row * w_cell_int * X_int, i.e. cell weights scale the raw (uncentered) predictor values. Tukey/Huber weights are < 1 for any cell with |u|>0, so on perfectly clean data weights vary in ~[0.3, 1] (observed), and multiplying values like x~100 by them injects multiplicative noise ~70x larger than the predictor's real variation, annihilating the slope. Affects imputeCellIRMI (R/imputeCellwise.R:307), imputeCellM (:679), and imputeCellMCD's imputation step (R/imputeCellEM.R:1314-1321). imputeCellEM is unaffected (Gaussian conditional means). This directly defeats the strategic bar: the flagship cellwise methods lose to unconditional median imputation on clean data and to plain irmi(robust=TRUE) under actual cellwise contamination. Fix: never scale raw design values — use convex shrinkage toward a robust center (x_eff = w*x + (1-w)*mu_j, so w=1 keeps x and w=0 substitutes the center), or set low-weight cells to conditional expectations before an ordinary robust fit (as in the cellMCD/DDC detect-then-impute paradigm), keeping w_cell out of the LS design. Add a clean-data efficiency regression test (see test-gap finding).

**Evidence:** Isolation test: cellIRWLS(X, y) with w_cell from cellWeightsMCD on CLEAN data (x~N(100,2), y=2x+e, R2~0.94) returns slope 0.034 (intercept 197 = mean y); with unit weights slope 2.034. End-to-end: imputeCellIRMI RMSE 3.54 (default), 3.44 (hard_threshold=0), 3.41 (huber) vs lm 0.955 vs median-imputation 3.455; centered variant still 3.10. Contaminated data (5% cells +30): cellIRMI RMSE 3.22 vs irmi robust 1.51. Cell weight range on clean data: [0.323, 1].

**Verifier:** Code reading confirms R/cellwise_utils.R:498 (.weighted_qr_solve) builds X_tilde <- sqrt_w_row * w_cell_int * X_int, i.e. Tukey/Huber cell weights multiply the raw uncentered predictor values (the intercept column keeps weight 1, lines 355-357), and the roxygen docs at cellwise_utils.R:280-287 document exactly this formula — so it is the designed algorithm, and the design is statistically broken. Call sites confirmed: R/imputeCellwise.R:307 (imputeCellIRMI, with w_cell = W[,pred_cols] and w_response = W[,j] from cellWeightsMCD), R/imputeCellwise.R:679 (imputeCellM), R/imputeCellEM.R:1314-1321 (imputeCellMCD imputation step via cellIRWLS). Empirical reproduction with the pre-installed build: (1) Isolation — clean data x~N(100,2), y=2x+e (R2=0.93, n=200); the package's own cellWeightsMCD weights range [0.305, 1] on this clean data; VIM:::cellIRWLS with those weights returns slope 0.0755 and intercept 193.3 (= approx mean(y)=200) vs slope 1.9862 with unit weights. Mechanism isolated: w_cell alone gives slope 0.071, w_response alone gives 1.966 — the raw-value scaling by w_cell is the cause. (2) End-to-end, 10 replications, 20% MCAR in y on clean data — mean RMSE: imputeCellIRMI 4.17, imputeCellIRMI(uncert='none') 4.34, imputeCellMCD 5.06, imputeCellM 5.87, unconditional median 4.35, lm 0.97. cellMCD and cellM are clearly WORSE than median imputation; cellIRMI is statistically indistinguishable from median (in my seeds marginally better, in the claimant's marginally worse — either way it extracts essentially none of the R2=0.93 signal that lm exploits at RMSE 0.97). (3) Contaminated data (5% of x cells +30), 10 reps: cellIRMI RMSE 4.23 vs plain irmi(robust=TRUE) 1.31 — the cellwise flagship loses badly to the rowwise-robust classic under the exact contamination model it targets. The claim's headline numbers differ slightly from mine (different seeds) but every qualitative statement reproduces. Only nuance: 'worse than median' is strictly true for cellMCD/cellM; for cellIRMI it is 'no better than median' within noise. Core P0 finding stands.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim1_cellirwls.R (Parts A-C: isolation slope test, clean-data end-to-end RMSE vs median/lm, contaminated vs irmi robust) plus the mechanism side-check at the top of scratchpad/claim2_cellreg.R (w_cell-only slope 0.071 vs w_response-only 1.966). Output observed: weights [0.305,1] on clean data; slope 0.0755 vs 1.9862; RMSE cellIRMI 4.17 / cellMCD 5.06 / cellM 5.87 / median 4.35 / lm 0.97; contaminated cellIRMI 4.23 vs irmi robust 1.31.

### P0.4 [classic-integration] imputeRobustChain() imputes zeros by default; multiple guaranteed crash paths masked via globalVariables
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeRobustChain.R*

With defaults (uncert="pmm"), selectDonor defines my_distance_function inside the loop but never calls it (R/imputeRobustChain.R:416-437), so donors stay numeric(length(val))=0 and ymiss = pred + (0 - pred) = 0: every missing numeric value is imputed as 0. Verified: imputeRobustChain(sleep[,1:5]) returns 0 for all NonD missings. Further dead-on-arrival paths: method="gam" never assigns mod (:345,:358 -> 'mod' not found); method="lm"+robustboot uses undefined alpha (:322); bin/count types call nonexistent useLogistic/useGLMpoisson (:236-237); the convergence criterion is never updated (criteria set once at :147, d computed at :213 but never assigned to criteria, so it always runs maxit); the nominal branch fits lm() on a factor response and references mod$best before definition (:275-277); outCoDa needs pivotCoord (robCompositions, not a dependency, :126). All undefined symbols are silenced in R/zzz.R:8-9 (utils::globalVariables includes 'alpha','factors','pivotCoord','robGAM','supportedMethods','useGLMpoisson','useLogistic','x_reg'). Roxygen is still the placeholder template (FUNCTION_TITLE / PARAM_DESCRIPTION, :1-17). Recommendation: defunct it or reimplement as a thin vimpute(sequential=TRUE, method="robust", boot=, uncert=) wrapper; do not ship as-is in a CRAN release.

**Evidence:** Run on VIM 7.1.0 build: imputeRobustChain(data=sleep[,c("BodyWgt","BrainWgt","NonD","Dream","Sleep")]) -> all imputed NonD values are 0. zzz.R:7-10 lists the undefined symbols. No test_imputeRobustChain*.R exists in inst/tinytest.

**Verifier:** Core claim reproduced on the pre-installed build: imputeRobustChain(data=sleep[,c("BodyWgt","BrainWgt","NonD","Dream","Sleep")]) returned exactly 0 for ALL 30 originally-missing cells (14 NonD, 12 Dream, 4 Sleep). Root cause verified at R/imputeRobustChain.R:416-437: inside selectDonor, my_distance_function is defined in the loop body but never invoked, so donors stays numeric(length(val)) = all zeros; then residuals = 0 - pred[index] and ymiss = pred[index] + residuals = 0. Crash paths all confirmed empirically: method="gam" -> "Objekt 'mod' nicht gefunden" (mgcv::gam result never assigned at :345/:358); method="lm" with robustboot=TRUE -> "Objekt 'alpha' nicht gefunden" (:322; alpha is not a parameter of useRobustNumeric); any factor column -> "konnte Funktion 'pivotCoord' nicht finden" (:126; robCompositions appears nowhere in DESCRIPTION); logical column -> crash. Convergence criterion confirmed dead: criteria set once at :147, never reassigned in the while body (:149-220), d computed at :212-219 but unused; trace run with maxit=3 showed exactly 3 iterations. zzz.R:7-10 masks alpha, factors, pivotCoord, robGAM, supportedMethods, useGLMpoisson, useLogistic, x_reg from R CMD check. Roxygen is the placeholder template (FUNCTION_TITLE/PARAM_DESCRIPTION, :1-18), and grep finds no imputeRobust* test in inst/tinytest. One mechanical correction that does not change the verdict: the bin branch never actually reaches useLogistic, because imp() is called with the raw types[i] (:197), not the mapped meth (:164-175 is computed but only used for trace messages). Factor levels are relabelled "binary"/"nominal", never "bin", so binary/logical/integer columns fall through the switch (:231-240) to NULL and crash with "Ersetzung hat Länge 0" (length-zero replacement) — reproduced for both a logical and an integer column; integer columns crashing is an additional dead path beyond the claim. useLogistic/useGLMpoisson (:236-237) indeed do not exist anywhere in the package (grep confirms; count branch would hit the missing-function error only for a literal class "count" column). The nominal-branch defects (:275 lm on factor response, :277 mod$best self-reference before assignment) are confirmed by reading but are unreachable in practice because the pivotCoord crash at :126/:141 fires first whenever a factor exists. Substance of the claim — zeros by default, every non-numeric path dead on arrival, undefined symbols silenced in zzz.R — is fully correct.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep); d5 <- sleep[,c("BodyWgt","BrainWgt","NonD","Dream","Sleep")]; r <- imputeRobustChain(data=d5); print(r$NonD[is.na(d5$NonD)]); print(try(imputeRobustChain(data=d5, method="gam"))); print(try(imputeRobustChain(data=d5, method="lm", robustboot=TRUE)))' — imputed NonD all 0; gam errors "Objekt 'mod' nicht gefunden"; lm+robustboot errors "Objekt 'alpha' nicht gefunden". Adding a factor column errors "konnte Funktion 'pivotCoord' nicht finden"; logical/integer columns error "Ersetzung hat Länge 0". trace=TRUE, maxit=3 prints "start of iteration" exactly 3 times.

### P0.5 [deps-arch] imputeRobustChain() silently imputes 0 for every missing value in its default configuration; every other code path errors
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeRobustChain.R*

The default path (method='lts', uncert='pmm') is silently wrong: in R/imputeRobustChain.R:416-439 `selectDonor()` initialises `donors <- numeric(length(val))` (all zeros), then wraps the actual donor draw inside a closure `my_distance_function` (lines 425-431) that is never called, so it returns all zeros; `ymiss <- pred[index] + (selectDonor(...) - pred[index])` collapses to exactly 0. Reproduced on the installed 7.1.0 build: variables ~N(50,5) get imputed value 0 for all NAs (imputeRobust() on the same data gives ~50). All other paths error: any factor column -> `pivotCoord()` not found (R/imputeRobustChain.R:126, called via the copied outCoDa at line 141; robCompositions is declared nowhere in DESCRIPTION); integer/binary/ordered/logical targets -> `imp()` (lines 230-241) is passed raw `type = types[i]` (line 197) but switches on 'numeric/nominal/bin/count', so 'integer'/'binary' fall through to NULL -> 'replacement has length zero' (the correct `meth` mapping computed at lines 164-174 is never passed); 'bin'/'count' branches call `useLogistic`/`useGLMpoisson` (lines 236-237), functions that do not exist anywhere in the package, with undefined args `x_reg`, `ndata`, `step`, `robust` (leftovers from irmi.R's getM at R/irmi.R:415); method='gam' -> mgcv::gam result never assigned to `mod` (line 345) -> 'object mod not found'; method='lm' -> 'object alpha not found'. The function is exported, has placeholder roxygen docs (FUNCTION_TITLE/PARAM_DESCRIPTION, plus a `familiy` arg typo), and has zero tinytest coverage (no imputeRobustChain test in inst/tinytest/). Every one of these defects was hidden from R CMD check by utils::globalVariables() in R/zzz.R (see separate finding). Recommend: fix selectDonor + imp() dispatch, define or remove the bin/count/gam branches, declare robCompositions or inline pivot coordinates, add tests -- or deprecate the function until it works, since a default-path silent-zero imputation is worse than no function for the 'beats mice' story.

**Evidence:** Reproduced on installed build: imputeRobustChain(data.frame(a=rnorm(80,50,5),b,c) with 5 NAs) returns 0,0,0,0,0 for the missing cells; method='gam' -> 'Objekt mod nicht gefunden'; method='lm' -> 'Objekt alpha nicht gefunden'; factor column -> 'konnte Funktion pivotCoord nicht finden'; integer column -> 'Ersetzung hat Laenge 0'. Code: R/imputeRobustChain.R:126, 141, 194-208, 230-241, 343-350, 416-439.

**Verifier:** Core claim fully reproduced on the installed 7.1.0 build. Default call imputeRobustChain(data=d) on numeric data ~N(50,5) with 5 NAs returned exactly 0, 0, 0, 0, 0 for the missing cells (imputeRobust() on the same data returned 42.0-50.6). Mechanism verified in code: R/imputeRobustChain.R:416-435 selectDonor() initialises donors <- numeric(length(val)) (all zeros) and only DEFINES the closure my_distance_function (lines 425-431) containing the actual donor draw — it is never invoked — so selectDonor returns all zeros and ymiss <- pred[index] + (0 - pred[index]) collapses to exactly 0 (lines 436-437). All enumerated broken paths reproduced verbatim: method='gam' -> "object 'mod' not found" (mgcv::gam result never assigned at :345); method='lm' -> "object 'alpha' not found" (:322 uses alpha, which is not a parameter of useRobustNumeric); any factor column -> could not find function "pivotCoord" (:126 inside the copied outCoDa, called at :141; robCompositions appears nowhere in DESCRIPTION or NAMESPACE); integer target -> "replacement has length zero" (imp() switch at :230-241 receives raw types[i]='integer' with no matching branch -> NULL; the correct meth mapping at :164-175 is computed but never passed). useLogistic/useGLMpoisson (:236-237) are defined nowhere in the package. Placeholder roxygen docs (FUNCTION_TITLE/PARAM_DESCRIPTION, 'familiy' typo at :14/:43) confirmed; no tinytest file mentions imputeRobustChain; every involved symbol (alpha, factors, ndata, pivotCoord, robGAM, useGLMpoisson, useLogistic, x_reg, r, p, supportedMethods) is masked via utils::globalVariables in R/zzz.R:7-10. One precision caveat on the title only: 'every other code path errors' is slightly overbroad — method='MM' with default uncert='pmm' also SILENTLY imputes zeros (reproduced: 0,0,0,0,0), and uncert='normalerror'/'resid' with default method='lts' actually work (imputed 46.3-54.3). This makes the defect broader, not narrower; the P0 substance (silent-zero default plus multiple dead/broken paths) stands.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(1); d <- data.frame(a=rnorm(80,50,5), b=rnorm(80,30,2), c=rnorm(80,10,1)); d$a[c(3,10,20,40,77)] <- NA; print(imputeRobustChain(data=d)[c(3,10,20,40,77),"a"])' -> 0 0 0 0 0. Same data: method="gam" -> object 'mod' not found; method="lm" -> object 'alpha' not found; add factor column -> could not find function "pivotCoord"; add integer column with NAs -> replacement has length zero; method="MM" -> also 0 0 0 0 0 (silent). Full script: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/repro_claims12.R

### P0.6 [mice] Native Rubin's-rules pooling: pool(), mipo/mira classes, summary/confint, broom glance/tidy, pool.r.squared, D1/D2/D3 Wald/LR tests, predict_mi pooled prediction
*kind: method-gap (vs mice::pool, mice::D1/D2/D3, mice::predict_mi) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Absent. with.vimmi returns a bare list (R/vimmi.R:178-186); every MI analysis must call mice::pool (mice is only Suggests). VIM cannot complete an MI analysis on its own.

PROPOSAL: Implement pool.vimmi(): have with.vimmi return class c('vimira','list'); pool via broom::tidy per fit + Rubin's rules with Barnard-Rubin df (~50 LOC), print/summary/confint methods. Keep as.mids.vimmi as the bridge for D1/D2/D3 initially; add D1 (multivariate Wald) natively later. This is the single biggest blocker to 'better than mice'.

REFERENCE: R/vimmi.R:178-186, R/vimmi.R:264-283

**Verifier:** No pooling exists anywhere in VIM. NAMESPACE exports no pool/D1/D2/D3/predict_mi; grep over R/ finds only doc references to mice::pool. with.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:178-186) returns a bare unclassed list — functionally verified: class(with(vimmi_obj, lm(...))) == 'list' of lm objects, no vimira class. as.mids.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:264-283) is the only pooling route and requires mice, which is only in Suggests (DESCRIPTION:58). Status as stated is accurate: VIM cannot complete an MI analysis on its own.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("<Rlib>", .libPaths())); library(VIM); "pool" %in% getNamespaceExports("VIM"); mi <- vimpute(sleep[,c("Sleep","Dream","Span","BodyWgt")], method="ranger", sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE, m=3, boot=TRUE, uncert="resid"); class(with(mi, lm(Sleep ~ Dream + Span)))'  # -> FALSE, "list"

### P0.7 [mice] MI/FCS diagnostics: convergence() trace plots, densityplot/stripplot/xyplot/bwplot observed-vs-imputed lattice family on mids
*kind: method-gap (vs mice::convergence, mice densityplot/stripplot/xyplot/bwplot methods) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Absent for vimmi/vimpute. pred_history already collects per-iteration predictions (vimpute.R:80-81) but no plot method exists; workaround is as.mids.vimmi + mice's lattice plots (no chain statistics survive the conversion, so convergence plots are lost).

PROPOSAL: plot.vimmi in VIM's native base-graphics style: (a) observed-vs-imputed density/spinogram per variable reusing histMiss/barMiss machinery with VIM's blue/red convention; (b) trace plots of per-iteration means/SDs from pred_history for convergence assessment. VIM is the visualization package — this gap directly undercuts the brand.

REFERENCE: vimpute.R:80-81, R/histMiss.R

**Verifier:** No plot method for vimmi exists (NAMESPACE S3 methods: only plot.aggr). pred_history collects per-iteration predictions (docs vimpute.R:80-81, collection at vimpute.R:2123-2130), but it is even worse than claimed for MI: the m>1 loop hardcodes pred_history = FALSE in its recursive single-imputation calls (vimpute.R:438), so a vimmi object never has traces at all — this also tempers the related win #13 ('full prediction traces'), which holds only for single imputation. Minor nuance not affecting the verdict: mgcv is a 'recommended' package and hence usually present even on noSuggests machines, so glmnet is the practically fatal entry — glmnet alone suffices to ERROR the check. ### P1.2 [vimpute-core] Internal '<var>_zero_prob' column leaks into returned data and into predictors
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

For semicontinuous variables, predict_imputations() adds a working column paste0(var, '_zero_prob') directly to `data` (helper_vimpute.R:1898-1901); it is never removed. It appears in the final returned dataset and, worse, is present in names(data) when subsequent variables build their predictor set (vimpute.R:664 feature_cols <- setdiff(names(data), var)), so later variables and iterations train on a mostly-NA meta column. Confirmed on the pre-installed build: vimpute(data.frame(x1,x2,x3) with x2 semicontinuous, method='ranger', imp_var=FALSE) returns columns 'x1, x2, x3, x2_zero_prob' in both sequential and non-sequential mode. Fix: keep pi_hat in a local structure, or strip *_zero_prob columns before predictor selection and in build_vimpute_result().

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1898-1901 `data[[zero_prob_col]] <- NA_real_; data[[zero_prob_col]][missing_idx] <- pi_hat`; repro: output columns include x2_zero_prob (run on scratchpad Rlib build)

**Verifier:** Code path verified: predict_imputations() adds the working column at helper_vimpute.R:1898-1901, returns the modified `data` in its result list (helper_vimpute.R:2137), and the caller reassigns it at vimpute.R:2115, so the column persists in `data` for the rest of the run. It is never removed: build_vimpute_result (helper_vimpute.R:1828) returns `data` directly when imp_var=FALSE, and feature_cols for every subsequently processed variable is setdiff(names(data), var) (vimpute.R:664), so later variables (and, in sequential mode, ALL variables from iteration 2 on) train on this mostly-NA meta column. Reproduced on the installed 7.1.0 build: with a semicontinuous x2 (VIM:::is_semicontinuous TRUE), vimpute(data.frame(x1,x2,x3), method='ranger', imp_var=FALSE) returns columns 'x1, x2, x3, x2_zero_prob' in both sequential=FALSE and sequential=TRUE/nseq=2 runs; x2_zero_prob has only 8 of 60 non-NA values (the x2 missing rows). One nuance the claim overstates slightly: with imp_var=TRUE (the default) the returned object is data_new, which never receives the column (apply_imputations, helper_vimpute.R:2168-2183, only writes var and *_imp into data_new), so the output leak requires imp_var=FALSE — but the predictor-set contamination via vimpute.R:664 occurs regardless of imp_var because it flows through `data`.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(42); n<-60; x2<-ifelse(runif(n)<0.35,0,abs(rnorm(n,5))); d<-data.frame(x1=rnorm(n),x2=x2,x3=rnorm(n,10)); d$x2[sample(n,8)]<-NA; d$x1[sample(n,6)]<-NA; names(suppressWarnings(vimpute(d, method='ranger', sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE)))  # -> 'x1' 'x2' 'x3' 'x2_zero_prob' (8/60 non-NA)

### P1.3 [vimpute-core] tune=TRUE is silently ignored when sequential=FALSE or nseq=1
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Tuning is triggered only when `i == round(nseq / 2)` (vimpute.R:1202). With sequential=FALSE, nseq is forced to 1 (vimpute.R:326-329), and round(1/2)==0 in R, so the condition is never true: no tuning ever runs, no warning is emitted, and the returned tuning_log claims tuned_better=FALSE as if tuning were evaluated. Confirmed on the build: vimpute(..., sequential=FALSE, tune=TRUE) produces no tuning activity/messages. Same for sequential=TRUE with nseq=1. Given the strategic claim 'hyperparameter tuning via mlr3', the one-shot path silently dropping tuning is a serious usability defect. Fix: use max(1L, round(nseq/2)) or tune at i==1 when nseq==1, and document.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1202 `i == round(nseq / 2)` with nseq coerced to 1 at vimpute.R:326-329; round(0.5)==0; empirical run shows no tuning messages and tuning_log$tuned_better FALSE

**Verifier:** The tuning gate is `!tuning_status[[var]] && isTRUE(tune[[var]]) && i == round(nseq / 2)` (vimpute.R:1202). With sequential=FALSE, nseq is forced to 1 (vimpute.R:326-329; the message there is itself verbose-gated). round(1/2) is 0 in R (IEC 60559 round-half-to-even; verified: round(1/2)==0), and the iteration loop is `for (i in seq_len(nseq))` (vimpute.R:505), i.e. i=1 only — so the gate can never fire for nseq=1. Reproduced on the installed build: with tune=TRUE and verbose=TRUE, the gate-entry debug print at vimpute.R:1210 ('is.null(search_space) = ...'), which fires unconditionally whenever the gate is entered, never appears for sequential=FALSE nor for sequential=TRUE/nseq=1, while it does appear in the contrast run sequential=TRUE/nseq=2 (round(2/2)=1 -> tuned at i=1). No warning is emitted. Worse, the return value still switches to a list containing tuning_log (helper_vimpute.R:1831-1843 keys any_tuned off the tune argument, not off actual tuning), and each per-variable entry reports tuned_better=FALSE (vimpute.R:1421-1428, since hyperparameter_cache[[var]] stays NULL), giving the false impression tuning was evaluated and lost. The docs (vimpute.R:86: 'Tuning is performed halfway through nseq iterations.') never state that tune is inert with the one-shot path.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(7); d<-data.frame(y=rnorm(60),z=rnorm(60,5),w=rnorm(60,2)); d$y[sample(60,8)]<-NA; d$z[sample(60,6)]<-NA; out<-capture.output(r<-suppressWarnings(vimpute(d,method='regularized',sequential=FALSE,tune=TRUE,imp_var=FALSE,verbose=TRUE))); any(grepl('is.null(search_space)',out,fixed=TRUE))  # FALSE (gate never entered); sapply(r$tuning_log,`[[`,'tuned_better') # all FALSE. Contrast: same with sequential=TRUE,nseq=2 -> TRUE

### P1.4 [vimpute-core] vimpute() silently drops all columns not in considered_variables from the output
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

data is subset to considered_variables at vimpute.R:194 and build_vimpute_result() (helper_vimpute.R:1825-1847) returns only that subset; data_all_variables is only used for the m>1 recursion. Confirmed: vimpute(d, considered_variables=c('a','b')) on a 4-column data.frame returns only columns a and b — id and character columns are lost. Every other VIM imputation function (kNN, hotdeck, irmi via imp_var conventions) returns the full dataset. Users doing d <- vimpute(d, considered_variables=...) lose data irreversibly. Fix: merge imputed considered columns back into data_all_variables before returning.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:194 `data <- as.data.table(data)[, considered_variables, with = FALSE]`; repro: output cols 'a, b' only, 'id' and 'keepme' dropped

**Verifier:** Code path verified: data is subset at vimpute.R:194 (`data <- as.data.table(data)[, considered_variables, with = FALSE]`); data_all_variables occurs only at vimpute.R:193 (definition) and vimpute.R:424 (input to the m>1 recursion, which immediately re-subsets), so the full data is never merged back; build_vimpute_result (helper_vimpute.R:1825-1847) returns only the subset (plus *_imp columns). Reproduced on the installed build: vimpute(data.frame(id, a, b, keepme), considered_variables=c('a','b'), sequential=FALSE) returns columns 'a, b, a_imp, b_imp' — 'id' and the character column 'keepme' are silently dropped, with no message or warning. Contrast confirmed: kNN(same data, variable=c('a','b')) returns all of 'id, a, b, keepme, a_imp, b_imp'. The data loss extends to the MI path: with considered_variables=c('a','b') and m=2, complete(result, 1) also returns only 'a, b', because original_data (vimpute.R:401) is a copy of the already-subset data and is stored as the vimmi data slot (vimpute.R:478). The documentation for considered_variables (vimpute.R:8-9: 'excluding irrelevant columns from the imputation process') does not state that excluded columns are removed from the returned dataset, so users have no warning of the row-aligned data loss. Whether the fix is merging back or documenting is a design call, but the claimed silent-drop behavior and inconsistency with the rest of VIM are demonstrated.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(99); d<-data.frame(id=1:60,a=rnorm(60),b=rnorm(60,3),keepme=sample(letters[1:4],60,TRUE)); d$a[sample(60,8)]<-NA; d$b[sample(60,5)]<-NA; names(suppressWarnings(vimpute(d,considered_variables=c('a','b'),sequential=FALSE)))  # -> 'a' 'b' 'a_imp' 'b_imp'; names(kNN(d,variable=c('a','b'))) # keeps id/keepme; complete(suppressWarnings(vimpute(d,considered_variables=c('a','b'),sequential=FALSE,imp_var=FALSE,m=2,boot=TRUE)),1) # only a,b

### P1.5 [vimpute-helpers] Default PMM is deterministic: vimpute(pmm=TRUE, m>1) returns m identical imputations with no warning
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

map_pmm_k defaults to k=1 when pmm_k=NULL (R/helper_vimpute.R:669) and pmm_k_method defaults to 'mean' (R/helper_vimpute.R:771, vimpute() formal default). One donor + mean aggregation is fully deterministic, so with a deterministic learner (robust/gam) every one of the m imputations is identical -> zero between-imputation variance -> Rubin pooling via vimmi/mice silently underestimates SEs. The m>1 safety warning (R/vimpute.R:339-344) explicitly treats pmm as a sufficient variability source and is skipped, and setting pmm also forces uncert='none' (R/vimpute.R:333-337), removing the other variability channel. Repro: d$y with 15 NAs; mi <- vimpute(d, method='robust', pmm=TRUE, m=3, sequential=FALSE); complete(mi,1)$y identical to actions 2 and 3 (verified TRUE). Fix: default pmm_k=5 with pmm_k_method='random' (mice-compatible), or at minimum extend the m>1 warning to deterministic pmm configurations (k=1, or k>1 with mean/median).

**Evidence:** Ran against installed build: vimpute(pmm=TRUE, m=3) -> identical(c1,c2) && identical(c2,c3) == TRUE; no warning emitted. Root lines helper_vimpute.R:669, 771; warning gap vimpute.R:340.

**Verifier:** All cited code locations check out: map_pmm_k defaults pmm_k to 1L when NULL (R/helper_vimpute.R:669), pmm_k_method formal default is 'mean' (R/vimpute.R:160; helper default at R/helper_vimpute.R:771), setting pmm forces uncert='none' (R/vimpute.R:333-337), and the m>1 no-variability warning is skipped whenever any pmm is TRUE because of the '!has_any_pmm' term (R/vimpute.R:340). The PMM donor step (R/helper_vimpute.R:2107-2126) with k=1 picks the single nearest donor via order(), which is deterministic; 'mean' of one neighbor is that neighbor. Reproduced against the installed build: vimpute(d, method='robust', pmm=TRUE, m=3, sequential=FALSE) returned a vimmi with complete(mi,1)$y, complete(mi,2)$y, complete(mi,3)$y all identical (max within-row variance of imputed values = 0) and NO warning; same result with sequential=TRUE. Controls: the same call without pmm emits the 'all imputations will be identical' warning (proving the warning logic treats pmm as a sufficient variability source), and pmm_k=5 with pmm_k_method='random' yields differing imputations (proving the determinism comes from the default k=1/'mean' config). Identical imputations give zero between-imputation variance, so Rubin pooling via vimmi/mice silently underestimates SEs. The claim is fully accurate.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('<scratch>/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(42); n<-120; d<-data.frame(x1=rnorm(n),x2=rnorm(n)); d$y<-2*d$x1-d$x2+rnorm(n,sd=.5); d$y[sample(n,15)]<-NA; mi<-vimpute(d,method='robust',pmm=TRUE,m=3,sequential=FALSE); identical(complete(mi,1)$y,complete(mi,2)$y) && identical(complete(mi,2)$y,complete(mi,3)$y)  # TRUE, no warning emitted

### P1.6 [vimmi-mi] complete(vimmi) stops dispatching as soon as mice is attached — the exact package users must load to pool
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimmi.R*

R/vimmi.R:56-58 defines VIM's own S3 generic 'complete', and complete.vimmi is registered only on that generic (NAMESPACE: S3method(complete,vimmi); the method itself is not exported). mice re-exports the tidyr 'complete' generic, so library(mice) after library(VIM) masks VIM::complete; calling complete(vimmi_obj) then dispatches through mice's generic, which cannot find complete.vimmi, and fails with 'no applicable method for complete applied to an object of class "vimmi"'. Verified empirically (scratchpad/t4_mask.R): works before library(mice), fails after. This is guaranteed to hit real users because as.mids.vimmi's docs and the vimmi help page direct them to mice::pool / mice infrastructure. Fix options: (1) in .onLoad, register complete.vimmi on the tidyr/mice generic when available (registerS3method("complete", "vimmi", ..., envir=asNamespace("tidyr")) or vctrs::s3_register pattern); (2) also export complete.vimmi so users can call it directly; (3) simplest robust route — depend on the generics location mice uses. Note mice's complete signature is (data, ..., fill, explicit) i.e. tidyr's, so VIM's (data, action=1, ...) signature is compatible with dispatch once the method is findable.

**Evidence:** R/vimmi.R:56-58; NAMESPACE lines 'S3method(complete,vimmi)' + 'export(complete)' (complete.vimmi itself not exported). Repro t4_mask.R: after library(mice), complete(obj,1) errors 'nicht anwendbare Methode für complete auf Objekt der Klasse "vimmi"'.

**Verifier:** Code/NAMESPACE: R/vimmi.R:56-58 defines VIM's own S3 generic complete(); NAMESPACE line 5 registers S3method(complete,vimmi) against that generic and line 24 exports the generic, but complete.vimmi itself is not exported (verified: 'complete.vimmi' %in% getNamespaceExports("VIM") is FALSE; it lives only in VIM's .__S3MethodsTable__., not tidyr's). mice 3.19.0's NAMESPACE contains importFrom(tidyr,complete) plus export(complete) and S3method(complete,mids) — i.e. mice re-exports tidyr's generic and registers its own method on it ('complete.mids' IS in tidyr's S3 table). Empirical reproduction with a real vimmi object from vimpute(sleep[,c("Dream","Sleep","Span")], method="xgboost", m=2, boot=TRUE, uncert="resid"): before library(mice), complete(obj,1) works (find("complete") = package:VIM). After library(mice), the visible complete() is tidyr's generic (environmentName = "tidyr", find order package:mice before package:VIM) and complete(obj,1) fails with 'nicht anwendbare Methode für complete auf Objekt der Klasse "vimmi"' — the exact claimed failure. This hits the documented workflow: vimpute.Rd examples, the vimmi help page and the vignette all show plain complete(result, ...) while simultaneously directing users to mice::pool / as.mids.vimmi, so attaching mice after VIM is the natural pooling path. VIM::complete(obj,1) still works and complete(mids) is unaffected, so severity is P1 (workaround exists), matching the claim. One trivial inaccuracy in the claim's detail (irrelevant to the verdict): mice's complete.mids formals are (data, action, include, mild, order, ...) — the (data, ..., fill, explicit) signature quoted belongs to the tidyr generic — but dispatch compatibility of complete.vimmi(data, action=1, ...) holds either way, as stated.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/v3_mask.R — before mice: works; after library(mice): 'nicht anwendbare Methode' error; complete.vimmi absent from tidyr's S3 table and from VIM's exports; VIM::complete() workaround works.

### P1.7 [cellwise] imputeCellReg treats crmReg's continuous cellwise deviations as binary flags, producing negative cell weights
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellReg.R*

R/imputeCellReg.R:257 sets cell_flags <- abs(crm_res$cellwiseoutliers), but crmReg::crm's cellwiseoutliers component is a numeric matrix of deviations (empirically range -2.78..9.29 on a small contaminated example; 8% of |values| > 1), not 0/1 flags. The update W[obs_k,k] <- pmin(W[obs_k,k], 1 - cell_flags[obs_k,k_local]) at :138-139 then writes negative weights into W, which are (a) returned to the user as 'cellweights (1 = clean)', (b) fed as multiplicative response weights into .engine_cellwise_mm (:286 w_row * W[,j], lmrob rejects negative weights, silently triggering the fallback), and (c) clipped to 1e-10 in the multinomial row weights, effectively deleting rows with modest deviations. Additionally the k_local <- match(k, pred_cols) mapping (:135-136) misaligns flag columns whenever factor predictors are dummy-expanded — the shooting-s engine's own comment at :412-414 admits the columns correspond to expanded X, yet the caller indexes them by original predictor position. Fix: threshold deviations to [0,1] weights (e.g. via .apply_weight_fun on standardized deviations), and map flags via the design-matrix column mapping.

**Evidence:** Empirical run with crmReg installed: imputeCellReg(engine='crm') on n=100 data with 5 cellwise outliers returned cellweights range -8.294..1 with 25 negative cells. crmReg::crm cellwiseoutliers verified as 100x2 numeric matrix, range -2.779..9.294.

**Verifier:** Core defect empirically demonstrated. crmReg::crm's cellwiseoutliers component is a continuous numeric matrix, not 0/1 flags: on my n=100 test (5 cellwise outliers in x1, 15 missing y) it is a 100x2 matrix with 40 distinct values, range [-2.25, 11.60], 11% of |values| > 1. R/imputeCellReg.R:257 sets cell_flags <- abs(crm_res$cellwiseoutliers) under the comment 'Cell flags: 1 = outlying, 0 = clean' (:256), and the caller at R/imputeCellReg.R:138-139 writes W[obs_k,k] <- pmin(W[obs_k,k], 1 - cell_flags[obs_k,k_local]) — negative whenever a deviation exceeds 1. End-to-end: imputeCellReg(dna, engine='crm') returned user-facing cellweights with range [-10.598, 1] and 31 negative cells, violating the documented contract 'cellweights: n x p matrix of cell weights (1 = clean)' (R/imputeCellReg.R:18). Propagation path (c) confirmed by code reading: the multinomial row weights clip at pmax(ww, 1e-10) (R/imputeCellReg.R:150), so any cell with deviation > 1 effectively deletes its row. Two secondary details need correction, though they do not change the verdict: (b) the claimed propagation of negative weights into .engine_cellwise_mm (:286, w_row * W[,j]) is unreachable in practice — engines are mutually exclusive per call, and engine='cellwise-mm' never produces cell_flags (returns cell_flags = NULL at :318), so W stays in [0,1] for that engine; negatives arise only under engine='crm', which never calls .engine_cellwise_mm. (b2) For engine='crm' with factor predictors, crmReg::crm itself errors ('The following variables have 0 scale: fb, fc'), so .engine_crm's tryCatch silently falls back to lmrob with cell_flags=NULL — the k_local misalignment is therefore not reached via crm; it IS real for engine='shooting-s' by unambiguous code reading: cell_flags are built on the dummy-expanded design matrix (R/imputeCellReg.R:334-347, 365) with the engine's own comment admitting the mismatch (:412-414), while the caller indexes them by original predictor position via k_local <- match(k, pred_cols) (:135-136), guarded only against out-of-bounds, not misalignment. Core bug (continuous deviations treated as flags -> negative user-facing weights, row-deletion in the multinomial) confirmed.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim2_cellreg.R. Output observed: imputeCellReg(engine='crm') cellweights range [-10.598, 1], 31 negative cells; crm$cellwiseoutliers is 100x2 numeric, 40 distinct values, range [-2.248, 11.598], 11% |v|>1; crm with a factor predictor errors ('variables have 0 scale: fb, fc') triggering the silent lmrob fallback.

### P1.8 [cellwise] imputeCellMCD boot=TRUE fits the bootstrap model and discards it — no parameter-uncertainty propagation despite documentation
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellEM.R*

In the m>1 wrapper (R/imputeCellEM.R:998-1013), the boot=TRUE branch computes res_boot on resampled rows (:1002-1006), then computes res_orig by re-running imputeCellMCD on the ORIGINAL data with the same defaults (:1008-1012) and stores only res_orig (:1013). res_boot is never used — the comment 'Use bootstrapped parameters to impute original data' describes unimplemented behavior. Result: boot=TRUE doubles the runtime and is statistically identical to boot=FALSE (m independent reruns), so between-imputation variance omits parameter uncertainty and downstream Rubin pooling understates total variance, contradicting @param boot ('bootstrap resampling propagates parameter uncertainty across the m imputations', :942-944). Fix: extract mu/Sigma/W from res_boot and run the imputation/uncertainty step on the original data conditional on those parameters (requires factoring the parameter-estimation loop out of the imputation step). Also consider returning a vimmi object instead of the ad-hoc imputed_list for consistency with vimpute(m>1).

**Evidence:** Code: results[[mi]] <- res_orig at R/imputeCellEM.R:1013; res_boot last referenced at :1006. Empirical: m=3 runs, elapsed 0.07s (boot=FALSE) vs 0.13s (boot=TRUE, ~2x = fit-and-discard); between-imputation variance of mean imputed value 1.853 vs 1.891 (no inflation).

**Verifier:** Unambiguous from code and demonstrated byte-for-byte empirically. In the m>1 wrapper (R/imputeCellEM.R:994-1031), the boot=TRUE branch draws boot_idx (:1000), fits res_boot <- imputeCellMCD(data_boot, ...) (:1002-1006), then computes res_orig <- imputeCellMCD(data, ...) on the ORIGINAL data with no argument derived from res_boot (:1008-1012) and stores results[[mi]] <- res_orig (:1013). grep confirms 'res_boot' occurs exactly once in the file (the assignment at :1002) — it is dead computation; the comment at :1007 ('Use bootstrapped parameters to impute original data') describes unimplemented behavior, contradicting @param boot at :942-944 ('bootstrap resampling propagates parameter uncertainty across the m imputations'). Decisive reproduction: with the same seed, imputeCellMCD(d, m=2, boot=TRUE)$imputed_list is identical() (TRUE for both imputations) to manually re-running plain imputeCellMCD(d, m=1, boot=FALSE) on the original data while merely burning the same RNG on a discarded bootstrap fit — i.e., boot=TRUE is distributionally exactly boot=FALSE. Runtime: m=3 elapsed 0.451s (boot=FALSE) vs 1.006s (boot=TRUE), ratio 2.23x — the doubled cost buys nothing. Between-imputation variance of mean imputed value: 0.000141 (boot=FALSE) vs 0.000203 (boot=TRUE), no systematic inflation (any difference is pure RNG noise, as the identical() test proves the same generating process). Consequence as claimed: between-imputation variance omits parameter uncertainty, so downstream Rubin pooling understates total variance.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim3_boot.R. Output observed: 'boot=TRUE imputation 1/2 identical to plain rerun on ORIGINAL data: TRUE TRUE'; elapsed ratio 2.23x; between-imputation var 0.0001406 vs 0.0002034. Also: grep -n res_boot R/imputeCellEM.R -> single hit at line 1002.

### P1.9 [cellwise] Insufficient numerical guards: absolute 1e-10 ridge crashes imputeCellIRMI on n<p or collinear data; .robust_scale fallback of 1 injects N(0,1) noise into constant columns in imputeCellMCD
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/cellwise_utils.R*

(a) .weighted_qr_solve's rank-deficiency fallback (R/cellwise_utils.R:505-510) adds an absolute ridge diag(1e-10, p) before solve(). For n<p designs or duplicated/collinear predictors — especially at large data scales where diag(XtX) ~ 1e11 — the ridge is relatively ~1e-21, so solve() still fails and the error propagates uncaught out of cellIRWLS and aborts imputeCellIRMI entirely. Fix: scale the ridge by mean(diag(XtX)) (e.g. 1e-8 * mean) or use qr.coef with pivoting and zero-fill NA coefficients. (b) .robust_scale (R/cellwise_utils.R:79-82) returns 1 when both MAD and IQR are ~0 (constant columns). That neutral value is harmless for weights (u=0) but leaks into imputeCellMCD's final uncertainty step (R/imputeCellEM.R:1469-1471) as residual sigma, adding sd=1 Gaussian noise in arbitrary data units to imputations in constant/degenerate columns — the method is not scale-equivariant there. cellIRMI (pmm default), cellEM and cellMM handle the same case cleanly. Fix: in the noise step treat degenerate sigma as 0 (skip noise) rather than 1.

**Evidence:** Repro (a): imputeCellIRMI on 10x15 all-numeric data -> 'System ist für den Rechner singulär: reziproke Konditionszahl = 2.2e-16'; duplicated predictor at scale 1e5 -> 'Lapackroutine dgesv: System ist genau singulär: U[3,3] = 0'. imputeCellEM on the same 10x15 data works (warns as designed). Repro (b): column constant=5 with 5 NAs -> imputeCellMCD imputes values in [2.594, 6.582]; cellIRMI/cellEM/cellMM impute exactly 5.

**Verifier:** (a) Reproduced both legs. n<p: imputeCellIRMI on 10x15 rnorm data with 15 NAs aborts with 'system is computationally singular' in 7/10 seeds at scale 1 and 10/10 seeds at scales >=100. withCallingHandlers traceback pins the error to solve(XtX, Xty) at R/cellwise_utils.R:509 inside the rank-deficiency fallback (XtX <- crossprod(X_tilde) + diag(1e-10, p_int) at :507), reached via imputeCellIRMI -> cellIRWLS (R/imputeCellwise.R:307, no tryCatch) -> .weighted_qr_solve (R/cellwise_utils.R:395). imputeCellEM on identical data completes with warnings, as claimed. Collinear-at-scale: an exact duplicate predictor at scale 1e5 aborts with 'Lapack routine dgesv: system is exactly singular: U[4,4] = 0', while the IDENTICAL data divided by 1e5 completes OK — direct proof the absolute ridge is scale-dependent (diag(XtX)~1e12, and 1e12 + 1e-10 == 1e12 in double precision, so duplicated rows of XtX stay exactly identical -> exact zero pivot). (b) Reproduced: data.frame(a=rnorm(40,10,2), b=rnorm(40,-3,1), cc=rep(5,40)) with 5 NAs in cc -> imputeCellMCD (default uncert='conditional') imputes 5.206, 4.639, 5.758, 4.273, 3.632 (range 3.63–5.76, sd 0.822 ~ N(0,1) noise); imputeCellIRMI and imputeCellMM impute exactly 5; imputeCellEM imputes 5.0002/4.9999/... Mechanism verified directly: VIM:::cellIRWLS on the constant response returns sigma = 1 (max |residual| = 8.9e-16 -> mad < .Machine$double.eps -> .robust_scale fallback returns 1 at R/cellwise_utils.R:79-81 per its final-quantities block :443-446), which enters s2 <- max(fit_j$sigma^2, 1e-10) = 1 at R/imputeCellEM.R:1469 and rnorm(., 0, 1) at :1470-1471. One nuance the claim overstates slightly: the trigger requires residuals EXACTLY below machine eps — with constant column = 5000, floating-point residuals ~1e-12 keep mad above eps and no visible noise is injected. This scale-dependence of whether sd=1 noise appears at all actually reinforces the non-equivariance point rather than refuting it; the claim's stated repro (constant=5) reproduces exactly.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(2); X <- matrix(rnorm(150), 10, 15); X[sample(150, 15)] <- NA; imputeCellIRMI(as.data.frame(X))'  # -> Error: system is computationally singular, rcond = 1.95e-16 (from solve() at R/cellwise_utils.R:509). Duplicate-predictor leg: set.seed(2); n<-30; x1<-rnorm(n,0,1e5); x2<-rnorm(n,0,1e5); df<-data.frame(x1,x2,x3=x2,y=x1+x2+rnorm(n,0,1e5)); df$y[sample(n,5)]<-NA; imputeCellIRMI(df) # -> 'dgesv: exactly singular U[4,4]=0'; same data /1e5 completes OK. Noise leg: set.seed(3); dfc<-data.frame(a=rnorm(40,10,2), b=rnorm(40,-3,1), cc=rep(5,40)); dfc$cc[sample(40,5)]<-NA; set.seed(42); imputeCellMCD(dfc)$data_imputed$cc  # imputed 3.63..5.76 instead of 5; imputeCellIRMI/imputeCellMM give exactly 5, imputeCellEM ~5.0001. Mechanism: VIM:::cellIRWLS(VIM:::.build_design_matrix(dfc, 1:2), dfc$cc, w_response=c(rep(0,5),rep(1,35)))$sigma == 1.

### P1.10 [cellwise] Cellwise methods are unreachable from vimpute() — register them via a detection pre-pass plus an mlr3 learner wrapper
*kind: design | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

vimpute()'s registry contains only ranger/regularized/xgboost/robust/gam/robgam (supported_methods at R/helper_vimpute.R:997, learners_list at R/vimpute.R:708-724); grep finds zero cellwise references in vimpute.R/helper_vimpute.R. So the 7.1.0 flagship family gets no per-variable method mixing, no mlr3tuning of alpha/method, and no vimmi-based MI — exactly the three axes where VIM aims to beat mice. Proposal, two complementary paths: (1) Dataset-level pre-pass (recommended first, method-agnostic): add a vimpute argument cellwise = c('none','mcd','ddc') that runs cell-outlier detection on the continuous block (cellWeightsMCD, or cellWise::DDC as already guarded in imputeCellIRMI:207-231), sets observed cells with weight < threshold to NA (the detect-once strategy already implemented at R/imputeCellwise.R:242-261 and R/imputeCellEM.R:1112-1130), then lets any per-variable method impute genuine NAs and outlying cells together; return the weight matrix in the vimpute result for diagnostics. Works immediately with m>1/vimmi and tuning. (2) Per-variable learner: wrap cellIRWLS as a custom learner 'regr.cellrob' following the existing LearnerRegrRobustLM pattern (R/helper_vimpute.R:9-131, registered via mlr3::mlr_learners$add), with a paradox ParamSet for method/alpha/maxit so method='cellrob' becomes tunable per variable. Path 2 requires the P0 cellIRWLS fix first. Joint-model methods (cellEM, cellMCD) do not fit the per-variable learner abstraction — expose them through path 1 or as documented standalone alternatives.

**Evidence:** R/helper_vimpute.R:997 supported_methods <- c('ranger','regularized','xgboost','robust','gam','robgam'); grep -rn 'imputeCell|cellIRMI|cellwise|cellWeights' over R/vimpute.R and R/helper_vimpute.R returns no hits.

**Verifier:** The factual core is confirmed at code and runtime level. R/helper_vimpute.R:997: supported_methods <- c("ranger", "regularized", "xgboost", "robust", "gam", "robgam") — no cellwise entry; the same six methods (and only those) appear in learners_list at R/vimpute.R:708-724 for both numeric and factor targets. grep -rniE 'imputeCell|cellIRMI|cellwise|cellWeights|cellrob' over R/vimpute.R, R/helper_vimpute.R and R/vimmi.R returns zero matches (exit 1). Empirically, vimpute(df, method = "cellirmi") errors with "Unsupported method 'cellirmi'." So the 7.1.0 cellwise family gets none of vimpute's per-variable method mixing, mlr3 tuning, or vimmi-based MI (m>1) — the three axes named in the package's strategic aim. The proposal's cited anchors also check out: the LearnerRegrRobustLM R6 custom-learner pattern exists at R/helper_vimpute.R:9-131 with mlr3::mlr_learners$add("regr.lm_rob", ...) at :131, and the detect-once cell-outlier strategy exists at R/imputeCellwise.R:242-261 and R/imputeCellEM.R:1112-1130, so both proposed integration paths are grounded in existing code. This is a design/enhancement claim, not a bug; the specific remedy is opinion, but the unreachability gap it describes is real and accurately evidenced.

**Repro:** grep -n 'supported_methods' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/helper_vimpute.R  # line 997 lists only ranger/regularized/xgboost/robust/gam/robgam; grep -rniE 'imputeCell|cellIRMI|cellwise|cellWeights|cellrob' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/helper_vimpute.R /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimmi.R  # no matches. Runtime: Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); df <- data.frame(a=rnorm(50), b=rnorm(50)); df$a[1:5] <- NA; vimpute(df, method="cellirmi")'  # -> Error: Unsupported method 'cellirmi'.

### P1.11 [classic-integration] imputeRobust(): method="gamRob" and uncert="wresid" always crash; PMM donor pool contaminated by kNN-initialised values
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeRobust.R*

(a) method="gamRob"/"robGAM"/"robGam" (advertised in supportedMethods, R/imputeRobust.R:47) calls robGAM() at :157, which is not defined anywhere in the package (grep for 'robGAM <- function' finds nothing; the symbol is masked in zzz.R). Verified crash: 'konnte Funktion "robGAM" nicht finden'. (b) uncert="wresid": my_distance_function is defined (:223-229) but never called, so :231 references undefined d. Verified crash: 'Objekt d nicht gefunden'. (c) Unknown uncert values fall through with ymiss undefined (no validation). (d) Statistical leak: missindex is computed at :73, then takeAll=TRUE (default) runs VIM::initialise (kNN-imputes the whole data, :77-79); the PMM donor pool na.omit(data[,ynam]) at :254 is then a no-op, so previously-missing, kNN-initialised y values act as donors, and models/residuals are fit treating initialised values as observed. (e) PMM k is hardcoded to 1:5 (:250). Since vimpute() now exposes boot/robustboot/uncert natively, either fix these paths or deprecate imputeRobust toward vimpute the way irmi was.

**Evidence:** Verified: imputeRobust(Sleep~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, sleep, method="gamRob") errors 'robGAM nicht gefunden'; uncert="wresid" errors 'Objekt d nicht gefunden'. No tinytest coverage (no test_imputeRobust*.R).

**Verifier:** All parts verified. (a) imputeRobust(Sleep~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, sleep, method="gamRob") errors "konnte Funktion 'robGAM' nicht finden": robGAM is called at R/imputeRobust.R:157 and :182 but defined nowhere in the package (grep over R/ finds no definition; vimpute's separate internal robGAM logic uses a local fit_one_robgam at R/helper_vimpute.R:2967 which is not the robGAM symbol); "gamRob"/"robGAM"/"robGam" are advertised in supportedMethods at :47, and robGAM is masked in R/zzz.R:8. (b) uncert="wresid" errors "Objekt 'd' nicht gefunden": my_distance_function defined at :223-229 is never called, and :231 references d. (c) uncert="bogus" errors "Objekt 'ymiss' nicht gefunden" — no validation of uncert; all uncert blocks are skipped and :263 uses undefined ymiss. (d) Statistical leak confirmed: missindex is computed at :73, then takeAll=TRUE (default) runs VIM::initialise at :77-79, whose default method is kNN — kNN(x, imp_var=FALSE) fills every NA (R/irmi.R:666, :682-683). Empirically, after initialise sleep$Sleep has 0 NAs, so na.omit(data[,ynam]) at :254 is a no-op and the PMM donor pool contains all 62 values including the 4 kNN-initialised (previously missing) Sleep values 3.8, 9.8, 3.1, 17.4; the model at :109 (lmrob) is likewise fit on the fully initialised data, treating initialised y as observed. (e) PMM neighbourhood hardcoded to the 5 nearest donors at :250 (order(...)[1:5]), not exposed as a parameter. No test file in inst/tinytest references imputeRobust (grep returns nothing). The default path (method="MM", uncert="pmm") does run without error, so the function is not entirely broken — but the advertised gamRob method and the wresid uncertainty option crash unconditionally whenever there is at least one missing value, exactly as claimed.

### P1.12 [classic-integration] irmi(mi>1) with default imp_var=TRUE returns one mangled data.frame instead of a list of imputations
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/irmi.R*

When mi>1, x becomes a list of mi imputed data.frames (R/irmi.R:521-574), but the imp_var block then does x <- cbind(x, imp_vardf) (:597-603). cbind.data.frame flattens the list: verified irmi(sleep, mi=2) returns a single 62x25 data.frame with duplicated column names (BodyWgt, BrainWgt, ... appear twice) instead of a list of two datasets. With imp_var=FALSE the correct list is returned, but imp_var=TRUE is the default, so documented multiple imputation via irmi is effectively broken. Fix: if (mi>1) x <- lapply(x, function(xi) cbind(xi, imp_vardf)). Secondary inconsistency in the same MI loop: meth is re-derived from the column class (:548-553, inherits(y,"numeric")/nlevels) instead of reusing the types vector, so ordered factors with >2 levels are imputed with multinom in the MI draws while the main loop used polr.

**Evidence:** Verified on build: irmi(sleep, mi=2) -> class data.frame, dim 62x25, names contain each original column twice plus *_imp columns; irmi(df, mi=2, imp_var=FALSE) -> proper list of 2.

**Verifier:** Reproduced exactly as claimed. irmi(sleep, mi=2) (imp_var=TRUE is the default, R/irmi.R:113) returns a single data.frame of dim 62x25 whose names contain every original sleep column TWICE (BodyWgt, BrainWgt, ..., Danger, then the same 10 again) plus the 5 *_imp indicator columns — duplicated(names()) is TRUE. Mechanism verified in code: the MI block (R/irmi.R:521-574) sets x <- mimp, a list of mi imputed data.frames (:570-573); the imp_var block then does x <- cbind(x, imp_vardf) (:597-603, cbind at :602), and cbind.data.frame flattens the list of data.frames into one wide data.frame. With imp_var=FALSE the correct list of 2 data.frames (62x10 each) is returned. So documented multiple imputation via irmi is unusable with default arguments — the proposed lapply-based fix is the right shape. The secondary inconsistency is also confirmed: the MI loop re-derives meth from the column class at :548-553 (inherits(y,"numeric") / factor with nlevels==2 / else "factor") instead of reusing the types vector used by the main loop (:369-381) and the noise loop (:484-496), where ordered maps to "ordered". getM dispatches "ordered" -> useOrd -> polr (:701, :926) and "factor" -> useMN -> multinom (:697, :897). Empirically traced with an ordered 3-level factor: during irmi(df, mi=2), useOrd (polr) was called once (main loop) and useMN (multinom) was called once (MI loop) for the same variable — the mis-dispatch is real; in that test the MI run then aborted with "Argument der Länge 0" in the multinom path (my test data had sparse ordered levels, so the crash itself may be data-dependent, but the polr-vs-multinom discrepancy is unambiguous from both the trace and the code). A further consequence of the class-based re-derivation, beyond the claim: integer columns get meth="factor" in the MI loop because inherits(<integer>, "numeric") is FALSE.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep); set.seed(2); r <- suppressWarnings(irmi(sleep, mi=2)); print(class(r)); print(dim(r)); print(any(duplicated(names(r)))); r2 <- suppressWarnings(irmi(sleep, mi=2, imp_var=FALSE)); print(class(r2)); print(length(r2))' — output: "data.frame", 62 25, TRUE (duplicated names); with imp_var=FALSE: "list", 2. Ordered-factor dispatch: trace("useOrd", where=asNamespace("VIM")) and trace("useMN", ...) around irmi(df, mi=2) with an ordered 3-level column shows useOrd 1 call (main loop) and useMN 1 call (MI loop).

### P1.13 [classic-integration] regressionImp() docs promise lm/glm but the code fits glmnet with fixed lambda=0.01 for >=2 predictors
*kind: design | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/regressionImp.R*

The roxygen still states '[lm()] is used for family "normal" and [glm()] for all other families' (R/regressionImp.R:8-11), but the wrapper delegates to vimpute(method="regularized") i.e. glmnet whenever robust=FALSE, keeping a hidden plain-lm fast path only for exactly one numeric predictor (:82-116). Verified numerically: regressionImp(Sleep~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, sleep) imputes c(10.4,10.6,10.4,10.6) vs lm predictions c(9.82,10.96,10.03,11.04), with glmnet warnings ('Multiple lambdas have been fit. Lambda will be set to 0.01') leaking to the user. Consequences: silent method discontinuity between 1 and 2 predictors, shrunk/biased imputations under the name 'Regression Imputation', and irreproducibility vs VIM<=6 results. family= and mod_cat= are ignored (warned, :36-40). Concrete fix that also closes a registry gap: add methods "lm" and "logreg" to vimpute backed by mlr3learners regr.lm/classif.log_reg (a dead 'logreg' branch already exists at R/vimpute.R:2063 but 'logreg' is not in supported_methods), then route regressionImp(robust=FALSE) to them.

**Evidence:** Verified run comparing regressionImp output vs stats::lm predictions on sleep; helper_vimpute.R:997 supported_methods lacks any unpenalised lm/glm; vimpute.R:2063 contains an unreachable method_var=="logreg" branch.

**Verifier:** Behavioral core fully confirmed, and it is worse than claimed. Code: R/regressionImp.R:74 sets method='regularized' (glmnet) whenever robust=FALSE; the hidden stats::lm fast path at :82-116 fires only for exactly one RHS predictor with numeric LHS and family='AUTO'. Empirically (pre-installed build, sleep data): regressionImp(Sleep~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, sleep) leaks glmnet warnings "Multiple lambdas have been fit. Lambda will be set to 0.01 (see parameter 's')... This happened in PipeOp regr.glmnet's $predict()" and its imputations differ from stats::lm predictions (lm: 9.815/10.963/10.028/11.035; typical vimpute output: 10.5/10.5/10.5/10.5, i.e. shrunk to roughly the grand mean). Worse, output is NON-DETERMINISTIC: across 5 fresh sessions/repeat calls I observed 9.80/10.96/10.10/10.96, all-10.5, and 10.5/10.6/10.5/10.6 (the reviewer's quoted c(10.4,10.6,10.4,10.6) fits this family; their exact numbers did not reproduce, but the qualitative claim does in every run). The 1-predictor call regressionImp(Sleep~BodyWgt, sleep) is exactly equal to lm() with no warnings — silent method discontinuity confirmed. family=/mod_cat are ignored with a warning (:36-40). Registry gap confirmed: helper_vimpute.R:997 supported_methods = c('ranger','regularized','xgboost','robust','gam','robgam') has no unpenalised lm/logreg, and vimpute() rejects anything else (:1019,:1028,:1046,:1073); the method_var=='logreg' branch at vimpute.R:2063 is unreachable (method_var is only ever set from the validated method list or reassigned to 'robust' at :801/:878/:1640). One nuance moderates the 'docs promise' half: the stale sentence '[lm()] is used for family "normal" and [glm()] for all other families' does exist at R/regressionImp.R:9-11, but it sits inside the first of two duplicate @param formula tags (:7 and :13) and roxygen drops it — the rendered man/regressionImp.Rd does NOT show it and its \description correctly discloses glmnet/robust delegation. So the user-facing help page does not promise lm(); the stale text plus duplicated @param is a source-level doc defect. The behavioral finding (glmnet at fixed s=0.01, hidden lm path, leaked warnings, non-reproducibility, ignored family=) stands as a genuine P1 design problem.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep, package="VIM"); idx <- is.na(sleep$Sleep); r <- regressionImp(Sleep ~ BodyWgt + BrainWgt, sleep); mod <- lm(Sleep ~ BodyWgt + BrainWgt, data=sleep[!idx,]); print(cbind(imp=r$Sleep[idx], lm=unname(predict(mod, sleep[idx,])))); r1 <- regressionImp(Sleep ~ BodyWgt, sleep); print(all.equal(r1$Sleep[idx], unname(predict(lm(Sleep~BodyWgt, sleep[!idx,]), sleep[idx,]))))' — emits the lambda=0.01 glmnet warnings, imputations differ from lm (often constant ~10.5) and vary across sessions; the 1-predictor call matches lm exactly and silently.

### P1.14 [tests] evaluation() with default vartypes="guess" silently returns error 0 for arbitrarily bad imputations
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R*

The advertised default vartypes="guess" is not implemented: evaluation() only enters its two branches on explicit "numeric"/"factor" strings, so any(vartypes=="numeric") is FALSE for the default and the function returns list(err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0) for ANY input. Reproduced live: x=iris[,1:4]; y=x; y[1,1]<-99; m marks that cell; evaluation(x,y,m) returns all zeros. This is VIM's own imputation-quality metric reporting perfect imputation for a wildly wrong one — worst-case silent failure for the 'beats mice on diagnostics' pillar. Related edge verified: nrmse() returns NA when exactly one cell is missing (var() of length-1). None of the 5 evaluation.R exports (evaluation, nrmse, pfc, msecor, msecov) is touched by any test. Fix: implement guessing (vartypes <- ifelse(sapply(x, is.numeric), "numeric", "factor")) or stop() on "guess"; then add PROPOSED TEST 1: known-truth recovery — for the reproduced setup expect_true(evaluation(x, y, m)$error > 0); nrmse(x_perfect,x_perfect,m)==0; nrmse monotone in perturbation size; pfc on a factor column with 1 of 4 masked cells wrong equals 1/4; msecov/msecor==0 for identical inputs; plus expect_true(is.na(nrmse(...))) pinned or fixed for the single-cell case.

**Evidence:** R/evaluation.R:36-48 (branches test vartypes=="numeric"/"factor" only; default "guess" handled nowhere); live run returned err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0 for y[1,1]=99 vs x[1,1]=5.1, and nrmse=NA for a single missing cell; grep over inst/tinytest/ shows zero hits for evaluation/nrmse/pfc/msecov/msecor

**Verifier:** Code reading and live reproduction both confirm the claim. R/evaluation.R:36 declares `evaluation <- function(x, y, m, vartypes = "guess")`, but the only branches are `if(any(vartypes == "numeric"))` (line 38) and `if(any(vartypes == "factor"))` (line 41); the string "guess" is handled nowhere in the file, so with the default both conditions are FALSE and the function returns list(err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0) unconditionally (lines 37, 44-47). Reproduced against the pre-installed build: x=iris[,1:4]; y=x; y[1,1]<-99; m marks that one cell; evaluation(x,y,m) returned err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0, while evaluation(x,y,m, vartypes=rep("numeric",4)) returned error=8817.21 for the identical inputs. The related edge also reproduced: nrmse(x,y,m) with exactly one missing cell returns NA (R/evaluation.R:53-55 divides by var(x[m]), and var() of a length-1 vector is NA), while nrmse with 2 cells and perfect imputation correctly returns 0. Test gap confirmed: grep for evaluation|nrmse|pfc|msecov|msecor over /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/inst/tinytest/ returns zero hits — none of the 5 exports in R/evaluation.R is touched by any test. Note the docs (@param vartypes, line 11) describe only an explicit vector like the example at line 31; "guess" is an advertised default that was never implemented, not intended behavior. The proposed fix (implement guessing via sapply(x, is.numeric) or stop() on "guess") and the known-truth tests are sound.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); x <- iris[,1:4]; y <- x; y[1,1] <- 99; m <- matrix(FALSE, nrow(x), ncol(x)); m[1,1] <- TRUE; print(evaluation(x,y,m)$error); print(evaluation(x,y,m, vartypes=rep("numeric",4))$error); print(nrmse(x,y,m))'  # prints 0, then 8817.208, then NA
