### P1.16 [api-consistency] VIM's new complete() generic masks mice::complete and breaks complete(mids) when both packages are loaded
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimmi.R*

R/vimmi.R:56 defines and exports a plain S3 generic `complete <- function(data, ...) UseMethod("complete")` with only a vimmi method. mice::complete() is a regular function, so attaching VIM after mice masks it: `library(mice); library(VIM); imp <- mice(nhanes); complete(imp)` errors with 'no applicable method for complete applied to class "mids"'. This is exactly the joint-usage pattern VIM's own MI docs push (as.mids.vimmi -> mice::pool), so the flagship interop story breaks in the most common session layout. Harmonisation: (1) register a passthrough method `complete.mids <- function(data, ...) mice::complete(data, ...)` guarded by requireNamespace("mice"), and (2) add a `complete.default` that gives an informative error naming both packages. Zero deprecation cost, one-file fix; alternatively align the generic signature with tidyr/mice conventions (`complete(data, action = 1L, ...)`) so vimmi and mids users see the same argument names.

**Evidence:** R/vimmi.R:55-58 (generic definition, @export); NAMESPACE exports complete + S3method(complete,vimmi) only. Reproduced on the installed build: environmentName(environment(complete)) == "VIM" after library(mice); library(VIM), and complete(mice::mice(nhanes, m=2)) errors 'nicht anwendbare Methode für complete ... Klasse "mids"'.

**Verifier:** Reproduced exactly as claimed. R/vimmi.R:56-58 defines and @exports a fresh S3 generic `complete <- function(data, ...) UseMethod("complete")`; NAMESPACE contains `export(complete)` and only `S3method(complete,vimmi)` — no complete.mids, no complete.default. With mice 3.19.0 installed: after `library(mice); library(VIM)`, `complete` resolves from the VIM namespace and `complete(mice::mice(nhanes, m=2))` errors with "no applicable method for 'complete' applied to an object of class 'mids'". One mechanism detail in the claim is slightly off but immaterial: mice::complete is not "a regular function" in mice 3.19.0 — mice re-exports the tidyr generic (environmentName(environment(mice::complete)) == "tidyr") and registers complete.mids on it. Because VIM defines its OWN separate generic, mice's complete.mids (registered in tidyr's methods table, not exported) is invisible to VIM's dispatch — same breakage, as reproduced. The conflict is in fact symmetric and thus worse than claimed: in the reverse attach order (VIM then mice), `complete` resolves from tidyr and `complete(vimmi_obj)` errors with "no applicable method for 'complete' applied to an object of class 'vimmi'" — so one attach order breaks mice's flagship call and the other breaks VIM's own vimmi workflow. Given VIM's docs push joint mice usage (as.mids.vimmi -> mice::pool, R/vimmi.R:23-26), this is a real P1 interop bug. A robust fix should define the method against the tidyr/mice generic (or register methods both ways), not merely add complete.mids to VIM's own generic, since the reverse order also breaks.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); Sys.setenv(LANGUAGE="en"); library(mice); library(VIM); cat(environmentName(environment(complete)), "\n"); imp <- mice(nhanes, m=2, printFlag=FALSE); complete(imp)'  ->  prints "VIM" then Error: no applicable method for 'complete' applied to an object of class "mids". Reverse order (library(VIM); library(mice)) then complete(vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", m=2), 1) -> Error: no applicable method for 'complete' applied to an object of class "vimmi".

### P1.17 [api-consistency] Two incompatible MI containers: vimpute(m>1) returns vimmi, imputeCellMCD(m>1) returns a bare list; irmi calls the same concept `mi`
*kind: design | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellEM.R*

vimpute(..., m>1) returns a vimmi object with complete()/with()/summary()/as.mids() and Rubin pooling (R/vimpute.R docs lines 107-115). imputeCellMCD(..., m=2) instead returns an unclassed list(imputed_list=, cellweights_list=, converged, iterations, m) (R/imputeCellEM.R:1025), so cellwise multiple imputations cannot be pooled with complete()/with()/mice::pool — the user must hand-roll Rubin's rules, which negates the package's MI selling point precisely for its most novel methods. Naming is also inconsistent: irmi uses `mi = 1` (R/irmi.R signature), evaluation() reuses `m` for the missingness-indicator matrix (R/evaluation.R:10), while vimpute/impPCA/imputeCellMCD use `m` = number of imputations. Harmonisation: make every m>1 path build and return a vimmi via the existing new_vimmi() constructor (cellweights lists can ride along as an extra slot); deprecate irmi's `mi` in favour of `m` (accept both for 2 releases, warn once); rename evaluation()'s `m` to `na_mask`/`M` with the old positional still working.

**Evidence:** R/imputeCellEM.R:1025 (`imputed_list = lapply(results, ...)` inside imputeCellMCD); empirical: class(imputeCellMCD(d, m=2)) == "list" with names imputed_list,cellweights_list,... while class(vimpute(d, m=2)) == "vimmi". irmi formals: mi = 1 (R/irmi.R:113). evaluation(x, y, m, vartypes): m documented as 'the indicator matrix for missing cells' (R/evaluation.R:10).

**Verifier:** Every factual component verified. (1) R/imputeCellEM.R:984-991 gives imputeCellMCD an `m = 1L, boot = FALSE` MI interface, and the m>1 branch returns an unclassed `list(imputed_list=, cellweights_list=, converged=, iterations=, m=)` at R/imputeCellEM.R:1024-1030. Empirically: `class(imputeCellMCD(sleep, m=2))` is "list" with exactly those names, and `complete()` on it errors ("no applicable method for 'complete' applied to an object of class 'list'") — so cellwise MI output cannot use complete()/with()/as.mids()/pool, and users must hand-roll Rubin's rules for VIM's most novel methods. (2) `class(vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", m=2))` is "vimmi" and complete(v, 1) returns a data.frame — two incompatible containers for the same concept confirmed. (3) Naming inconsistency confirmed: formals(irmi) has `mi` (default 1, R/irmi.R:112) and no `m`; evaluation(x, y, m, vartypes) documents `m` as "the indicator matrix for missing cells" (R/evaluation.R:10,36); vimpute/impPCA/imputeCellMCD use `m` = number of imputations (R/vimpute.R:175, R/impPCA.R:59, R/imputeCellEM.R:990). This is a design-level inconsistency, not a crash bug, but it directly undercuts the package's stated MI/USABILITY pillar and the proposed harmonisation (route all m>1 paths through new_vimmi(), which exists at R/vimmi.R:74) is feasible.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep, package="VIM"); r <- imputeCellMCD(sleep, m=2); print(class(r)); print(names(r)); v <- vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", m=2, imp_var=FALSE); print(class(v)); print(names(formals(irmi))); print(names(formals(evaluation)))'  ->  r: "list" with names imputed_list, cellweights_list, converged, iterations, m; v: "vimmi"; irmi formals include mi (no m); evaluation formals x,y,m,vartypes.

### P1.18 [api-consistency] xgboostImpute/rangerImpute delegate to vimpute() and silently ignore their documented hyperparameters (nrounds, objective, ... 'passed to xgboost/ranger')
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/xgboostImpute.R*

Since the 7.x rewrite both wrappers only warn and drop tuning arguments: xgboostImpute's roxygen still says `@param ... Arguments passed to [xgboost::xgboost()]`, `@param nrounds max number of boosting iterations`, `@param objective objective for xgboost` (R/xgboostImpute.R:12-16), but the body warns '`nrounds`, `objective`, and additional xgboost arguments are ignored; xgboostImpute() delegates to vimpute().' (R/xgboostImpute.R:43-46). rangerImpute does the same for `...` (R/rangerImpute.R:31-33; its doc at least admits 'Currently ignored'). Any pre-7.0 script that tuned num.trees/mtry/nrounds now silently runs with defaults — the opposite of the FLEXIBILITY pillar, and for xgboostImpute the shipped Rd actively contradicts behaviour. Harmonisation: vimpute already has the exact mechanism — map dots into `learner_params = list(xgboost = c(list(nrounds = nrounds, objective = objective), list(...)))` (rangerImpute analogously, as it already does for predict_median), validating names against the mlr3 learner's param_set and erroring on unknowns instead of warning-and-ignoring. Until then, fix the roxygen to state the args are inoperative.

**Evidence:** R/xgboostImpute.R:12-16 (docs promise passthrough) vs :43-46 (warning + ignore); R/rangerImpute.R:31-33 (dots ignored, only `median` forwarded via learner_params = list(ranger = list(predict_median = median))). Reproduced: rangerImpute(x~y+z, d, med=TRUE) runs with warning 'Additional ranger arguments are ignored'.

**Verifier:** Confirmed with one wording caveat: the ignoring is not literally silent — both wrappers emit a warning (which the claim's own detail acknowledges; only the title says "silently"). The substantive defect is fully reproduced. Docs: R/xgboostImpute.R:12-16 and the shipped man/xgboostImpute.Rd:32-38 (also present in the installed help of the build) still promise `nrounds`, `objective`, and `...` are "passed to xgboost::xgboost()". Behavior: R/xgboostImpute.R:43-46 warns "`nrounds`, `objective`, and additional xgboost arguments are ignored; xgboostImpute() delegates to vimpute()." and drops them (note: the warning fires only when nrounds != 100, objective non-NULL, or dots non-empty). Empirically the parameters are inoperative: with identical seeds, xgboostImpute(..., nrounds=2) and nrounds=500 return identical() results, and objective="reg:absoluteerror" is identical to the default. rangerImpute (R/rangerImpute.R:30-33) warns "Additional ranger arguments are ignored; only `median` is passed to vimpute()." and num.trees=5 gives results identical to the default; its roxygen at least honestly says `...` is "Currently ignored" (R/rangerImpute.R:9-10), so the active doc-behavior contradiction applies to xgboostImpute only — as the claim states. The regression framing is also accurate: git history shows the pre-rewrite xgboostImpute (before commit e389295 "xgboostImpute as a wrapper of vimpute") passed nrounds/objective/... directly into xgboost::xgboost(). So pre-7.0 tuning scripts now run with vimpute defaults (with a warning, not silently). The doc fix is mandatory either way; the proposed learner_params passthrough matches the mechanism rangerImpute already uses for `median` (R/rangerImpute.R:75).

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep, package="VIM"); d <- sleep[,c("Dream","BodyWgt","BrainWgt")]; set.seed(42); a <- xgboostImpute(Dream~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, data=d, nrounds=2); set.seed(42); b <- xgboostImpute(Dream~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, data=d, nrounds=500); print(identical(a,b))'  ->  TRUE (plus warning "`nrounds`, `objective`, and additional xgboost arguments are ignored..."). Same pattern: objective="reg:absoluteerror" identical to default; rangerImpute(..., num.trees=5) identical to default with warning "Additional ranger arguments are ignored; only `median` is passed to vimpute()."

### P1.19 [deps-arch] imputeRobust() broken for method='gamRob' (ghost function robGAM) and uncert='wresid' (dead closure leaks lookup to calling environment)
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeRobust.R*

R/imputeRobust.R:182 calls `robGAM(form, data = boot_dat, fraction = 0.75)$mod`, but no function robGAM is defined anywhere in the package (grep over R/ finds only strings/messages; the vimpute learner LearnerRegrRobGAM in helper_vimpute.R:2770 is unrelated and not callable this way). Since boot=TRUE is the default, imputeRobust(..., method='gamRob'|'robGAM'|'robGam') always errors 'could not find function robGAM' -- and DESCRIPTION (lines 73-75) specifically advertises robust GAM-based imputation (Templ 2024, Stat Comput) as a package feature; only the vimpute(method='robgam') route works. Second break: in the uncert='wresid' branch (R/imputeRobust.R:223-231) the pdist call is wrapped in a never-invoked closure `my_distance_function`, after which `d <- 1 - d@dist/max(d@dist)` reads an undefined `d`; R's scoping then finds any `d` in the caller/global environment (reproduced: with a data.frame named d in globalenv the error becomes 'no applicable method for @ applied to data.frame'; otherwise 'object d not found'). The same dead-closure pattern exists in imputeRobustChain.R:399-407. Both symbols (`robGAM`, `r`, `p`) are masked via R/zzz.R globalVariables. Fix: implement/restore robGAM (or route gamRob to the working helper_vimpute robust-GAM irw loop), unwrap the pdist calls (the correct pattern exists 20 lines later at imputeRobust.R:249-251: check_suggested('pdist') + direct call), and add tinytest coverage for imputeRobust (currently none).

**Evidence:** Reproduced on installed build: imputeRobust(a~b+c, data=d, method='gamRob') -> 'konnte Funktion robGAM nicht finden'; uncert='wresid' -> 'no applicable method for @ applied to an object of class data.frame'. Code: R/imputeRobust.R:182, 223-231; correct guarded pattern at 249-251.

**Verifier:** Both defects reproduced on the installed build. (1) robGAM is defined nowhere in the package: grep over R/ finds only the calls at R/imputeRobust.R:157 (tmp <- robGAM(form, data=data, fraction=alpha)) and :182, the globalVariables mask at R/zzz.R:8, and unrelated strings/warnings in vimpute.R/helper_vimpute.R. imputeRobust(a~b+c, data=d, method='gamRob') errors 'could not find function "robGAM"' — and (stronger than claimed) it errors for boot=FALSE too, because the first robGAM call at :157 sits outside the boot branch. helper_vimpute.R:2770 defines LearnerRegrRobGAM, an R6 mlr3 learner (id 'regr.robgam_imp') not callable as robGAM(form, ...) — unrelated, as claimed. (2) uncert='wresid': R/imputeRobust.R:223-229 wraps the pdist call in the never-invoked closure my_distance_function, then :231 reads undefined d. ### P1.20 [deps-arch] car accounts for 55 of VIM's 105 recursive hard dependencies but is used only for one optional Box-Cox call in prepare()
*kind: refactor | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/prepare.R*

Measured against the installed library: VIM has 26 direct hard deps (24 Imports + colorspace/grid in Depends) and 105 recursive Depends/Imports/LinkingTo (excluding base). Removing only `car` from the set drops the recursive tree by 55 packages (car pulls carData, abind, Formula, mgcv, pbkrtest, quantreg, lme4, nlme, scales, Rdpack, minqa, nloptr, RcppEigen, ...). The entire usage is car::powerTransform + car::bcPower in the internal boxcoxVIM() (R/prepare.R:128, 130, 138, 142), reached only via prepare(transformation='boxcox') -- a non-default option of a helper documented as 'used by the VIM GUI' (R/prepare.R:11-12). Two zero-risk fixes: (a) demote car to Suggests and guard boxcoxVIM with requireNamespace('car') + informative error (no behaviour change for the >99% of calls that never use boxcox); or (b) drop car entirely by estimating lambda with a ~15-line profile-log-likelihood optimize() (note car's matrix branch does joint multivariate lambda estimation, so exact replication of the powers=NULL matrix case needs care -- the guard route avoids that). Either way VIM's recursive footprint roughly halves (105 -> ~50), which directly serves the usability/install-cost story against mice (mice's recursive tree is far smaller).

**Evidence:** Marginal-dependency measurement on installed lib: car subtree=69, marginal=55 of TOTAL 105 recursive deps; only usages R/prepare.R:128,138 (powerTransform) and :130,142 (bcPower); NAMESPACE:89-90 importFrom(car,...).

**Verifier:** Independently recomputed on the installed library (tools::package_dependencies over installed.packages(), which=Depends/Imports/LinkingTo, recursive, excluding base-priority packages) and every number matches exactly: 26 direct hard deps (24 Imports incl. car + colorspace/grid in Depends, per DESCRIPTION:15-41); 105 total recursive hard deps; dropping car alone -> 50, i.e. marginal contribution of car = 55 packages (incl. carData, abind, Formula, mgcv, pbkrtest, quantreg, lme4, nlme, scales, Rdpack, minqa, nloptr, plus ggplot2/dplyr/tidyr/stringi/survival/forecast/...); car's own subtree = 69, matching the claim's evidence line. For scale: the next-largest marginal among VIM's direct deps is 2 (mlr3tuning, xgboost); laeken/vcd/sp are 1 each — car is a 27x outlier. Usage verified as claimed: the only calls are inside the internal boxcoxVIM() in R/prepare.R (powerTransform at :128 and :138, bcPower at :130 and :142, imported unqualified via NAMESPACE:89-90 / roxygen tags R/VIM-package.R:12-13); boxcoxVIM is reached only via prepare(transformation='boxcox'), a non-default option (default 'none') of a function documented as 'used by the VIM GUI' (R/prepare.R:10-12), and grep finds no other internal caller of prepare()/boxcoxVIM in R/. The mice comparison also holds: mice's recursive hard-dep tree measured at 62 packages (incl. mice itself) vs VIM's 106 — and VIM without car (~51) would undercut mice. Two trivial snapshot details, not refutations: (a) RcppEigen, listed among car's example pulls, is not in the current marginal set (installed lme4 no longer depends on it); (b) exact counts drift with CRAN snapshots, but the measured state matches the claim to the digit. The proposed fixes (demote car to Suggests with a requireNamespace guard in boxcoxVIM, or replace with a profile-likelihood optimize()) are sound; the claim itself already flags the multivariate-lambda subtlety of the powers=NULL matrix branch (car::powerTransform on a matrix estimates lambda jointly), which the Suggests route sidesteps.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/deps_car.R -> 'Direct hard deps: 26', 'TOTAL recursive hard deps: 105', 'Without car: 50 -> marginal contribution of car: 55', 'car's own subtree size: 69', marginal(mlr3tuning)=2, marginal(xgboost)=2. grep -rn 'powerTransform\|bcPower' R/ -> only R/prepare.R (:128,:130,:138,:142) + roxygen import tags in R/VIM-package.R:12-13.

### P1.21 [deps-arch] No minimum version pins on the mlr3 stack: importFrom(mlr3tuning, TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit) breaks library(VIM) at load time against pre-1.0 mlr3tuning
*kind: design | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: medium | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/DESCRIPTION*

DESCRIPTION (lines 35-41) lists mlr3, mlr3pipelines, R6, paradox, mlr3tuning, mlr3learners, future all unversioned. NAMESPACE:132 does importFrom(mlr3tuning, TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit); the Batch-prefixed classes only exist since the bbotk/mlr3tuning 1.0.0 'batch' refactor (VERIFY exact release: mlr3tuning 1.0.0, mid-2024). Because importFrom is resolved when the namespace loads, a user with an older-but-CRAN-valid mlr3tuning (e.g. a frozen Posit Package Manager snapshot for R 4.2/4.3, which satisfies R >= 4.1.0) gets a hard failure of library(VIM) itself -- not just of vimpute(). Same class used at R/vimpute.R:1253 and 1345. Recommend pinning at least: mlr3tuning (>= 1.0.0), and sane floors for mlr3 (as_task_regr/as_task_classif era) and paradox (ps()/p_dbl syntax, >= 0.7.1). Conversely the one existing pin is stale to the point of being decorative: data.table (>= 1.9.4) dates from 2014 (DESCRIPTION:34, also missing a space before the parenthesis); any R >= 4.1.0 system has data.table far newer. Cheap insurance against exactly the class-renaming churn the mlr3 ecosystem has a track record of.

**Evidence:** DESCRIPTION:34-41 (only data.table pinned, at 1.9.4); NAMESPACE:132 importFrom(mlr3tuning,TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit); R/vimpute.R:1253,1345 uses; installed build resolves against mlr3tuning 1.5.1. VERIFY: Batch classes introduced in mlr3tuning 1.0.0 (2024).

**Verifier:** Every element of the claim checks out, and the load failure was reproduced end-to-end. (1) /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/DESCRIPTION lines 34-41: data.table(>= 1.9.4) is the only versioned dependency (also missing the space before the parenthesis, which is cosmetic — R's parser resolves name/op/version correctly, verified via tools:::.split_op_version); mlr3, mlr3pipelines, R6, paradox, mlr3tuning, mlr3learners, future are all unversioned; Depends R (>= 4.1.0) at line 16. data.table 1.9.4 is from 2014-10-02 (CRAN archive), so that pin is indeed decorative. (2) /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/NAMESPACE:132 has importFrom(mlr3tuning,TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit) (source: @importFrom at R/VIM-package.R:26; class used at R/vimpute.R:1253 and 1345). (3) TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit was introduced in mlr3tuning 1.0.0 (CRAN 2024-06-29) as a documented BREAKING CHANGE rename of TuningInstanceSingleCrit (mlr3tuning NEWS.md, '# mlr3tuning 1.0.0' section); the last pre-1.0 release 0.20.0 (CRAN 2024-03-05) exports only TuningInstanceSingleCrit/MultiCrit — grep of its NAMESPACE from the CRAN archive tarball finds zero occurrences of the Batch name. (4) Reproduction: installed mlr3tuning 0.20.0 into a scratch library; its own namespace loads cleanly against the current mlr3 1.5.0/bbotk 1.9.0/paradox 1.0.1 stack (no confounding failure), and 0.20.0 satisfies VIM's unversioned Imports requirement; with it first on .libPaths(), library(VIM) hard-fails: "Laden von Paket oder Namensraum für 'VIM': fehlgeschlagen — Objekt 'TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit' ist nicht von 'namespace:mlr3tuning' exportiert". This kills the ENTIRE package at namespace-load time — kNN, hotdeck, aggr and all visualization functions included — not just vimpute(). Baseline control: VIM 7.1.0 loads fine with mlr3tuning 1.5.1. Because DESCRIPTION carries no floor, dependency solvers (install.packages, renv restore/upgrade=FALSE, pak, frozen PPM repos, stale site libraries with a freshly updated VIM) have no information that mlr3tuning >= 1.0.0 is required, and the user gets a cryptic 'object not exported' error instead of the clear 'namespace ... is being loaded, but >= 1.0.0 is required' message a version pin would produce. Recommended fix (as the claim says): pin mlr3tuning (>= 1.0.0) at minimum; floors for mlr3/paradox are cheap insurance given the ecosystem's rename track record (VIM's paradox imports ps/p_dbl/p_int/p_fct and mlr3 imports as_task_regr/as_task_classif are older APIs, so mlr3tuning is the binding constraint today).

**Repro:** cd $SCRATCH && curl -sO https://cran.r-project.org/src/contrib/Archive/mlr3tuning/mlr3tuning_0.20.0.tar.gz && mkdir -p oldlib && R CMD INSTALL --no-docs --library=oldlib mlr3tuning_0.20.0.tar.gz && Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("'$SCRATCH'/oldlib", "'$SCRATCH'/Rlib", .libPaths())); loadNamespace("mlr3tuning"); library(VIM)'  # mlr3tuning 0.20.0 loads OK on its own; library(VIM) then fails with: object 'TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit' is not exported by 'namespace:mlr3tuning' (where SCRATCH=/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad)

### P1.25 [mice] Ordinal imputation (proportional-odds) and preservation of ordered factors
*kind: method-gap (vs mice.impute.polr) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Defect + gap: vimpute coerces ordered factors to plain factors (vimpute.R:816-819, again at 1624-1631) and returns them UNORDERED — verified functionally (is.ordered = FALSE after imputation). Silent type corruption of user data; no ordinal-aware model.

PROPOSAL: Minimum fix: restore the ordered class (and level order) on return. Full fix: register LearnerClassifPolr wrapping MASS::polr exactly like the existing LearnerClassifGlmRob pattern (helper_vimpute.R:138-258) and route ordered targets to it by default.

REFERENCE: vimpute.R:816-819, helper_vimpute.R:138-258

**Verifier:** The vimpute defect is real and functionally verified: an ordered factor with NAs goes in, a plain factor comes out (is.ordered = FALSE); coercion via factor(as.character(x)) at vimpute.R:816-820 and again at 1624-1632. One correction to the claim: the level ORDER is preserved on return (levels still low<mid<high via the factor_levels restore) — only the ordered class is dropped, so the 'minimum fix' is smaller than stated. Important nuance on 'no ordinal-aware model': deprecated irmi() DOES impute ordered responses with MASS::polr (useOrd, R/irmi.R:911-932) and preserves orderedness (functionally verified is.ordered=TRUE after irmi), and kNN handles ordinal via gowerD + ordFun=medianSamp (kNN.R:122). But irmi warns 'IRMI is deprecated. Please use vimpute()' (irmi.R:123), so the strategic successor genuinely lacks ordinal support and silently degrades the type — the gap stands for vimpute.

**Repro:** Rscript: d$o <- factor(..., ordered=TRUE); d$o[1:15] <- NA; res <- vimpute(d, method="ranger", sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE); is.ordered(res$o)  # FALSE; irmi(d3) on ordered -> is.ordered TRUE

### P1.27 [competitors] Per-variable imputation-quality metric returned by default (OOB / holdout error without ground truth)
*kind: method-gap (vs missForest (OOBerror: NRMSE for numeric, PFC for factors; variablewise=TRUE gives per-variable vector — verified locally, v1.6.1 docs); miceRanger (plotModelError, OOB per iteration)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: No OOB/holdout metric anywhere in R/ (grep 'oob' returns nothing); resampling metrics are computed during tuning then discarded unless tune=TRUE (R/vimpute.R:1276-1285); evaluation()/nrmse() require the true values (R/evaluation.R:36-55), which users never have

PROPOSAL: Return per-variable model quality as attr(result, 'model_error') and show it in print/summary.vimmi: ranger OOB R2/MSE comes free from the fitted learner; use a small holdout or mlr3 resample for the other learners. Near-zero cost, directly answers the practitioner's 'can I trust this imputation?' question.

REFERENCE: missForest.Rd Value section (verified locally); Stekhoven & Buehlmann (2012) Bioinformatics 28(1):112-118, doi:10.1093/bioinformatics/btr597 (from package docs)

**Verifier:** Case-insensitive grep for 'oob' over R/ returns nothing. Per-variable CV metrics are computed only inside the tuning branch (default_metric/tuned_metric via mlr3 resample at R/vimpute.R:1272-1285 and :1361-1369) and are then collapsed to a boolean tuned_better in tuning_log (:1425-1428) — the metric values are never returned, and nothing is computed at all when tune=FALSE (the default). evaluation()/nrmse()/pfc() all require the true data as input (R/evaluation.R:36-67). print.vimmi/summary.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:193-241) show missing counts and between-imputation spread but no model-quality metric. ranger's free OOB error is simply discarded with the fitted learner.

### P1.28 [competitors] Overimputation calibration diagnostic (impute observed cells, compare to truth)
*kind: method-gap (vs Amelia::overimpute(output, var, draws=20) — plots observed vs imputed mean with CIs, colored by row missingness (verified locally, 1.8.3); rMIDAS monitors overimputation error during autoencoder training) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Nothing equivalent; VIM's quality tools all require external truth (R/evaluation.R:36-55)

PROPOSAL: Add overimpute(data, ...) for vimpute: for one variable, sequentially treat each observed cell as missing, impute with m draws, plot observed vs imputed mean ± 90% interval. Model-agnostic (works for all learners), reuses vimmi machinery, and is the gold-standard answer to 'is my imputation model well calibrated?'.

REFERENCE: args(Amelia::overimpute) verified locally; Honaker, King & Blackwell, Amelia II, JSS 45(7) 2011 (from package docs)

**Verifier:** grep -rni 'overimput' over R/, man/, vignettes/, NEWS.md returns nothing; no exported function provides an Amelia::overimpute-style diagnostic. The only quality tools (R/evaluation.R:36-67) compare against externally supplied truth. Nothing in the installed build's export list matches either (checked getNamespaceExports('VIM')).

### P1.29 [competitors] Model persistence + predict on new/unseen data (train/predict separation)
*kind: method-gap (vs missRanger 2.6+ predict.missRanger(object, newdata, iter) with keep_forests=TRUE (verified locally); mixgb save.models + impute_new(); miceRanger impute(newdata, miceObj); NADIA train/predict PipeOps) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

PROPOSAL: Add vimpute(..., keep_models = TRUE) returning class 'vimpute' with a predict(newdata, iter = 1) method that reuses the stored mlr3 learners. Required for production scoring and for leakage-free imputation inside cross-validation — the use case NADIA exists to serve.

**Verifier:** vimpute() returns only the imputed data, a list(data, pred_history/tuning_log), or a vimmi object (R/vimpute.R:111-115; return paths at :477-488 and build_vimpute_result at R/helper_vimpute.R:1825-1847). No keep_models-style argument exists (formals(vimpute) verified on the installed build).

### P1.30 [competitors] Tuning ergonomics: tune=TRUE silently never runs with sequential=FALSE; budget hidden; re-tunes per imputation
*kind: method-gap (vs mlim (its entire pitch is a loud, automatic per-variable tuning loop); mixgb (mixgb_cv() pre-tunes nrounds explicitly)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: sequential=FALSE forces nseq <- 1 (R/vimpute.R:326-329) while tuning fires only when i == round(nseq/2), i.e. i == 0, which never happens (R/vimpute.R:1202) — empirically confirmed this audit (tuning_log shows tuned_better=FALSE, no search executed, vs real tuning entries at nseq=4); n_evals budgets are hardcoded (R/helper_vimpute.R:2365-2410); with m>1 tuning re-runs inside every imputation

PROPOSAL: Fire tuning at i == max(1, round(nseq/2)); warn (or tune immediately) when tune=TRUE and sequential=FALSE; expose tune_budget/tune_time arguments; cache tuned params across the m loop (hyperparameter_cache already exists, R/vimpute.R:499). The silent no-op is a bug-level UX failure against the tuning pillar of the strategic claim.

REFERENCE: R/vimpute.R:326-329 + R/vimpute.R:1202; reproduced with VIM build from working tree (scratchpad Rlib)

**Verifier:** All three sub-claims verified. (1) Silent no-op: sequential=FALSE forces nseq <- 1 (R/vimpute.R:326-329) and the tuning gate is i == round(nseq/2) (R/vimpute.R:1202); round(0.5) is 0 in R, i starts at 1, so tuning never fires and no warning is emitted — the docs even promise 'Tuning is performed halfway through nseq iterations' (R/vimpute.R:86). Empirically reproduced on the installed build (n=250, 2 NA variables, method='ranger'): tune=TRUE+sequential=FALSE finished in 0.4s with tuning_log all tuned_better=FALSE and no search executed; identical call with sequential=TRUE, nseq=4 took 10.4s and produced tuned_better=TRUE. (2) Hidden budget: n_evals hardcoded per learner/data size at R/helper_vimpute.R:2365, :2376, :2387, :2396, :2401, :2409; no tune_budget/tune_time in formals(vimpute). (3) Re-tuning per imputation: the m-loop recurses vimpute(m=1, tune=tune) (R/vimpute.R:419-445) and hyperparameter_cache is a fresh per-call local (:499), so each of the m runs re-tunes independently. Caveat for the related win #4 ('real per-variable tuning'): it is real, but only when sequential=TRUE and nseq>=2 — the win needs this bug fixed before being marketable.

**Repro:** d <- data.frame(a=rnorm(250), b=rnorm(250), c=rnorm(250)); d$y <- d$a+0.5*d$b+rnorm(250,0,0.3); d$y[sample(250,40)] <- NA; d$a[sample(250,20)] <- NA; system.time(r <- vimpute(d, method='ranger', tune=TRUE, sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE)) # 0.4s, r$tuning_log all tuned_better=FALSE; vs sequential=TRUE, nseq=4 -> 10.4s, tuned_better=TRUE appears

### P1.31 [competitors] Parallelize over m imputations with reproducible seeding
*kind: method-gap (vs miceRanger (parallel = TRUE over datasets via foreach/doParallel); Amelia (parallel = 'multicore'/'snow', ncpus — verified locally, 1.8.3)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: m-loop is strictly sequential: for (mi in seq_len(m)) at R/vimpute.R:419; future is already a dependency but used only to size learner threads (R/vimpute.R:179-180, :900); no seed argument in the signature (R/vimpute.R:154-176)

PROPOSAL: Wrap the m loop in future.apply::future_lapply(..., future.seed = TRUE) and add a seed argument. The m x nseq x p learner fits are embarrassingly parallel; with m=5-20 this is a 3-8x usability win for the MI workflow VIM is betting on.

REFERENCE: R/vimpute.R:419 (loop), :179 (future already imported); VERIFY: miceRanger parallel mechanics from memory

**Verifier:** The m-loop is strictly sequential: for (mi in seq_len(m)) at R/vimpute.R:419, recursing into full single imputations one at a time. future is a dependency but is used only to save/restore the plan (R/vimpute.R:179-180), to size learner threads via future::availableCores() (:900, feeding nthread at :917), and to force plan('sequential') after tuning (:1411). No parallel backend for the m runs, and no seed argument anywhere in the signature (R/vimpute.R:154-176; confirmed via formals(vimpute) on the installed build: data, considered_variables, method, pmm, pmm_k, pmm_k_method, learner_params, formula, makeNA, donorcond, sequential, nseq, eps, imp_var, pred_history, tune, verbose, boot, robustboot, uncert, m).

### P1.32 [methodology-docs] Deterministic PMM silently yields m identical imputations (degenerate MI, Rubin's rules invalid)
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

The m>1 guard (R/vimpute.R:339-343) exempts has_any_pmm from the 'all imputations will be identical' warning, but PMM with its documented defaults (pmm_k=1; or k>1 with "mean"/"median") is fully deterministic given the fit. With a deterministic learner (robust/regularized/gam) and boot=FALSE, all m completed datasets are byte-identical and NO warning fires; between-imputation variance is 0, so mice::pool SEs/CIs are severely understated. Worse, pmm=TRUE silently cancels uncert (R/vimpute.R:333-337: 'pmm takes precedence; uncert ignored'), so a user requesting m=5, pmm=TRUE, uncert="resid" gets degenerate MI. Fix: only treat PMM as a variability source when pmm_k_method=="random" (or boot=TRUE), and document in vimpute.Rd @param m / vignette 'Parameter m' which settings produce proper (stochastic) imputations.

**Evidence:** Reproduced on installed build: vimpute(sleep, method="robust", m=3, pmm=TRUE, sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE) -> identical(complete(mi,1), complete(mi,2)) == TRUE, identical(d1,d3) == TRUE; only lmrob fit warnings emitted, no MI-degeneracy warning. Warning condition at R/vimpute.R:340: `if (m > 1L && !boot && uncert == "none" && !has_any_pmm)`.

**Verifier:** Reproduced end-to-end on the installed build. Code: R/vimpute.R:340 guard `if (m > 1L && !boot && uncert == "none" && !has_any_pmm)` exempts any pmm=TRUE from the 'all imputations will be identical' warning, and R/vimpute.R:334-337 silently cancels a user-requested uncert when pmm=TRUE ('pmm takes precedence; uncert ignored'). PMM defaults are deterministic: pmm_k defaults to 1 (R/helper_vimpute.R:666-670), pmm_k_method defaults to "mean" (R/vimpute.R:160), and pmm_donor_selection (R/helper_vimpute.R:1640-1658) picks order(abs(score_obs - s))[seq_len(k)] then aggregates by mean/median — only "random" is stochastic. Empirically: vimpute(sleep, method="robust", m=3, pmm=TRUE, sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE) returns a vimmi whose 3 completed datasets are identical() == TRUE pairwise (even lmrob's internal subsampling does not break byte-identity), the imp$Sleep matrix has zero row-wise variance, and NO degeneracy warning fires (only lmrob fit warnings). Adding uncert="resid" fires the precedence warning, cancels uncert, and MI stays degenerate. Downstream damage confirmed: with(mi, lm(Sleep~Dream+Span)) -> mice::pool gives between-imputation variance b = 0 and riv = 0 for all coefficients, i.e. pooled SEs collapse to single-imputation SEs. Controls match the claim: without pmm the warning at vimpute.R:341 fires; pmm_k=5 + pmm_k_method="random" produces non-identical imputations. Docs (@param m at R/vimpute.R:106-110, @param pmm/pmm_k/pmm_k_method at 22-47, vignette 'Parameter m') nowhere state that default PMM is deterministic and yields degenerate MI. The proposed fix direction (treat PMM as a variability source only when pmm_k_method=="random" or boot=TRUE) is consistent with the code.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(1); mi <- vimpute(sleep, method="robust", m=3, pmm=TRUE, sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE, verbose=FALSE); print(identical(complete(mi,1), complete(mi,2))); print(identical(complete(mi,1), complete(mi,3))); print(mi$imp$Sleep); p <- mice::pool(with(mi, lm(Sleep ~ Dream + Span))); print(p$pooled$b); print(p$pooled$riv)'  # -> TRUE, TRUE, identical columns m1..m3, b = 0 0 0, riv = 0 0 0; no MI-degeneracy warning emitted (verified via withCallingHandlers; only lmrob fit warnings). Control: same call without pmm=TRUE fires 'all imputations will be identical'; pmm_k=5, pmm_k_method="random" gives identical()==FALSE.

*kind: doc-gap | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

No guidance on when MI vs single imputation, how to choose m (only m=5 shown; no rule-of-thumb a la White et al. 2011 / van Buuren FIMD), no Rubin's-rules mention, no congeniality/compatibility caveat between imputation and analysis model, and no warning that ML learners without boot/uncert understate uncertainty. Tuning (lines 435-457) is likewise a one-line eval=FALSE chunk with no tuning_log output shown. Per-variable methods ARE demonstrated live — good — but the two headline capabilities vs mice (tuning, MI) exist only as untested toy snippets. vimmi.Rd/with.vimmi.Rd (R/vimmi.R:158-176) also promise pooling without stating validity conditions.

**Evidence:** vimpute.Rmd:417-430 (eval=FALSE, complete() only; text mentions as.mids only 'for downstream pooling workflows'); 438-443 (tune eval=FALSE); verified pooling works: pooled lm(Sleep~Dream+Span) identical via with.vimmi->pool and as.mids->with->pool (estimates 8.131/1.842/-0.064).

**Verifier:** Verified by inspection of the working tree plus a positive control run. vignettes/vimpute.Rmd 'Parameter m' section: chunk at lines 417-430 is eval=FALSE and shows only complete(mi, 1/"all"/"long"); prose at line 432 mentions as.mids.vimmi() only 'for downstream pooling workflows' with no demonstration. grep across all 8 vignettes finds zero occurrences of mice::pool, Rubin, or a with() pooling demo — vimpute.Rmd line 432 is the only mention of 'pooling' in the entire vignettes/ directory. No guidance exists on choosing m (only m=5 shown), on Rubin's rules, on congeniality/compatibility, or on which vimpute settings give proper stochastic imputations (directly relevant given the confirmed claim above). Tuning: the 'Parameter tune' chunk at lines 438-443 is an eval=FALSE one-liner vimpute(data=data, tune=TRUE); tuning_log is mentioned in prose (line 457) but never shown. Overall 14 of 32 chunks are eval=FALSE, while per-variable method choice IS demonstrated live (live chunk at line 137), matching the claim's characterization. R/vimmi.R:158-177: with.vimmi docs promise 'results can be pooled using mice::pool() or mitools::MIcombine()' with a dontrun example and no validity conditions. Positive control confirms this is a doc-gap, not a broken feature: with.vimmi -> mice::pool works (b > 0 with boot=TRUE, uncert="normalerror") and as.mids.vimmi -> with -> mice::pool yields matching pooled estimates (all.equal TRUE). Note the claim's specific estimates (8.131/1.842/-0.064) are seed-dependent and were not re-obtained (different seed here gave 6.876/2.297/-0.052), but the substantive point — both pooling paths work and agree — was reproduced.

### P1.34 [usability] Length-1 named method list silently reinterpreted as global method; variable name (even misspelled) discarded
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/helper_vimpute.R*

helper_vimpute.R branches on is.list(method) && length(method)==1L && is.character(method[[1]]) BEFORE the named-list branch, so list(Dream="gam") becomes global method "gam" for ALL variables and the name is never checked. Verified live: vimpute(sleep, method=list(Dream="gam"), sequential=FALSE, verbose=TRUE) prints '--- GAM params for variable NonD/Dream/Sleep/Span/Gest ---' (gam used for every variable); vimpute(sleep, method=list(Sleeep="ranger"), sequential=FALSE) with a misspelled variable succeeds silently. With 2+ entries the named-list branch correctly errors on unknown names (helper_vimpute.R:1036-1043), so behavior is inconsistent by list length. Because the m=1 result carries no record of methods used, the user cannot detect that their per-variable choice was globalized. Fix: check names(method) first; treat any named list per-variable.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1025-1032 (length-1 list branch ignores names) vs :1036-1043 (named branch validates). Commands: vimpute(sleep, method=list(Sleeep="ranger"), sequential=FALSE) -> [OK], no warning; vimpute(sleep, method=list(Dream="gam"), sequential=FALSE, verbose=TRUE) -> 'GAM params for variable NonD', 'GAM params for variable Sleep', etc.

**Verifier:** Code reading and live repro both confirm every part of the claim. /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/helper_vimpute.R:1025-1032 branches on is.list(method) && length(method)==1L && is.character(method[[1]]) BEFORE the named-list branch at :1035-1065, and rebuilds method as setNames(as.list(rep(single_method, length(variables_NA))), variables_NA) — the original list's name is never read or validated. Reproduced on the pre-installed build: (1) vimpute(sleep, method=list(Sleeep="ranger"), sequential=FALSE) succeeds silently despite the misspelled variable name; (2) the 2-entry control vimpute(sleep, method=list(Sleeep="ranger", Dream="ranger"), sequential=FALSE) correctly errors with "Unknown variable name(s) in 'method': Sleeep" (validation at helper_vimpute.R:1037-1043), proving the length-dependent inconsistency; (3) vimpute(sleep, method=list(Dream="gam"), sequential=FALSE, verbose=TRUE) prints "--- GAM params for variable X ---" for ALL five NA variables (NonD, Dream, Sleep, Span, Gest), i.e. the per-variable choice was globalized; (4) the 2-entry control list(Dream="gam", Sleep="ranger") prints GAM params only for Dream, confirming correct per-variable behavior when length > 1. The m=1 return value is a plain data.table with no record of methods used, so the user indeed cannot detect the globalization. The suggested fix (check names(method) first, treat any named list per-variable) is sound.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("<scratchpad>/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); vimpute(sleep, method=list(Sleeep="ranger"), sequential=FALSE)' -> succeeds silently; same with method=list(Sleeep="ranger", Dream="ranger") -> Error "Unknown variable name(s) in 'method': Sleeep"; vimpute(sleep, method=list(Dream="gam"), sequential=FALSE, verbose=TRUE) -> "--- GAAM params for variable ---" lines for NonD, Dream, Sleep, Span, Gest (all 5). Full script: <scratchpad>/claim1_method_list.R, output claim1_out.txt.

### P1.35 [usability] Documented flagship MI example emits ~45 raw internal warnings (mlr3 PipeOp/robustbase internals, German base-R messages, leaked helper columns)
*kind: usability | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/man/vimpute.Rd*

Running the ?vimpute example verbatim — vimpute(data=sleep, method="robust", m=5, boot=TRUE, robustboot="stratified", uncert="normalerror") — produced ~45 warnings in 22.5s: 'S-estimated scale == 0: Probably exact fit' / 'M-step did NOT converge' each suffixed 'This happened in PipeOp regr.lm_rob's $train()', a German base recycling warning 'Länge des längeren Objektes ist kein Vielfaches der Länge des kürzeren Objektes' (a raw recycling warning suggests an unguarded vectorized assignment somewhere in the boot/uncert path), leaked internal helper column names ('Dropping constant or single-level predictors for Sleep: Dream_zero_prob'), and 'reg_data empty after NA handling for NonD - skipping regressor.'. A new user cannot tell signal from noise and concludes the run failed; mice on the same data is silent and stores 4 rows in mids$loggedEvents. Even success paths leak: method="robust" single imputation (F1/F3) emits 2-6 robustbase warnings. Recommended: catch/deduplicate learner warnings, rephrase in user vocabulary, and persist a loggedEvents-style log in the result.

**Evidence:** man/vimpute.Rd:192-194 example run verbatim -> 45 [WARNING] lines captured (exp6 EX7, 22.5s). Baseline: mice::mice(VIM::sleep, m=5) -> 1.65s, 4 loggedEvents, no console spam. Recycling warning text: 'Länge des längeren Objektes ist kein Vielfaches der Länge des kürzeren Objektes'.

**Verifier:** Reproduced and the true scale is worse than claimed. The example exists verbatim at /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/man/vimpute.Rd:192-194 (inside \dontrun). Running it with a withCallingHandlers collector on the pre-installed build raised 1569 warning conditions in 21.7 s (the reviewer's "~45" is R's console-truncated view; R stops listing at 50). Every claimed warning type is present: 423x "S-estimated scale == 0: Probably exact fit" and 427x "initial estim. 'init' not converged" and 221x "prediction from a rank-deficient fit may be misleading", all suffixed "This happened in PipeOp regr.lm_rob's $train()/$predict()"; 8x "M-step did NOT converge"; 152x the German base recycling warning "Länge des längeren Objektes ist kein Vielfaches der Länge des kürzeren Objektes" (locale-dependent text, substance locale-independent); ~239x leaked internal helper column "Dream_zero_prob" inside "Dropping constant or single-level predictors" messages; 2x "reg_data empty after NA handling for NonD/Dream - skipping regressor.". The returned vimmi object has no log/loggedEvents element, confirming nothing is persisted. mice baseline on the same machine: mice::mice(VIM::sleep, m=5) ran in 0.12 s with 5 loggedEvents rows and one warning condition — direction of the comparison confirmed (claimed 1.65 s / 4 rows; minor machine/seed variation). One refinement to the claim's speculation about the recycling warning: a sys.calls() trace shows it originates in robustbase's summary.lmrob (est/se on a degenerate fit), reached via VIM's own extract_model_info() at /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/helper_vimpute.R:1527 (called from R/vimpute.R:1941/1966/1976 in the uncert path), whose tryCatch catches errors only, not warnings — so it is not a VIM vectorized assignment, but it IS an unguarded VIM call site leaking a raw base warning 152 times. This detail does not weaken the usability finding; the recommended remediation (catch/deduplicate learner warnings, user-vocabulary phrasing, loggedEvents-style log on the result) is well targeted.

**Repro:** Script <scratchpad>/claim2_warnings.R: runs vimpute(data=sleep, method="robust", m=5, boot=TRUE, robustboot="stratified", uncert="normalerror") verbatim under withCallingHandlers -> 1569 warnings, 21.7 s, frequency table in claim2_out.txt. Trace script claim2_trace.R shows recycling-warning stack: vimpute -> extract_model_info -> summary.lmrob -> .signalSimpleWarning(..., quote(est/se)); mice baseline 0.12 s, 5 loggedEvents.

### P1.36 [framework-design] tune = TRUE is a silent no-op with sequential = FALSE and whenever convergence breaks before mid-sequence
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Tuning fires only when `i == round(nseq / 2)` (vimpute.R:1202). With sequential = FALSE, nseq is forced to 1 (vimpute.R:326-329), and round(1/2) == 0 in R, so the condition is never true: the user asks for tuning, pays nothing, gets nothing, and receives no warning — only a tuning_log whose entries all say tuned_better = FALSE, indistinguishable from 'tuning ran and defaults won'. Empirically confirmed on the installed build: vimpute(sleep, method='ranger', sequential=FALSE, tune=TRUE) returns tuning_log with 5 entries, none tuned. Same silent skip occurs with default nseq=10 whenever check_convergence breaks the loop before iteration 5 (possible from i=3 on, helper_vimpute.R:2235-2238) — i.e. precisely on easy, fast-converging data. Fix contract: decouple tuning from the iteration index — tune at a fixed, guaranteed point (e.g. iteration min(2, nseq) or immediately before the final sweep), and if tuning was requested but never executed, emit a warning naming the variables affected. Add a regression tinytest: vimpute(..., sequential=FALSE, tune=TRUE) must either tune or warn.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1202 `if (!tuning_status[[var]] && isTRUE(tune[[var]]) && i == round(nseq / 2))`; vimpute.R:326-329 nseq <- 1 when !sequential; verified: Rscript run of installed build prints round(1/2)=0 and tuning_log with any(tuned_better)==FALSE

**Verifier:** Reproduced on the installed build. Mechanism verified in code: R/vimpute.R:326-328 forces nseq <- 1 when sequential = FALSE (message only shown if verbose); R/vimpute.R:1202 gates tuning on `i == round(nseq / 2)`, and round(1/2) == 0 in R (banker's rounding), so with nseq = 1 the condition can never be true. Empirical run: vimpute(sleep, method='ranger', sequential=FALSE, tune=TRUE) completed in 0.6 s, emitted NO warning, and returned a tuning_log with 5 entries all tuned_better = FALSE; the control run (sequential=TRUE, nseq=2, tune=TRUE) took 11.5 s and produced tuned_better = TRUE entries — proving tuning never executed in the first case. The log is genuinely indistinguishable from 'tuning ran and defaults won': R/vimpute.R:1421-1428 sets tuned_flag = FALSE both when hyperparameter_cache[[var]] is NULL (never tuned) and when tuning ran but defaults won (R/vimpute.R:1383 sets is_tuned = FALSE). The second part also reproduced: with sequential=TRUE, nseq=10, tune=TRUE and early convergence, the loop broke after 3 iterations (break at R/vimpute.R:2181-2183) — before the tuning point i = 5 — again with all tuned_better = FALSE and no warning. Earliest possible break is indeed i = 3: check_convergence returns counter = 0 at i = 1 (helper_vimpute.R:2193-2195) and requires two consecutive quiet iterations (helper_vimpute.R:2235-2238). The docs (R/vimpute.R:86, 'Tuning is performed halfway through nseq iterations') give no caveat for either case, so this is a silent contract violation, not intended behavior.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(42); r <- vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", sequential=FALSE, tune=TRUE); print(do.call(rbind, lapply(r$tuning_log, as.data.frame)))' -> 5 entries, all tuned_better FALSE, runtime ~0.6 s, no warning (vs 11.5 s when tuning actually fires with sequential=TRUE, nseq=2). Early-break variant: vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", sequential=TRUE, nseq=10, tune=TRUE, eps=1e9) stops after 3 iterations (15 log entries / 5 vars), never tunes. Full scripts: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/verify_claim1.R

### P1.37 [framework-design] complete(vimmi, 1) breaks as soon as the user loads mice or tidyr — the canonical pooling workflow masks VIM's own generic
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimmi.R*

vimmi.R:56 defines a fresh S3 generic `complete <- function(data, ...) UseMethod("complete")` and exports it (NAMESPACE:24). tidyr exports a generic of the same name and mice re-exports it, so `library(mice)` — which the docs themselves recommend for pooling (?vimmi: 'pooling with mice::pool()') — masks VIM::complete, and dispatch on the tidyr generic finds no vimmi method. Empirically confirmed: after library(VIM); library(mice), complete(vimmi_obj, 1) errors with 'nicht anwendbare Methode für complete auf Objekt der Klasse "vimmi"'. This poisons exactly the workflow vimmi exists for. Fix contract (three layers): (1) in .onLoad, conditionally register the method on the foreign generic: `if (requireNamespace("tidyr", quietly=TRUE)) registerS3method("complete", "vimmi", complete.vimmi, envir = asNamespace("tidyr"))` (plus an onLoad hook via setHook(packageEvent("tidyr", "onLoad"), ...) for load-order independence); (2) keep VIM's generic for mice-free sessions; (3) export an unambiguous alias `vim_complete(x, action)` and use it in all examples/vignettes. Same audit applies to with.vimmi (safe: base::with is the generic) and as.mids.vimmi (see separate finding).

**Evidence:** vimmi.R:56-58; NAMESPACE:5,24; verified: environmentName(environment(complete)) == 'tidyr' after library(mice), complete(mi,1) errors 'nicht anwendbare Methode'

**Verifier:** Reproduced exactly as claimed. R/vimmi.R:56-58 defines a fresh S3 generic `complete <- function(data, ...) UseMethod("complete")`; NAMESPACE line 24 exports it and line 5 registers S3method(complete, vimmi) on VIM's own generic only. No dynamic registration exists anywhere in the package (grep for registerS3method/setHook/onLoad across R/*.R returns nothing), so the vimmi method is invisible to the tidyr generic that mice re-exports. Empirical run: after library(VIM), complete(mi, 1) works (62x10, no NAs); after library(mice), environment(complete) reports 'tidyr' and complete(mi, 1) errors with 'nicht anwendbare Methode für complete auf Objekt der Klasse "vimmi" angewendet'. Identical failure after library(tidyr) alone. VIM::complete(mi, 1) still works, but the package's own documentation drives users into the broken path: ?vimmi recommends pooling via mice (R/vimmi.R:25-26) and both ?vimpute and ?vimmi examples use bare complete(result, 1) (R/vimpute.R:138-140, R/vimmi.R:41-42). Load order matters (VIM loaded last wins), but impute-then-pool is precisely the order library(VIM); library(mice) — the workflow vimmi exists for — and tidyr is also attached by library(tidyverse), making the breakage common in practice.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(7); mi <- suppressWarnings(vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE, m=2, boot=TRUE)); print(dim(complete(mi,1))); library(mice); print(environmentName(environment(complete))); complete(mi, 1)' -> works before, then 'tidyr', then error: nicht anwendbare Methode für 'complete' auf Objekt der Klasse "vimmi" angewendet. Full script: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/verify_claim2.R

### P1.38 [framework-design] No predictorMatrix equivalent: per-variable predictor choice is impossible for the default ML methods (ranger, xgboost)
*kind: design | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Predictor control exists only via `formula`, which is hard-rejected for ranger/xgboost: vimpute.R:684-687 stops with 'A formula can only be used with the robust, regularized, gam, or robgam methods' (duplicated at helper_vimpute.R:1091). For the default method (ranger) and xgboost, feature_cols is always setdiff(names(data), var) (vimpute.R:664) — every considered variable predicts every target. mice gives predictorMatrix + formulas for ALL methods; here the flagship ML methods have the least control, inverting the 'FLEXIBILITY beats mice' claim. Also missing: visit-sequence control (order is fixed to column order of variables_NA) and any way to use a variable as predictor-only vs impute-only (considered_variables conflates both roles). Proposed contract: `vimpute(data, ..., predictors = NULL, visit_sequence = c("asis","increasing.na","decreasing.na") | character())` where predictors is a named list of character vectors (`list(mpg = c("hp","wt"))`) or a logical/0-1 matrix accepted verbatim from mice::make.predictorMatrix for migration. Implementation is cheap in mlr3: after task creation call task$select(predictors[[var]]) — no formula machinery needed, works uniformly for every learner including ranger/xgboost. visit_sequence reorders variables_NA before the loop at vimpute.R:512.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:664 `feature_cols <- setdiff(names(data), var)`; vimpute.R:684-687 formula rejected for ranger/xgboost; helper_vimpute.R:1091; no visit-sequence argument in signature vimpute.R:154-176

**Verifier:** All factual assertions verified in code and empirically. (1) formula is the only predictor-control mechanism and is hard-rejected for ranger/xgboost: vimpute(sleep, method='ranger', formula=list(Sleep ~ Span + BodyWgt), sequential=FALSE) stops with 'A formula can only be used with the robust, regularized, gam, or robgam methods' (precheck at R/helper_vimpute.R:1091-1093, duplicated mid-loop at R/vimpute.R:684-686); same for xgboost; formula + robust is accepted. This restriction is documented (R/vimpute.R:55-57), so the rejection itself is intended — but that documented restriction is exactly what leaves the flagship default methods with zero predictor control. (2) For non-formula methods, feature_cols <- setdiff(names(data), var) at R/vimpute.R:664 — every considered variable always predicts every target. (3) formals(vimpute) confirms no predictors/predictorMatrix/visit_sequence argument (signature R/vimpute.R:154-176). (4) Role conflation confirmed: R/vimpute.R:194 subsets data to considered_variables (excluded variables are dropped as predictors AND from the output entirely), and R/vimpute.R:262-268 auto-imputes every considered variable containing NAs — verified empirically that a variable with NAs cannot be predictor-only, and excluding it removes it from the returned data. (5) Visit order is fixed to considered_variables order (default column order) via the loop at R/vimpute.R:512; the only workaround is reordering considered_variables, which also reorders output columns and is undocumented as a visit-sequence mechanism. Given the package's stated aim of beating mice on per-variable flexibility (mice offers predictorMatrix + formulas for all methods, plus visitSequence), this is a genuine design gap, correctly characterized. The proposed task$select() implementation route is plausible in mlr3 but was not tested.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); try(vimpute(sleep, method="ranger", sequential=FALSE, formula=list(Sleep ~ Span + BodyWgt))); print(names(formals(VIM::vimpute)))' -> error 'A formula can only be used with the robust, regularized, gam, or robgam methods'; formals contain no predictors/visit_sequence argument. ### P1.39 [formulas] evaluation() default vartypes="guess" silently returns zero error (guessing never implemented)
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R*

The signature is evaluation(x, y, m, vartypes = "guess") (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R:36) but no guessing code exists: only the literal branches vartypes=="numeric" (line 38) and vartypes=="factor" (line 41) do anything, so the default returns list(err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0) for arbitrarily bad imputations. Any other type string (e.g. "integer") is also silently ignored. Related doc rot in the same block: @details (lines 18-20) refers to a "ni parameter" that does not exist in any signature. Also note the denominator convention: err_num/err_cat sum differences over ALL cells but divide by sum(m) over missing cells only (lines 39, 42), and pfc does the same (lines 65-67) — correct only when x and y agree exactly on observed cells; silently inflated otherwise (e.g. comparing two independently imputed datasets). None of the metrics has a documented formula. Fix: implement type guessing (or make vartypes required and error on unknown strings), restrict sums to m, drop the ni sentence, and document each formula in the Rd.

**Evidence:** Reproduced with installed build: x=data.frame(a=c(1,2,3),b=c(4,5,6)); y=data.frame(a=c(1,99,3),b=c(4,5,66)); m marks the two changed cells; evaluation(x,y,m) returns err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0. Code: R/evaluation.R:36-48; phantom 'ni parameter' at R/evaluation.R:19-20; all-cells numerators at R/evaluation.R:39,42,66.

**Verifier:** Reproduced with the installed build (VIM 7.1.0): x=data.frame(a=c(1,2,3),b=c(4,5,6)); y=data.frame(a=c(1,99,3),b=c(4,5,66)); m marking the two changed cells; evaluation(x,y,m) returns err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0 despite grossly wrong imputations, and vartypes=c("integer","integer") also silently returns all zeros. Code confirms: the signature is evaluation(x, y, m, vartypes = "guess") (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R:36) but the body only has literal branches any(vartypes=="numeric") (line 38) and any(vartypes=="factor") (line 41); no guessing code exists anywhere in the package (grep over R/, man/, inst/, vignettes/ finds "guess" only in the signature and the auto-generated Rd), and the roxygen @param documents vartypes as "a vector of length ncol(x) specifying the variables types" with no mention of a guess mode. The phantom "ni parameter" is at R/evaluation.R:19 (propagated to man/evaluation.Rd:38); no ni argument exists in any signature in the file. The denominator convention also reproduced: with an additional disagreement on an OBSERVED cell, err_num inflates from 6504.5 (missing-cells-only expectation) to 7705 because line 39 sums squared differences over ALL cells but divides by sum(m) over missing cells; pfc (lines 65-67) likewise returns 1.5 (>1) for 3 differing cells over 2 missing cells. Every element of the claim verified.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); x <- data.frame(a=c(1,2,3), b=c(4,5,6)); y <- data.frame(a=c(1,99,3), b=c(4,5,66)); m <- matrix(FALSE,3,2); m[2,1] <- TRUE; m[3,2] <- TRUE; evaluation(x,y,m)  # -> err_num=0, err_cat=0, error=0; evaluation(x,y,m,vartypes=c("integer","integer")) # -> all 0; evaluation(x,y,m,vartypes=c("numeric","numeric")) # -> 6504.5; y2 <- y; y2[1,1] <- 50; evaluation(x,y2,m,vartypes=c("numeric","numeric")) # -> 7705 (observed-cell diff counted in numerator); pfc(x,y2,m) # -> 1.5

### P1.40 [formulas] Semi-continuous (mixed) variables are never range-scaled: unbounded Gower contribution silently dominates kNN distances
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R*

The R wrapper scales only `numerical` columns by range/IQR (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R:95-115); `mixed` columns are passed raw. The C++ kernel then uses the raw absolute difference for two non-spike values (src/gowerD.cpp:35-37), while every other variable type contributes at most 1. Consequence: for a semi-continuous variable like income (spike at 0), two non-zero values 50 apart contribute distance 50 while spike-vs-nonspike contributes 1 — so any kNN(..., mixed=) with a variable whose scale exceeds ~1 has its neighbour search dominated by that single variable, and the ordering is inverted (0 vs 100 counts as far closer than 100 vs 50). The package's own C++ unit test only feeds pre-scaled mixed values in [0,1] (inst/tinytest/test_gowerD_cpp.R:12-29) and the kNN mixed tests use rnorm data and only check that imputation happened (inst/tinytest/test_kNN.R:35-53), so the gap is untested. VERIFY: the JSS paper (Kowarik & Templ 2016, JSS 74(7)) description of the semi-continuous distance ('as for continuous variables' when both differ from mixed.constant, i.e. range-scaled) — check before citing; the internal inconsistency alone (numeric scaled, mixed not, identical C++ |x-y| logic) already establishes the defect. Fix: apply the same rmin/rmax scaling (excluding the spike value from the range, and scaling mixed.constant along) to mixed columns in gowerD().

**Evidence:** Reproduced: gowerD(data.frame(v=c(0,100,50)), numerical=vector(), mixed="v") returns d(100,50)=50 and d(0,100)=1; declaring the same column numerical gives all distances in [0,1]. Scaling loop covers only `numerical`: R/gowerD.R:111-114; raw |x-y| branch for mixed: src/gowerD.cpp:29-37.

**Verifier:** Reproduced with the installed build: gowerD(data.frame(v=c(0,100,50)), numerical=vector(), mixed="v") returns d(0,100)=1 and d(0,50)=1 but d(100,50)=50 — the spike-vs-nonspike distance (capped at 1) is dwarfed by the raw nonspike-nonspike difference, inverting the ordering; declaring the same column numerical yields all distances in [0,1]. Code confirms the mechanism: the standardization block at /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R:95-115 is guarded by if(length(numerical)>0) and the scaling loop (lines 111-114) iterates only seq_along(numerical), so mixed columns are passed raw; the C++ semi-continuous branch (src/gowerD.cpp:29-37) uses weight*abs(x-y)/weightsum for two non-spike values — identical to the numeric branch that DOES get scaled — establishing the internal inconsistency without needing the JSS paper. kNN-level consequence also reproduced: kNN(data.frame(inc=c(0,98,100), y=c(10,20,NA)), variable="y", dist_var="inc", mixed="inc", k=1) imputes y[3]=10 (the inc=0 donor) instead of 20 (the inc=98 donor), i.e. 0 is treated as closer to 100 than 98 is. The cited test characterizations are accurate: inst/tinytest/test_gowerD_cpp.R:12-29 feeds mixed values only in {0.0, 0.8, 0.3} (all within [0,1]) and inst/tinytest/test_kNN.R:35-53 uses rnorm-scale mixed data checking only that imputation occurred (sum(d2$y_imp)==6L). No documentation (man/gowerD.Rd, man/kNN.Rd, vignettes) states mixed variables must be pre-scaled, so this is not intended behavior. I did not independently verify the JSS paper's formula wording (the claim itself flags that as VERIFY), but the defect stands on the code alone.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); gowerD(data.frame(v=c(0,100,50)), numerical=vector(), mixed="v")  # d(100,50)=50, d(0,100)=d(0,50)=1; gowerD(data.frame(v=c(0,100,50)))  # numerical: all in [0,1]; kNN(data.frame(inc=c(0,98,100), y=c(10,20,NA)), variable="y", dist_var="inc", mixed="inc", k=1, imp_var=FALSE)$y[3]  # -> 10, donor inc=0 chosen over inc=98
