### P2.1 [check] tests/test_vimpute_smoke.R: fragile dual source()/library() mode, hand-rolled test framework, always runs in full on CRAN
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/tests/test_vimpute_smoke.R*

The file is a standalone script, not tinytest-managed. (a) Dual mode (lines 29-35): when run from the repo root it source()s R/helper_vimpute.R, R/vimmi.R, R/vimpute.R into globalenv WITHOUT attaching VIM -- it then tests unbuilt source code with no namespace isolation, silently diverging from the installed package; this works today only because the trio is currently self-contained (verified empirically: sourcing + a minimal vimpute call succeeds), and it breaks the moment vimpute.R calls any function defined in another R/ file. Under R CMD check the cwd is VIM.Rcheck/tests so it always takes the library(VIM) branch (verified in test_vimpute_smoke.Rout: all 21 run_case blocks + 8 optional cases ran, 'All vimpute smoke tests passed', 16-17s). (b) quit(status=0L) at line 15 as skip mechanism kills the R session if a developer source()s the file interactively. (c) Lines 37-72 re-implement check()/expect_warning()/expect_error() by hand, so a failure surfaces as an opaque script error with no assertion counts. (d) It is not in .Rbuildignore, and its guard packages (mlr3 stack, ranger, future, data.table) are all Imports, so the skip never triggers on CRAN -- the full model-fitting suite always runs there (16s on an M-series Mac; expect 40-60s+ on CRAN hardware). Clean layout: tests/ keeps only tinytest.R; move the cases to inst/tinytest/test_vimpute_smoke.R using native tinytest expect_error/expect_warning (which support pattern matching), gate heavy cases with if (!at_home()) exit_file("smoke suite runs at home"); drop source()-mode entirely -- dev iteration against source is pkgload::load_all() + tinytest::run_test_file(), not a shipped test file.

**Evidence:** tests/test_vimpute_smoke.R:13-16 (quit skip), :29-35 (dual mode), :37-72 (hand-rolled expectations); DESCRIPTION Imports: mlr3, mlr3pipelines, mlr3tuning, mlr3learners, paradox, ranger, future; 00check.log:76 'Running test_vimpute_smoke.R [16s/17s]'; Rout shows library(VIM) branch + 21 case markers; source-mode verified working from repo root; introduced in commits c5e66e7/ce1501b

### P2.2 [vimpute-core] 'identical imputations' warning (commit 8cc3020) is factually wrong for the default method
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

vimpute.R:340-343 warns 'm > 1 without boot/uncert/pmm: all imputations will be identical'. Verified false for the default method ranger: forest training consumes RNG, so m=3 runs produce different imputations (m1 != m2 confirmed on the build); factor targets also get probabilistic class draws (helper_vimpute.R:1979-1982) regardless of boot/uncert. Conversely, the warning is suppressed in a case where imputations ARE (near-)deterministic: pmm=TRUE with default pmm_k=1 and pmm_k_method='mean' on a deterministic learner (robust/glmnet) sets has_any_pmm=TRUE and skips the warning. Suggested wording: 'imputations will not reflect proper imputation uncertainty (identical for deterministic learners)', and extend the condition to cover pmm with k=1/deterministic aggregation.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:340-343; empirical: ranger m=3 imputations m1==m2 is FALSE while the warning claims identity; pmm k=1 'mean' path suppresses the warning via has_any_pmm (vimpute.R:333)

**Verifier:** Both directions of the warning's logic are demonstrably wrong. (1) The warning at R/vimpute.R:340-343 fires for the default method ranger with m>1, yet imputations are NOT identical: the m-loop (vimpute.R:419-445) recurses with m=1 and never re-seeds, so ranger's forest training consumes RNG each run. Reproduced on the installed build: vimpute(sleep, m=3) warned 'all imputations will be identical' while all(m1==m2) was FALSE for all 5 variables (NonD, Dream, Sleep, Span, Gest; max|m1-m2| up to 5.8 for Gest). (2) Factor targets get probabilistic class draws (helper_vimpute.R:1979-1982, condition isFALSE(sequential) || i == nseq) regardless of boot/uncert: with sequential=FALSE and ranger, 37/90 factor imputations differed between m1 and m2 while the warning still fired. (3) Conversely, the warning is suppressed via has_any_pmm (vimpute.R:333, 340) in a case where imputations ARE exactly identical: pmm=TRUE with defaults (pmm_k=NULL maps to 1L at helper_vimpute.R:669; pmm_k_method='mean' takes mean of the single nearest donor, helper_vimpute.R:2104-2126 — fully deterministic) on the deterministic xgboost learner. Reproduced: vimpute(sleep, method='xgboost', pmm=TRUE, m=2) emitted NO warning yet all 5 variables had max|m1-m2|=0 (bitwise identical across imputations). The warning text overstates for stochastic learners and the suppression condition understates for deterministic-PMM; the suggested rewording is justified.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); data(sleep, package="VIM"); set.seed(1); r <- vimpute(sleep, m=3, imp_var=FALSE); print(sapply(names(r$imp), function(v) all(r$imp[[v]]$m1 == r$imp[[v]]$m2)))  # warning fires, all FALSE; set.seed(2); r2 <- vimpute(sleep, method="xgboost", pmm=TRUE, m=2, imp_var=FALSE); print(sapply(names(r2$imp), function(v) all(r2$imp[[v]]$m1 == r2$imp[[v]]$m2)))  # no warning, all TRUE' (full script: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/test_claim1.R)

### P2.3 [vimpute-core] Final probabilistic factor draw on early convergence is computed and discarded (dead code); factor imputations stay biased argmax
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

For factor targets, intermediate iterations impute the argmax class and only i==nseq draws from predicted probabilities (helper_vimpute.R:1979-1986). When check_convergence() breaks early (two quiet iterations), the block at helper_vimpute.R:2245-2268 recomputes probabilistic draws via apply(...) but the result is never assigned or returned — a pure no-op — and it only references the LAST variable's learner/pred_task anyway. Consequence: on early convergence (common with default eps=0.005), all factor variables are imputed by majority-class argmax, systematically inflating the modal category, contrary to the design intent evidenced by the dead block. Fix: on break, redo the final draw per factor variable and apply it, then remove the dead apply().

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:2265-2267 `apply(pred_probs, 1, function(probs) sample(...))` result unassigned; draw condition helper_vimpute.R:1979 `isFALSE(sequential) || i == nseq`

**Verifier:** Dead code confirmed by reading: in check_convergence (R/helper_vimpute.R:2189-2271), the block at 2245-2268 recomputes normalized predicted probabilities and executes apply(pred_probs, 1, function(probs) sample(levels(...), 1, prob=probs)) at 2265-2267, but the result is never assigned or returned — the function's return value is the list at line 2270. It also only references the last-processed variable's data_temp/target_col/learner/pred_task, which are leftover loop variables passed at the call site (R/vimpute.R:2164-2179). Behavioral consequence reproduced on the installed build: n=600, binary factor y (65/35 marginal) with 240 NAs, predictors pure noise. With defaults (sequential=TRUE, nseq=10, eps=0.005) and method='xgboost', the loop broke early ('stop after 5 iterations', cat_diff 0.004167 < eps twice), and the imputed distribution was 193 A / 47 B (80.4% modal class) — identical under two different seeds, proving no probabilistic draw was applied at the end. The intended draw path (forced via sequential=FALSE, where helper_vimpute.R:1979 makes the draw unconditional) gave ~149 A / 91 B (~62%, matching the predicted probabilities) and was seed-dependent. Default method ranger showed the same effect: early break at iteration 3, 196/44 and 202/38 across seeds (82-84% modal) vs ~62% under the draw path. So on early convergence — which the reproduction shows is common with default eps — factor imputations remain majority-inflated argmax, exactly as claimed. One side observation (not refuting the claim): with method='robust' (classif.glm_rob) on the same data, factor imputations alternated completely every iteration (cat_diff=1.0), so convergence never triggered there; the claim reproduces cleanly with the default ranger and with xgboost.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/test_claim2b.R — output shows for xgboost: 'stop after 5 iterations', imputed table 193A/47B identical across seeds 101/999, vs sequential=FALSE draw path 149A/91B seed-dependent; ranger: 'stop after 3 iterations', 196A/44B vs draw-path 148A/92B.

### P2.4 [vimpute-core] Silent column type changes: logical -> numeric, character -> factor, ordered -> unordered factor
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

precheck() section 8 (helper_vimpute.R:1203-1220) coerces ordered factors to plain factors, logicals to numeric, characters to factors, and build_vimpute_result() never restores original types. Confirmed on the build: input (numeric, logical, character, ordered) returns classes (numeric, numeric, factor, factor). A logical column with imputed value 0.4 (regression prediction) is also possible since it is treated as continuous. Ordered variables lose ordering information both for modelling (no ordinal handling) and in the output. At minimum restore types on output and document; better, model logicals as binary classification and keep ordered as ordered.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1203-1220; empirical: classes out 'num=numeric lg=numeric ch=factor ord=factor'

### P2.5 [vimpute-core] Semicontinuous imputation uses expected-value shrinkage pi_hat * pred and silently skips boot/uncert
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

For semicontinuous variables the imputed value is `preds <- pi_hat * preds_reg` (helper_vimpute.R:1930): probability-of-positive times conditional-positive prediction. Imputed values are therefore neither 0 nor plausible positive values (e.g. pi_hat=0.5, pred=6 imputes 3), distorting both the zero share and the positive-part distribution — a marginal-distribution defect that matters for the 'beats mice' bar. Additionally, bootstrap and uncertainty injection are gated with `!is_sc` (vimpute.R:1940, vimpute.R:1975; helper_vimpute.R:2033), so under m>1 semicontinuous variables contribute essentially no between-imputation variability, without any warning. A two-part draw (Bernoulli(pi_hat) then conditional positive draw) would be the statistically defensible default, at least when uncert != 'none' or m > 1.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1930 `preds <- pi_hat * preds_reg`; vimpute.R:1940 `if (boot && !is_sc)`; helper_vimpute.R:2033 uncertainty gated by `!is_sc`

### P2.6 [vimpute-core] No learner encapsulation/fallback: a single learner failure on one variable aborts the entire imputation
*kind: method-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

learner$train(task) (vimpute.R:1936, also 1751, 1848) and learner$predict(...) run without tryCatch and without mlr3 encapsulation ($encapsulate('evaluate'/'callr') + $fallback). Only tuning and the bootstrap refit are guarded. If e.g. glmrob fails to converge or xgboost errors on variable 5 of 20 in iteration 8, all completed work is lost with a raw mlr3 error that does not name the variable. mlr3 provides exactly this machinery (fallback = lrn('regr.featureless')); wiring it in per-variable with a warning ('learner X failed for variable Y, fell back to Z') would materially deliver the promised USABILITY edge over mice, where a chain rarely dies wholesale. Sketch: any data where lmrob fails (e.g. constant predictor after donorcond filtering) currently stops vimpute() entirely.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1936 bare `learner$train(task)`; no $encapsulate/$fallback anywhere in R/vimpute.R or helper_vimpute.R (grep confirms only tuning/boot tryCatch at vimpute.R:1233, 1332, 1964)

### P2.7 [vimpute-helpers] precheck silently misassigns methods for unnamed method lists aligned with all columns
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

In the unnamed-list branch (R/helper_vimpute.R:1068-1078), when length(method)==length(variables) the mapping takes the FIRST length(variables_NA) entries (all_methods[seq_along(variables_NA)], line 1078) instead of the entries at the positions of the NA-variables. Verified: data(x1 complete, x2 with NAs), method=list('ranger','gam') -> x2 is imputed with 'ranger' (the method positioned for x1), not 'gam'. No error, no warning. The branch is also undocumented (roxygen promises only a single global method or a named list). Fix: all_methods[match(variables_NA, variables)] for the length(variables) case, or drop the unnamed-list branch and error with a clear message.

**Evidence:** Repro via VIM:::precheck(data, method=list('ranger','gam'), ...) with only x2 missing -> pc$method[['x2']] == 'ranger'.

**Verifier:** The unnamed-list branch (R/helper_vimpute.R:1068-1078) maps methods via all_methods[seq_along(variables_NA)] (line 1078), i.e. it takes the FIRST length(variables_NA) entries instead of the entries at the NA-variables' column positions. Reproduced: data with x1 complete and x2 containing NAs, VIM:::precheck(..., method=list('ranger','gam'), variables_NA='x2') assigns pc$method[['x2']] == 'ranger' (the entry positioned for x1); the reversed list('gam','ranger') assigns 'gam' — proving pure take-first indexing, not positional matching. End-to-end vimpute(d, method=list('ranger','gam'), verbose=TRUE) trains ranger on x2 ('Ranger params for variable x2') with no warning or error. A 3-column case (x1 complete, x2/x3 missing, method=list('ranger','gam','robust')) shifts both assignments: x2->'ranger', x3->'gam' instead of positional 'gam'/'robust'. The roxygen for 'method' (R/vimpute.R:10-21) documents only a single global method or a named list, so the unnamed-list branch is also undocumented, exactly as claimed. Note the length(method)==length(variables_NA) sub-case of the same branch is internally consistent (entries align with NA-variables in order); the bug is specifically the length(variables) alignment case.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('<scratch>/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); library(data.table); set.seed(1); d<-data.table(x1=rnorm(60),x2=rnorm(60)); d$x2[sample(60,10)]<-NA; pc<-VIM:::precheck(data=copy(d),pmm=FALSE,formula=FALSE,method=list('ranger','gam'),sequential=TRUE,pmm_k=NULL,pmm_k_method=NULL,learner_params=NULL,tune=FALSE,variables_NA='x2'); pc$method[['x2']]  # 'ranger', expected 'gam'

### P2.8 [vimpute-helpers] Convergence-tracking fix (f0571ac) incomplete: uncert='normalerror'/'resid' disables early stopping
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

predict_imputations tracks raw model predictions for convergence only when PMM or uncert in c('pmm','midastouch') (R/helper_vimpute.R:2083-2087); for uncert='normalerror'/'resid' the noise is injected into preds at line 2076 BEFORE convergence_preds is taken, so convergence_data carries fresh random noise every iteration and check_convergence's total_diff plateaus around 2*sigma^2, never dropping below eps. Verified: identical data/seed, method='robust', nseq=8: uncert='none' and pmm=TRUE both stop after 3 iterations; uncert='normalerror' runs all 8 with total_diff oscillating 0.16-0.45. Every uncert-based run silently pays the full nseq cost. Fix: include 'normalerror' and 'resid' in the raw_model_preds condition at line 2083 (i.e., track raw preds for all stochastic uncert methods).

**Evidence:** Verbose traces from installed build: baseline 'stop after 3 iterations' (total_diff 6.8e-4 -> 2.8e-5); normalerror total_diff 0.29, 0.37, 0.45, 0.37, 0.22, 0.16, 0.22 across iterations 2-8, no stop.

**Verifier:** Code reading confirms the mechanism: for uncert='normalerror'/'resid', inject_uncertainty adds fresh random noise into preds at R/helper_vimpute.R:2076, and the convergence_preds selection at R/helper_vimpute.R:2083-2087 falls back to the noisy preds because its condition only covers isTRUE(pmm[[var]]) || uncert %in% c('pmm','midastouch'). git show f0571ac confirms this exact condition was introduced by the 'fix convergence tracking' commit, so normalerror/resid were simply left out of the fix — the raw model predictions (which DO stabilize) are available in raw_model_preds at line 2025 but unused for these two methods. Reproduced with method='robust', nseq=8, sequential=TRUE, eps=0.005 on identical seeded data: uncert='none' stops after 3 iterations (total_diff 6.65e-4 -> 4.1e-5), pmm=TRUE stops after 3 (7.35e-4 -> 1.7e-5), uncert='pmm' stops after 3 (2.6e-3 -> 1.5e-4); but uncert='normalerror' runs all 8 iterations with total_diff oscillating 0.76-1.30 and uncert='resid' runs all 8 with 0.61-1.27 — a noise floor consistent with ~2*sigma^2 per variable (sigma=0.5, 2 NA-variables => ~1.0), which can never drop below eps. Every normalerror/resid run therefore silently pays the full nseq cost and never reports convergence. Impact is wasted compute and a misleading non-convergence trace (results themselves are not wrong); the claimed fix (adding 'normalerror'/'resid' to the raw_model_preds condition at line 2083) is consistent with the intent f0571ac established for the other stochastic methods.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c('<scratch>/Rlib', .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(2024); n<-150; x1<-rnorm(n); x2<-rnorm(n); d<-data.frame(x1,x2,y1=2*x1-x2+rnorm(n,.5),y2=-x1+.5*x2+rnorm(n,.5)); d$y1[sample(n,20)]<-NA; d$y2[sample(n,20)]<-NA; set.seed(123); vimpute(d,method='robust',nseq=8,verbose=TRUE)  # 'stop after 3 iterations'; rerun with uncert='normalerror' -> all 8 iterations, total_diff 0.76-1.30

### P2.9 [vimpute-helpers] check_convergence contains a dead re-sampling block: result of the final categorical draw is discarded
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

On the early-break path, if the last-processed variable's target is a factor, check_convergence re-predicts probabilities and samples labels via apply(pred_probs, 1, function(probs) sample(...)) (R/helper_vimpute.R:2245-2268) -- but the result is never assigned or returned; the function then returns list(...) at line 2270. Consequences: (a) when the loop breaks early (i < nseq), categorical imputations keep the deterministic which.max values from predict_imputations (R/helper_vimpute.R:1984-1985), whereas a full run to i==nseq samples from the predictive distribution (lines 1979-1982) -- so early convergence yields systematically modal-class imputations and distorted category marginals, apparently exactly what this dead block was meant to prevent; (b) wasted predict cost and RNG-state consumption for a discarded result; (c) side effects: learner$predict_type mutated (line 2246) and a possible stop() at line 2250; (d) it only sees the learner/pred_task of the LAST variable in the loop, so even if assigned it could not fix all factor variables. Fix: either delete the block, or restructure so that upon convergence each factor variable gets one final stochastic draw applied to data/data_new.

**Evidence:** Code-level: apply(...) at helper_vimpute.R:2265-2268 is the last expression before the unconditional list(...) return at 2270 and its value is unused. Caller (vimpute.R:2164-2183) only reads no_change_counter/should_break.

**Verifier:** Code reading confirms all parts. The apply(pred_probs, 1, function(probs) sample(...)) at R/helper_vimpute.R:2265-2268 is the last expression of an if-block whose value is never assigned; the function then unconditionally returns list(no_change_counter, should_break) at line 2270, and the only caller (R/vimpute.R:2164-2183) reads just those two fields. Empirical mock repro of VIM:::check_convergence on the installed build: returned names are exactly 'no_change_counter, should_break' (no sampled labels anywhere), the learner's $predict was called once (wasted compute), and .Random.seed advanced (RNG consumed for a discarded result). Consequence (a) demonstrated end-to-end: with a 61/39 binary factor independent of predictors, method='ranger', sequential=TRUE, nseq=10, an early break at i=3 (eps=10) yields imputed modal-class share 0.74, while a full run to i==nseq (eps=0, stochastic draw per helper_vimpute.R:1979-1982) yields 0.64, close to the observed marginal 0.61 — early convergence systematically inflates the modal class via the deterministic which.max branch (helper_vimpute.R:1984-1985). Consequences (c)/(d) also verified: learner$predict_type is mutated at line 2246 (by-reference for real R6 learners), stop() at 2250 is reachable on the convergence path, and data_temp/target_col/learner/pred_task at the call site are leftovers of the LAST variable of the per-variable loop (assigned at vimpute.R:2114 inside the loop ending at 2160), so the block could not fix all factor variables even if assigned. Minor precision: early-break imputations are per-row modal classes, so the share is 0.74 rather than literally 100% modal — direction and mechanism exactly as claimed.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/repro_claim1_mock.R -> 'returned names: no_change_counter, should_break; mock predict called: 1; RNG state advanced: TRUE; any sampled labels in return: FALSE'. Rscript .../repro_claim1_e2e.R -> early break imputed shares a=0.74/b=0.26 vs full run a=0.64/b=0.36 (observed marginal a=0.61).

### P2.10 [vimpute-helpers] eps convergence criterion is absolute and scale-dependent (unnormalized sum of MSE changes)
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

check_convergence sums raw mean-squared changes across numeric variables and compares against eps=0.005 (R/helper_vimpute.R:2208, 2222, 2231). The criterion therefore depends on measurement units and on the number of NA variables. Verified: identical data and seed, method='robust' -- original units converge after 3 iterations; the same data multiplied by 1000 shows total_diff 676 -> 28 -> 3.2 -> 0.38 -> 0.048 -> 0.0062 -> 0.0008 and does NOT stop within nseq=8. Income-scale variables will effectively never trigger early stopping; milli-scale variables 'converge' instantly. Recommendation: use a relative criterion, e.g. missForest-style sum((new-old)^2)/sum(new^2) per variable type, or normalize each variable's change by the variance of its observed values; document the semantics of eps accordingly (current @param text 'predictions change less than this amount' hides the scale dependence).

**Evidence:** Empirical trace from installed build: unscaled run 'stop after 3 iterations'; x1000-scaled run exhausts all 8 iterations (total_diff at iter 7 = 0.0062 > eps).

### P2.11 [vimpute-helpers] Tuning search space for regr.lm_rob is statistically mis-specified: tuning.psi/chi in [1.2, 1.5] excludes sane values
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

build_vimpute_search_space (R/helper_vimpute.R:2390-2397) tunes tuning.chi and tuning.psi both in [1.2, 1.5]. For the bisquare psi used by this learner, the standard tuning.psi is 4.685 (95% Gaussian efficiency) and tuning.chi is 1.5477 (50% breakdown); the search range excludes both, so with tune=TRUE for method='robust' every candidate is a drastically low-efficiency estimator and the tuner cannot even reach the untuned default (self$param_set$values tuning.psi=4.69, helper_vimpute.R:43). Tuning can only make the robust method worse. Looks like tuning.psi was confused with tuning.chi's neighborhood. Fix: tune tuning.psi over roughly [2.5, 6] (efficiency trade-off) and leave tuning.chi at its breakdown-determined default (or tie it to psi), and consider tuning method M vs MM instead. Same block: max.it tuning [50,200] is harmless but pointless as a hyperparameter.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:2391-2394 vs learner defaults at lines 17-18/42-43; robustbase defaults for bisquare MM are tuning.psi=4.685061, tuning.chi=1.54764 (excluded by the [1.2,1.5] range).

**Verifier:** build_vimpute_search_space (R/helper_vimpute.R:2391-2394) tunes tuning.chi and tuning.psi both in p_dbl(1.2, 1.5). Verified against defaults: the VIM learner default is tuning.psi=4.69/tuning.chi=1.55 (helper_vimpute.R:17-18, 42-43) and robustbase's bisquare standards are tuning.psi=4.685061 (95% Gaussian efficiency) and tuning.chi=1.54764 (50% breakdown); programmatic reachability check on the built ParamSet returns FALSE for both — the tuner cannot reach the untuned default psi, nor even the standard chi (1.54764 lies just above the 1.5 upper bound, supporting the 'confused with tuning.chi's neighborhood' reading). Numerical integration: asymptotic Gaussian efficiency of the bisquare M-step at c in [1.2, 1.5] is 16.1%-26.8% vs 95.0% at 4.685. Finite-sample simulation with the learner-exact lmrob control (method='MM' per helper_vimpute.R:40, which overrides KS2014's SMDM so all candidates DO fit without error): clean-data slope MSE inflates 3.03x at chi=psi=1.2 and 2.48x at chi=1.35/psi=1.5 relative to the default — every candidate is drastically low-efficiency, as claimed. Additional support: the same dispatch branch (line 2390) also serves classif.glm_rob, whose param set is EMPTY (no tuning.chi/tuning.psi/max.it exist), so tuning the robust method for factor targets can never work at all. One nuance softening only the phrasing 'tuning can only make the robust method worse': vimpute compares tuned vs default via CV and keeps the default when tuned loses (R/vimpute.R:1271-1307, 1361-1390), so the typical practical harm is wasted tuning compute that can never yield an improvement, with actively worse params adopted only when CV noise flips the comparison; the mis-specification itself is unambiguous.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/repro_claim2d.R -> search space bounds 1.2/1.5, 'tuner can reach learner default tuning.psi=4.69 : FALSE', 'tuner can reach robustbase tuning.chi=1.54764 : FALSE', 'classif.glm_rob param ids: [ ]'. Rscript .../repro_claim2_stats.R -> bisquare efficiency 16.1%/21.2%/26.8% at c=1.2/1.35/1.5 vs 95.0% at 4.685; robustbase defaults tuning.psi=4.685061, tuning.chi=1.54764. Rscript .../repro_claim2e.R -> slope MSE inflation 3.03x (chi=psi=1.2) and 2.48x (chi=1.35, psi=1.5) with learner-exact method='MM' control, 0 fit errors.

### P2.12 [vimmi-mi] Default robustboot="stratified" is a robustness-motivated bootstrap, not a sampling-distribution bootstrap — questionable as the MI default
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: medium | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

bootstrap_resample (helper_vimpute.R:1456-1470) with the default strategy "stratified" (vimpute.R:173) splits training rows into 'good' (|resid| <= 75% quantile) and 'bad' groups and draws EXACTLY round(n*0.75) from good and n - that from bad. This is designed to stabilize robust refits, but for MI the bootstrap's job is to approximate the sampling distribution of the parameter estimates (bootstrap-MI a la mice norm.boot uses iid resampling). Fixing strata counts removes the multinomial variability in group sizes and conditions on the residual ranking of the original fit, which biases the implied parameter-uncertainty distribution (typically understating it) — and it is applied to ALL learners (ranger, xgboost, glmnet), not just robust ones, since robustboot's default is global. "residual" (helper_vimpute.R:1473-1477) is worse for MI: it actively downweights high-residual rows, shrinking residual scale in each bootstrap fit. Recommendation: when m>1, default to strategy="standard" (classical bootstrap) unless the user explicitly opts into a robust strategy for a robust learner, and document that the robust strategies trade MI properness for outlier resistance. This distinction (robust point imputation vs valid variance estimation) deserves an explicit paragraph in the docs since it is exactly where VIM wants to differentiate from mice.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1415-1490 (bootstrap_resample: stratified fixes n_good=round(n*alpha), residual samples prob = max|r|-|r|); vimpute.R:173 (robustboot="stratified" default), vimpute.R:1945-1951 (applied for every method when boot=TRUE).

### P2.13 [vimmi-mi] No end-to-end tests for vimpute(m>1): vimmi creation, imputation variability, as.mids, and pooling are all untested
*kind: test-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: inst/tinytest/test_vimmi.R*

inst/tinytest/test_vimmi.R (100 lines) exercises only a hand-constructed VIM:::new_vimmi object (constructor, complete actions, with, print, summary); no test calls vimpute(..., m>1), so the entire m>1 recursion (vimpute.R:404-488), the imp_collector extraction, where-matrix construction, as.mids.vimmi -> mice::as.mids round-trip, and mice::pool compatibility have zero coverage. grep over inst/tinytest confirms no other file covers m>1/vimmi/as.mids. Both P0 findings above (identical PMM imputations; variance-free boot+none imputations) would be caught by a cheap regression test asserting that for m>1 with a proper configuration the imputed columns DIFFER across m (e.g. sd(colMeans(imp))>0 per variable) and that a deterministic configuration triggers a warning. Suggested additions (tinytest, guarded by requireNamespace("mice")): (1) small data, method="regularized", m=3, boot=TRUE, uncert="resid" → class vimmi, nmis correct, imputations differ across m; (2) as.mids.vimmi → mice::is.mids TRUE, dim(imp[[v]])==c(nmis,m), colSums(where)==NA counts; (3) mice::pool(with(res, lm(...))) runs without error and B>0; (4) complete(res,"long") row count == (m)*nrow.

**Evidence:** test_vimmi.R:14 builds the object via VIM:::new_vimmi directly; no vimpute(m=...) call anywhere in inst/tinytest (grep). Verified the end-to-end pipeline manually in t2_mids.R (it works today, but nothing guards it).

### P2.14 [cellwise] imputeCellwise() dispatcher exposes 2 working methods of the 6-method family; cellM option is a stop() stub; return types heterogeneous
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellwise.R*

R/imputeCellwise.R:994-1001: match.arg restricts method to c('cellIRMI','cellM','cellEM'); cellMCD, cellMM and cellReg are rejected outright (confirmed empirically), and method='cellM' unconditionally stop()s ('cellM requires a formula; use imputeCellM() directly') — an advertised option that can never succeed. The project docs (CLAUDE.md) describe imputeCellwise() as the dispatcher over the whole cellwise family. Return shapes also diverge: cellIRMI/cellMM/cellReg return 4-component lists, cellEM adds mu/Sigma/epsilon/pseudo_loglik, cellMCD adds mu/Sigma and for m>1 returns a structurally different list (imputed_list/cellweights_list/..., R/imputeCellEM.R:1024-1031) that is undocumented in its @return section; nothing is classed, so there are no print/summary methods and no programmatic dispatch. Fix: extend the switch to all six methods (cellM can dispatch when a formula is supplied via ...), drop or repair the stub, standardize on a classed return (e.g. 'cellImp') with common core components, and route m>1 through vimmi.

**Evidence:** Empirical: imputeCellwise(df, method='cellMCD'/'cellMM'/'cellReg') -> match.arg error listing only cellIRMI/cellM/cellEM; method='cellM' -> 'ERROR: cellM requires a formula; use imputeCellM() directly'.

### P2.15 [cellwise] imputeCellIRMI: two documented argument values error out (weight_update='univariate', init_weights='marginal'); hard_threshold documented behavior differs from implementation
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellwise.R*

The roxygen for weight_update (R/imputeCellwise.R:60-64) documents values 'multivariate' or 'univariate', but match.arg at :129 accepts c('multivariate','per-variable') — the documented value errors. The roxygen for init_weights (:65-68) documents 'mcd' or 'marginal', but match.arg at :130 accepts c('mcd','univariate','ddc') — documented 'marginal' errors and the implemented 'univariate'/'ddc' options are undocumented (ddc's silent fallback to univariate weights when cellWise is missing at :207-235 also deserves a message, unlike the warning imputeCellMCD emits in the analogous case at R/imputeCellEM.R:1159-1163). @param hard_threshold (:69-71) claims 'After convergence, cells with weight below this value are flagged as contaminated', but the implementation (:242-261) deletes such cells BEFORE iteration (sets them NA and re-imputes, detect-once) and returns no flag component at all. Also @param uncert omits the accepted 'none' (:128). Fix docs and option names together; consider deprecating aliases gracefully.

**Evidence:** Repro: imputeCellIRMI(df, weight_update='univariate') -> "'arg' sollte eines von 'multivariate, per-variable' sein"; imputeCellIRMI(df, init_weights='marginal') -> "'arg' sollte eines von 'mcd, univariate, ddc' sein".

**Verifier:** All parts reproduced/verified. (1) Roxygen at R/imputeCellwise.R:60-64 (shipped as man/imputeCellIRMI.Rd:48-52) documents weight_update values 'multivariate'/'univariate', but match.arg at R/imputeCellwise.R:129 accepts c('multivariate','per-variable'): calling imputeCellIRMI(df, weight_update='univariate') errors ('arg' should be one of "multivariate", "per-variable"), while the undocumented 'per-variable' is accepted. (2) Roxygen :65-68 (Rd :54-57) documents init_weights 'mcd'/'marginal', but match.arg at :130 accepts c('mcd','univariate','ddc'): init_weights='marginal' errors; implemented 'univariate' and 'ddc' are undocumented. (3) @param uncert (roxygen :57-59, Rd :44-46) lists pmm/normalerror/resid but match.arg at :128 also accepts 'none' — verified uncert='none' runs fine. (4) hard_threshold docs (roxygen :69-71, Rd :59-61) claim 'After convergence, cells with weight below this value are flagged as contaminated', but the implementation at :242-261 is detect-once BEFORE the outer loop (flagged observed cells set to NA, M updated, data re-initialised and re-imputed), and the return list at :493-498 has only data_imputed/cellweights/converged/iterations — no flag component (verified empirically via names()). (5) The ddc fallback claim also holds: at :206-207 the branch requires requireNamespace('cellWise'); when cellWise is missing the else branch at :231-235 silently uses univariate cellWeights with no message, whereas imputeCellMCD warns in its analogous cellWise-missing fallback at R/imputeCellEM.R:1159-1163. Documentation-vs-implementation bug, correctly rated P2.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(4); df <- data.frame(u=rnorm(30), w=rnorm(30), z=rnorm(30)); df$u[1:4] <- NA; try(imputeCellIRMI(df, weight_update="univariate")); try(imputeCellIRMI(df, init_weights="marginal")); r <- imputeCellIRMI(df, uncert="none"); print(names(r))'  # both documented values error via match.arg; undocumented "none" accepted; return components are data_imputed, cellweights, converged, iterations (no contamination flag).

### P2.16 [cellwise] Categorical imputation is silently deterministic mode imputation in cellIRMI/cellMCD/cellMM — contradicting cellIRMI's own comments and inconsistent with cellEM/cellM
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellwise.R*

imputeCellIRMI imputes categoricals with which.max (mode) during iteration with the comment 'stochastic sampling is added in the final uncertainty step' (R/imputeCellwise.R:382-387), but the final uncertainty step handles only continuous variables and skips categoricals with the contradictory comment 'categorical variables already have stochastic sampling' (:488) — so no draw ever happens. Confirmed: categorical imputations are bit-identical across different RNG seeds. imputeCellMCD (R/imputeCellEM.R:1386-1388) and imputeCellMM (R/imputeCellMM.R:147-149) have the same deterministic which.max behavior, while imputeCellEM (:500-504) and imputeCellM (:750-754) sample from predicted probabilities. Mode imputation systematically over-represents modal categories and understates uncertainty (relevant for any MI use), and the family behaves inconsistently for the same data. Fix: sample from predicted probabilities in the final pass (respecting uncert='none'), or document deterministic classification as intended for all methods.

**Evidence:** Repro: imputeCellIRMI on n=150 mixed data with 50 missing factor cells, two runs under different seeds -> identical(r1$g[gm], r2$g[gm]) TRUE. Contradictory comments at R/imputeCellwise.R:383 vs :488.

**Verifier:** All cited code locations verified and the behavior reproduced empirically. imputeCellIRMI imputes categoricals with which.max during iteration (R/imputeCellwise.R:384-387) under the comment 'stochastic sampling is added in the final uncertainty step' (:383), but the final uncertainty block (:465-490) only enters the is_continuous[j] branch (:469) and skips categoricals with the contradictory comment 'categorical variables already have stochastic sampling' (:488) — no draw ever happens. imputeCellMCD has the same which.max (R/imputeCellEM.R:1386-1388; fallback mode imputation at :1373) and its final-uncertainty loop iterates only seq_len(p_cont) continuous columns (:1431-1473). imputeCellMM likewise (R/imputeCellMM.R:147-149; uncertainty block skips non-continuous via 'if (!is_continuous[j]) next' at :192). In contrast imputeCellEM samples from predicted probabilities (R/imputeCellEM.R:500-504) and imputeCellM does too for categorical responses (R/imputeCellwise.R:750-754). The claim is actually stronger than stated: (1) the user-facing roxygen for imputeCellIRMI documents 'If j is categorical: ... impute by sampling from predicted probabilities' (R/imputeCellwise.R:32-34), so documented behavior contradicts the implementation, not just internal comments; (2) imputeCellMCD offers MI via m>1 whose non-bootstrap mechanism is documented as 'Repeated runs with different seeds ... provide parameter + imputation uncertainty' (R/imputeCellEM.R:1014-1016), yet imputeCellMCD(d, m=3) returned three bit-identical categorical imputations — zero between-imputation variance for categorical cells, invalidating Rubin-style pooling for those cells. Mode over-representation also reproduced: observed class shares (a,b,c)=(0.25,0.40,0.35) vs cellIRMI-imputed (0.02,0.48,0.50) — the minority class nearly vanishes.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim1_repro.R — n=150 mixed data (3 continuous + 1 three-level factor), 50 missing factor cells, each method run under set.seed(1) vs set.seed(2). Output: cellIRMI identical=TRUE (0/50 differ), cellMCD identical=TRUE (0/50), cellMM identical=TRUE (0/50), cellEM identical=FALSE (20/50 differ), cellM identical=FALSE (21/50 differ). Distribution: observed g = (a .25, b .40, c .35) vs cellIRMI-imputed g = (a .02, b .48, c .50). MI: imputeCellMCD(d, m=3) -> all three imputed_list factor vectors identical (m1==m2 TRUE, m2==m3 TRUE).

### P2.17 [cellwise] imputeCellEM stopping rule: undocumented rolling-average criterion 10x looser than eps_em is the rule that actually fires; converged=TRUE reported when the documented criterion is never met
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellEM.R*

Docs (R/imputeCellEM.R:12-13, 74-79) state convergence = relative parameter change (mu, Sigma) below eps_em. The implementation (:672-677) additionally declares convergence when the mean change over the last 4 iterations is below eps_em*10 — an effective tolerance 10x looser on an averaged criterion, mentioned only in a code comment. Empirically this secondary rule is what stops the algorithm even on clean data: with eps_em=5e-3 the run converged after 5 iterations with per-iteration changes 0.038/0.029/0.024/0.027 (all 5-8x above eps_em), avg 0.0296 < 0.05. The stability-based stopping concept is by design (non-monotone composite pseudo-likelihood — correctly documented at :86-97, and the tinytest at inst/tinytest/test_cellwise.R:16 correctly asserts finiteness, not monotonicity); the issue is purely that users tuning eps_em get a different, looser criterion than documented while converged=TRUE suggests the documented tolerance was reached. Fix: document the oscillation-averaged rule in @details/@param eps_em (or expose the window and multiplier as arguments), and consider reporting which criterion fired.

**Evidence:** Trace run (seed 903, 80x3, eps_em=5e-3): parameter changes 0.0383, 0.0292, 0.0242, 0.0268; converged=TRUE at iteration 5; last change < eps_em is FALSE. Code: avg_change < eps_em * 10 branch at R/imputeCellEM.R:674-677.

### P2.18 [cellwise] imputeCellM silently ignores formula transformations (and rejects 'y ~ .') for continuous responses
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellwise.R*

imputeCellM parses the formula only via all.vars() (R/imputeCellwise.R:607-608) and builds the design from raw data columns with .build_design_matrix (:667), so any transformation in the formula — log(x), poly(x,2), I(x^2), interactions — is silently dropped for continuous responses: y ~ log(x) is fitted as y ~ x with no warning. The categorical-response path passes the formula directly to nnet::multinom (:719) which DOES honor transforms, so the two paths interpret the same formula differently. 'y ~ .' fails with the misleading error 'Not all predictor variables found in data.' since '.' is treated as a variable name (:612-613). For a formula-based API this violates the core contract. Fix: construct the design via model.matrix(formula, data) (then map cell weights per term to parent variables, as .expand_cell_weights already does for factors), or detect non-trivial terms/'.' and error informatively.

**Evidence:** Repro: y = 5*log(x)+e; imputeCellM(y ~ log(x)) imputation RMSE 1.742 vs lm(y ~ log(x)) reference 0.237 (7x worse, no warning emitted).

**Verifier:** Verified in code and reproduced. imputeCellM parses the formula solely via all.vars() (R/imputeCellwise.R:607-608: y_var <- all.vars(formula)[1]; x_vars <- all.vars(formula)[-1]) and, for continuous responses, builds the design from raw data columns with .build_design_matrix(data_work, pred_cols) (:667) — so log(x), poly(x,2), I(x^2), and interactions all collapse to the raw variables with no warning (all.vars(y ~ poly(x,2)+I(x^2)+x:z) returns just y,x,z). Empirical proof of silent dropping: under the same seed, imputeCellM(y ~ log(x)+z) and imputeCellM(y ~ x+z) return bit-identical imputations and zero warnings. Accuracy impact reproduced: y=5*log(x)+e, 60 missing of n=200 -> imputation RMSE vs truth 1.547 for imputeCellM(y~log(x)+z) vs 0.251 for lm(y~log(x)+z) predictions (~6x worse; claim's 7x on their data, same order). 'y ~ .' fails with the misleading 'Not all predictor variables found in data.' because '.' is treated as a variable name (:612-613). The path asymmetry is also real: the categorical-response branch passes the formula directly to nnet::multinom (:717-721), which does evaluate transforms — same-seed A/B with g ~ log(x)+z vs g ~ x+z gave different imputations (6/50 differ). Incidental extra defect surfaced during repro: in that categorical branch, multinom evaluates weights=w_row in the user formula's environment, where w_row does not exist, so every user call warns 'Multinomial model failed ... Objekt w_row nicht gefunden - using unweighted model' and the 'cell-weighted' multinomial silently runs unweighted (the internally-constructed formulas in cellIRMI/cellMCD/cellMM don't hit this because as.formula() captures the function frame).

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim2_repro.R — Output: warnings emitted by imputeCellM(y ~ log(x)+z): NONE; imputations identical for 'y ~ log(x)+z' vs 'y ~ x+z' (same seed): TRUE; RMSE vs truth: imputeCellM = 1.547 vs lm(y~log(x)+z) = 0.251; imputeCellM(y ~ ., data) errors with 'Not all predictor variables found in data.'; categorical response g ~ log(x)+z vs g ~ x+z (same seed): NOT identical (6/50 differ), each run additionally warning 'Multinomial model failed: Objekt w_row nicht gefunden - using unweighted model'.

### P2.19 [cellwise] No tests for imputeCellMCD/imputeCellMM/imputeCellReg/cellWeightsMCD/dispatcher; existing tests use centered N(0,1) data with Huber weights, masking the P0 engine defect
*kind: test-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: inst/tinytest/test_cellwise.R*

inst/tinytest/test_cellwise.R (357 lines) covers cellWeights, cellIRWLS, imputeCellIRMI, imputeCellM and imputeCellEM only — imputeCellMCD (incl. m>1/boot paths), imputeCellMM, imputeCellReg (all three engines), cellWeightsMCD, cellWeightsFromResiduals and the imputeCellwise() dispatcher have zero coverage, which is how the boot no-op, the negative-weight update, and the dispatcher gaps went unnoticed. Moreover every accuracy-flavored test uses centered standard-normal predictors and method='huber' (e.g. :70-96, :186-206) — the unique regime where the multiplicative cell-weight defect is smallest (Huber weight is exactly 1 for |u|<=1.345 and 0 is the shrink target for centered data) — and the single quantitative bound is mse < 5 on data whose median-imputation MSE is ~5. Add: (1) a clean-data efficiency benchmark asserting imputation RMSE within ~1.5x of lm on UNcentered correlated Gaussian data with Tukey defaults; (2) a contamination benchmark asserting the cellwise method beats irmi(robust=TRUE); (3) structure/no-NA/guard tests for MCD/MM/Reg incl. skip-if-not-installed for cellWise/crmReg; (4) dispatcher round-trip tests for all six method names; (5) a seed-sensitivity test for categorical imputations once finding on deterministic mode imputation is resolved.

**Evidence:** ls inst/tinytest: only test_cellwise.R matches cell*; grep shows no imputeCellMCD/imputeCellMM/imputeCellReg/imputeCellwise/cellWeightsMCD calls in it. Accuracy test 9 threshold 'mse < 5' vs measured clean-data cellIRMI RMSE ~3.4 (MSE ~11.6) in the uncentered variant.

### P2.20 [classic-integration] Method gap: kNN() not callable through vimpute()
*kind: method-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

supported_methods (R/helper_vimpute.R:997) contains no donor-based method, yet vimpute's own docs borrow kNN semantics for makeNA/donorcond ('similar to kNN()', R/vimpute.R:63-71). kNN is VIM's flagship (JSS 2016) and its Gower-distance mixed-type matching is exactly what mice lacks, so its absence undercuts the 'per-variable method choice' pitch: users cannot mix e.g. list(income="robust", region="knn"). Proposal: a special-cased branch (donor methods do not fit the mlr3 fit/predict learner paradigm; wrapping as an mlr3 learner would need the whole training data at predict time), i.e. method="knn" dispatching per target variable to kNN(data, variable=var, dist_var=feature_cols, k=..., numFun=..., weights=...) with k/numFun/catFun/weights taken from learner_params$knn; skip tuning/boot/uncert for it (donor draw already carries uncertainty, so it composes naturally with m>1). This reuses the existing C++ gowerD backend at zero methodological risk.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:996-997 'Methods supported by vimpute()': c("ranger","regularized","xgboost","robust","gam","robgam"); grep of vimpute.R/helper_vimpute.R shows kNN referenced only in makeNA/donorcond doc text.

### P2.21 [classic-integration] Method gap: hotdeck() not callable through vimpute()
*kind: method-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/hotdeck.R*

Sequential/random hot-deck within domains (R/hotdeck.R) is unreachable from vimpute(); mice offers method="sample" so VIM currently cannot match even that baseline inside its unified API, despite owning a much better donor implementation (ord_var sorting, domain_var strata, donorcond). Proposal: special-cased branch method="hotdeck" that calls hotdeck(data, variable=var, ord_var=learner_params$hotdeck$ord_var, domain_var=..., donorcond=donorcond[[var]]) per target; document that pmm/boot/uncert/tune are not applicable for it and validate accordingly. Together with a knn branch this would let vimpute claim full coverage of VIM's classic donor methods, a clear differentiator vs mice for official-statistics users.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:997 has no donor method; hotdeck() has no vimpute pathway (grep 'hotdeck' in vimpute.R/helper_vimpute.R: zero hits).

### P2.22 [classic-integration] irmi deprecation creates a methods regression: vimpute has no count/Poisson, semi-continuous, or ordinal (polr) targets
*kind: method-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/irmi.R*

irmi() now warns unconditionally 'use vimpute()' (R/irmi.R:122-125), but three irmi capabilities have no vimpute equivalent: (1) count targets via glm/glmrob poisson (irmi.R:863-870 useGLMcount); (2) semi-continuous 'mixed' variables via the two-step binary-then-continuous model incl. mixed.constant (irmi.R:711-745 useLM); (3) ordered targets via MASS::polr (irmi.R:926) - vimpute coerces ordered to unordered factor before fitting (vimpute.R:816-819) and has no ordinal learner. mice ships polr (method 'polr') and handles counts via pmm, so deprecating irmi before closing these gaps weakens the 'beats mice on METHODS' claim for exactly the data types IRMI was published for (CSDA 2011). Proposal: add method="poisson" (mlr3 regr.glm/family=poisson or a thin custom learner like the existing gam_imp/robgam_imp R6 learners in helper_vimpute.R:2521ff), an ordinal learner (polr-based classif learner), and a two-step mixed pipeline; until then soften the irmi deprecation note for count/mixed/ordered data.

**Evidence:** irmi.R:369-381 supports types numeric/mixed/binary/nominal/count/ordered; supported_methods in helper_vimpute.R:997 covers only regression/classification learners; verified vimpute output returns ordered input as plain factor (is.ordered FALSE).

### P2.23 [classic-integration] Ordered-factor handling inconsistent: vimpute strips the ordered class from ALL considered columns, classics preserve it
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Cross-function check of ordered-factor behaviour: kNN keeps ordered targets ordered and uses ordinal Gower distance + ordFun=medianSamp (R/kNN.R:99-122,440); hotdeck preserves classes (donor values); irmi models them with polr and restores original levels (irmi.R:577-592). vimpute() converts every ordered column to factor(as.character(x)) for modeling (vimpute.R:816-819, 1624-1631; helper_vimpute.R:1203-1205) and never restores the ordered class: verified that both an imputed ordered target AND an ordered predictor that was never imputed come back with is.ordered()==FALSE (level order happens to survive via factor_levels bookkeeping at vimpute.R:273-277, but the class attribute is lost). Silent metadata corruption of untouched columns breaks downstream code (contrasts, comparisons, plotting) and is a usability regression vs both the classic functions and mice (which returns ordered columns intact). Fix: record is.ordered per column alongside factor_levels and re-apply factor(..., ordered=TRUE, levels=orig) on return.

**Evidence:** Verified on build: vimpute(data.frame(x, y, o=ordered levels low<mid<high)) returns o as unordered factor; same for an ordered column used only as predictor. Conversion sites vimpute.R:816-819 and helper_vimpute.R:1203-1205 have no ordered restoration counterpart.

**Verifier:** Reproduced on the pre-installed build with n=60, o = ordered(low<mid<high). Test A (o has NAs, is imputed): vimpute(dA, sequential=FALSE, nseq=1) returns o with is.ordered()==FALSE, class 'factor'. Test B (o complete, only numeric y imputed — o is purely a predictor): input is.ordered(dB$o)==TRUE, output is.ordered(outB$o)==FALSE. Level ORDER survives in both (levels low mid high, restored via the factor_levels bookkeeping saved at vimpute.R:271-279 before conversion), but the ordered class attribute is silently dropped — exactly as claimed, including the metadata corruption of never-imputed columns. Conversion sites verified: vimpute.R:816-819 and :1624-1631 (factor(as.character(x)) on data_temp/data_y_fill_final), helper_vimpute.R:1203-1205 (precheck converts by reference on the data.table, which is why untouched predictors are affected), plus helper_vimpute.R:329-331; grep over both files finds no site that re-applies ordered=TRUE. Baselines all preserve the class on the same data: kNN TRUE (default ordFun=medianSamp at kNN.R:122, ordered aggregation at :440), hotdeck TRUE, irmi TRUE (level restoration at irmi.R:577-592), and mice::complete(mice(dA, m=1)) TRUE. vimpute is the sole outlier. The proposed fix (record is.ordered per column alongside factor_levels and re-apply on return) is coherent with the existing factor_levels mechanism.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim2_ordered.R — output: 'A (o imputed): is.ordered(out$o): FALSE ... levels: low mid high'; 'B (o untouched): input is.ordered: TRUE | output is.ordered: FALSE'; kNN/hotdeck/irmi/mice all report is.ordered TRUE.

### P2.24 [classic-integration] kNN(): dead is.integer branch makes integer imputations truncate (floor) with a scary data.table warning
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/kNN.R*

R/kNN.R:432 and :441 test is.integer(data[,variable[j]]) on a data.table; in data.table j-evaluation variable[j] resolves to the character column NAME from the calling scope, not the column, so is.integer() is always FALSE and the round() branch (:442) is dead code. Imputed aggregates then hit `[<-.data.table` integer coercion: verified kNN(df, variable="a", k=4) on integer a with median 4.5 emits 'truncated (precision lost) when assigning to type integer' and stores the truncated value. Consequences: downward-biased integer imputations (truncation instead of rounding, e.g. 4.7 -> 4) plus an alarming warning on every affected call. One-character-class fix: use data[[variable[j]]] in both tests (:432,:441). Same idiom should be audited at :429-435 weightDist branch.

**Evidence:** Verified: kNN(data.frame(a=c(1L,2L,7L,8L,NA), b=c(1.1,2.2,7.7,8.8,5)), variable="a", k=4, dist_var="b") warns '4.500000 (type double) ... truncated (precision lost) ... column 1 named a' and imputes 4.

**Verifier:** Fully reproduced (data.table 1.18.2.1). (1) Exact claimed repro: kNN(data.frame(a=c(1L,2L,7L,8L,NA), b=c(1.1,2.2,7.7,8.8,5)), variable="a", k=4, dist_var="b") warns "4.500000 (type 'double') at RHS position 1 out-of-range(NA) or truncated (precision lost) when assigning to type 'integer' (column 1 named 'a')" and stores 4. (2) Dead-branch mechanism proven in isolation: with dt a data.table and variable=c("a","b") in the calling scope, dt[, variable[j]] returns the character string "a" (data.table j-evaluation resolves 'variable' from the calling frame, not as a column), so is.integer(data[,variable[j]]) at R/kNN.R:432 and :441 is always FALSE and the round() branches at :433/:442 are unreachable; is.integer(dt[[variable[j]]]) correctly returns TRUE, confirming the one-character-class fix. (3) Genuine value-level bias demonstrated: with donors 2,5,6,9 (median 5.5) kNN imputes 5 via data.table truncation, while the intended round(5.5) = 6 — so truncation systematically biases downward relative to the intended branch. One precision note on the claim's own example: round(4.5) is also 4 in R (round-half-to-even), so in that specific example the imputed VALUE coincides with truncation and only the warning differs; the 5.5 case is needed to expose the numeric divergence, and any non-half fractional aggregate (e.g. numFun=mean giving 4.75) diverges too. The weightDist branch at :432 uses the identical idiom and is equally dead by the same argument. Core claim (dead branch, truncation, warning, downward bias, proposed fix) is correct.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/claim3_knn.R — shows the truncation warning and imputed 4 for the claimed example; imputed 5 (vs round(5.5)=6) for donors 2,5,6,9; and class(dt[,variable[j]])=='character' proving the is.integer test is always FALSE.

**Evidence:** inst/tinytest/test_vimmi.R:86-100 (single m>1 test, all options at once); grep 'as.mids' over inst/tinytest/ returns nothing; R/vimmi.R:264-277; both proposed tests executed successfully against the pre-installed build (identical seeded completes; mids + mipo produced)

### P2.29 [api-consistency] imputeCellIRMI documents option values that error: weight_update="univariate" and init_weights="marginal" are rejected by match.arg; accepted values "per-variable" and "ddc" are undocumented
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellwise.R*

The roxygen block documents weight_update as '"multivariate" (default) ... or "univariate"' and init_weights as '"mcd" (default) ... or "marginal"' (R/imputeCellwise.R:60-68), but the code validates match.arg(weight_update, c("multivariate", "per-variable")) and match.arg(init_weights, c("mcd", "univariate", "ddc")) (R/imputeCellwise.R:129-130). Both documented values error on the installed build; the DDC initialisation — a genuinely attractive feature — is invisible to users. Additionally `uncert` is documented as pmm/normalerror/resid but the code also accepts "none" (:128 vs :57-59). Fix: align docs to code, and standardise the vocabulary across the family — I suggest "per-variable" -> "univariate" in code (matching the docs and the init_weights wording) with the old string kept as a silent alias for one release.

**Evidence:** Docs R/imputeCellwise.R:60-68 vs match.arg calls :127-130. Reproduced: imputeCellIRMI(d, weight_update="univariate") errors ''arg' sollte eines von "multivariate", "per-variable" sein'; imputeCellIRMI(d, init_weights="marginal") errors ''arg' sollte eines von "mcd", "univariate", "ddc" sein'.

**Verifier:** Reproduced on the pre-installed build of the working tree. The roxygen docs in /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellwise.R document weight_update as "multivariate"/"univariate" (lines 60-64) and init_weights as "mcd"/"marginal" (lines 65-68), but the validation code accepts different sets: line 129 `weight_update <- match.arg(weight_update, c("multivariate", "per-variable"))` and line 130 `init_weights <- match.arg(init_weights, c("mcd", "univariate", "ddc"))`. Both documented values error at runtime; both accepted alternatives ("per-variable", init_weights="univariate") run fine, as does the completely undocumented "ddc" initialisation (a real feature: cellWise::DDC-based cell-weight initialisation at lines 206-229, with MCD fallback). Additionally, uncert docs (lines 57-59) list only pmm/normalerror/resid while line 128 also accepts "none" (verified working; it skips the final uncertainty step at line 465). The rendered help users actually see carries the wrong values: man/imputeCellIRMI.Rd lines 51 and 56 contain "univariate" and "marginal", and the installed Rd help contains no occurrence of "per-variable", "ddc", or "none". The claim's severity assessment is fair: every documented non-default value for these two arguments errors, and the DDC feature is invisible. The suggested fix direction (align docs to code, prefer renaming code's "per-variable" to "univariate" to unify vocabulary with init_weights, keeping the old string as an alias) is reasonable but note one wrinkle: after such a rename, weight_update="univariate" and init_weights="univariate" would be distinct concepts sharing one name, so the docs must clearly distinguish them.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); set.seed(1); d <- data.frame(x=rnorm(60), y=rnorm(60), z=rnorm(60)); d$x[c(3,10,20)] <- NA; d$y[c(5,15)] <- NA; imputeCellIRMI(d, weight_update="univariate")' -> Error: 'arg' sollte eines von "multivariate", "per-variable" sein. Same with init_weights="marginal" -> Error: 'arg' sollte eines von "mcd", "univariate", "ddc" sein. Undocumented values weight_update="per-variable", init_weights="univariate", init_weights="ddc", uncert="none" all return successfully. Installed help check: tools::Rd_db("VIM") imputeCellIRMI.Rd contains "univariate" and "marginal" but not "per-variable", "ddc", or "none".

### P2.30 [api-consistency] Return-type conventions fragmented: vimpute always returns data.table (even for data.frame input) while kNN/hotdeck preserve input class; cellwise returns unclassed lists; value_back defaults differ between siblings
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

kNN/hotdeck return the input's class (df in -> df out, dt in -> dt out; verified). vimpute coerces immediately via as.data.table (R/vimpute.R:193-194) and returns a data.table for m=1 regardless of input, so `out[, 1]`, `out$col <- NULL`, drop semantics and reference semantics all change silently for data.frame users migrating from kNN to the recommended vimpute. The cellwise family returns bare lists (data_imputed + cellweights + ...), imputeRobust returns a data.frame, imputeCellM returns list-or-vector depending on value_back, and the sibling pair imputeRobust/imputeRobustChain default value_back to "all" vs "matrix" respectively (R/imputeRobust.R:46, R/imputeRobustChain.R:44), so the chain variant returns a different shape by default. Harmonisation: (1) vimpute should record the input class and return the same class (one as.data.frame() at the exit; document data.table as internal engine); (2) standardise value_back defaults to "all" everywhere; (3) give cellwise results a class (next finding). This is the single most visible inconsistency for users following the 'irmi is deprecated, use vimpute' migration path.

**Evidence:** R/vimpute.R:193-194 (`data <- as.data.table(data)[...]`); empirical: class(vimpute(data.frame(...))) == data.table/data.frame while class(kNN(data.frame(...))) == data.frame and class(kNN(as.data.table(...))) == data.table/data.frame. imputeRobust formals value_back="all" vs imputeRobustChain value_back="matrix".

### P2.31 [api-consistency] No S3 class or print/summary/plot methods for cellwise-imputation results; vimmi lacks a plot method — the diagnostics pillar has no API surface
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellwise.R*

imputeCellEM/MCD/IRMI/MM/Reg return plain lists (e.g. R/imputeCellwise.R:493-498), so printing floods the console with the full imputed data plus an n-by-p weight matrix, and there is no plot()/summary() showing which cells were downweighted/imputed — even though cellweights is precisely the diagnostic that differentiates VIM from mice. NAMESPACE registers S3 methods only for aggr (print/summary/plot) and vimmi (print/summary/with/complete — no plot). Harmonisation: introduce class "cellImp" (fields data_imputed, cellweights, converged, iterations, call, method) returned by all six cellwise functions; add print.cellImp (one-line: method, n cells imputed, n cells downweighted, converged), summary.cellImp (per-variable table), plot.cellImp (matrixplot-style heatmap of cellweights with imputed cells marked — the package already owns matrixplot()), and extract via complete()/as.data.frame() so downstream code doesn't index $data_imputed. Add plot.vimmi (between-imputation variability, e.g. strip/density per imputed variable) to complete the vimmi class. Backwards-compatible: a classed list keeps $-access working, so no deprecation cycle needed.

**Evidence:** R/imputeCellwise.R:493-498 (bare `list(data_imputed=..., cellweights=..., ...)` return); NAMESPACE S3method lines: only aggr (plot/print/summary), summary.aggr print, and vimmi (print/summary/with/complete) — no class for cellwise returns, no plot.vimmi.

### P2.32 [api-consistency] `method` means five different things across the imputation API; robust switches are scattered across robust=/robMethod=/method=
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeRobust.R*

Across exports, `method` selects: the regression estimator (imputeRobust method="MM", imputeRobustChain method="lts"), the M-weight function (imputeCell* method="tukey"/"huber"), the algorithm (imputeCellwise method="cellIRMI"), the per-variable learner (vimpute method=list(var="ranger")), the PCA flavour (impPCA method="classical"), and the initialisation method (initialise method="kNN"). Meanwhile robustness is toggled by robust=TRUE + robMethod="lmrob" in irmi, robust=TRUE in regressionImp, and implicitly by method= in imputeRobust(Chain). Shared numeric-control vocabulary also collides: eps defaults are 5 (irmi), 0.5 (impPCA, imputeRobustChain), 0.005 (vimpute, all imputeCell*) — same name, different scales/semantics. Harmonisation proposal: reserve `method` for 'which imputation model/learner' (vimpute semantics); rename weight-function args to `weight_fun` (imputeCell*) and estimator args to `estimator` (imputeRobust/Chain); keep old names as deprecated aliases for two minor releases (accept, warn once per session via a small deprecate_arg() helper that maps old->new, then remove in 8.0); document eps per-function with an explicit scale statement, and consider `tol` for the cellwise/vimpute relative-change criterion to break the false equivalence with irmi's eps=5.

**Evidence:** Formals from installed build: imputeRobust(method="MM"), imputeRobustChain(method="lts"), imputeCellIRMI/M/MCD(method="tukey"), imputeCellwise(method=c("cellIRMI","cellM","cellEM")), vimpute(method=setNames(list("ranger"...))), impPCA(method="classical"), initialise(method="kNN"); irmi(robust=FALSE, robMethod="lmrob"); eps defaults 5 / 0.5 / 0.005 across irmi, impPCA+chain, cellwise+vimpute.

### P2.33 [api-consistency] uncert vocabulary fragmented into five value sets with three different defaults; imputeRobust performs no validation and fails with 'object ymiss not found' on typos, plus an undocumented "wresid" option
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeRobust.R*

match.arg sets on the installed build: imputeCellMM/imputeCellReg c(pmm, normalerror, none); imputeCellIRMI c(pmm, normalerror, resid, none); imputeCellM c(pmm, normalerror, resid) — no none; vimpute c(none, normalerror, resid, pmm, midastouch); imputeCellEM/imputeCellMCD c(conditional, pmm). Defaults are "none" (vimpute), "pmm" (robust + most cellwise), "conditional" (EM/MCD) — so the recommended front door vimpute() does deterministic imputation by default while every robust/cellwise sibling adds stochastic uncertainty by default, a statistically consequential inconsistency that users won't notice. imputeRobust never validates uncert: a typo like uncert="pnm" crashes later with 'Objekt ymiss nicht gefunden' (reproduced), and a functional "wresid" branch exists at R/imputeRobust.R:213 but is absent from the docs. Harmonisation: one internal validate_uncert(x, allowed) helper used everywhere (clear error listing the per-method choices); document the union vocabulary in a single ?imputationUncertainty topic cross-linked from all @param uncert entries; treat "conditional" as EM-specific but stated in the shared vocabulary; align defaults (either all "pmm"-style stochastic or all "none") — given the MI ambitions, defaulting vimpute's uncert to "pmm" when m>1 (currently the user can produce m identical or improper imputations) deserves explicit consideration.

**Evidence:** grep match.arg(uncert: imputeCellMM.R:34, imputeCellwise.R:128+594, helper_vimpute.R:960, imputeCellEM.R:169+1037, imputeCellReg.R:66; imputeRobust.R has only if(uncert==...) chains at :205-239 incl. undocumented "wresid" at :213. Reproduced: imputeRobust(x~y+z, d, uncert="pnm") errors 'Objekt ymiss nicht gefunden'.

### P2.34 [api-consistency] Formula argument chaos: formula / form / formulas / modelFormulas across siblings, and vimpute reuses the name `formula` for a logical flag
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

The model-formula argument is `formula` in rangerImpute/xgboostImpute/regressionImp/imputeCellM, `form` in imputeRobust (R/imputeRobust.R:37), `formulas` (a list, with a default that lazily references the later `data` arg) in imputeRobustChain (R/imputeRobustChain.R:42), and `modelFormulas` in irmi. Worst: vimpute has `formula = FALSE` — a LOGICAL controlling whether per-variable formulas in `method` are interpreted — so the same argument name switches type and meaning exactly at the function users are migrating to. Formula-first signatures also break data-first piping: d |> kNN() works but d |> regressionImp(x~y) does not without naming. Harmonisation: standardise on `formula` for the model spec in all formula-based functions (imputeRobust: add formula=, keep form= as deprecated alias via missing()-based shim for 2 releases); in vimpute rename the logical to `use_formulas` (or fold it away by auto-detecting formula objects inside `method`/`learner_params`, which is the cleaner mlr3-era design), deprecating `formula` with a one-session warning; for new-era functions prefer data-first with formula second (regressionImp/rangerImpute cannot swap positionally without breakage, so only document named usage and apply data-first to future functions).

**Evidence:** Formals: imputeRobust(form, data, ...), imputeRobustChain(formulas = vector("list", ncol(data)), data, ...), irmi(..., modelFormulas = NULL), rangerImpute/xgboostImpute/regressionImp/imputeCellM(formula, data, ...), vimpute(..., formula = FALSE) where `formula` is logical (R/vimpute.R formals + docs).

### P2.35 [api-consistency] imputeRobustChain ships with placeholder roxygen (FUNCTION_DESCRIPTION / PARAM_DESCRIPTION / OUTPUT_DESCRIPTION), a typo argument `familiy`, and a robustboot type inconsistent with its siblings
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeRobustChain.R*

The entire roxygen block of the exported imputeRobustChain is unfilled scaffolding: @description FUNCTION_DESCRIPTION, 14x @param ... PARAM_DESCRIPTION, @return OUTPUT_DESCRIPTION (R/imputeRobustChain.R:2-17) — this renders verbatim in the shipped Rd/pkgdown page. Its formal `familiy = "Gaussian"` (:43) is a typo of `family`; sibling imputeRobust spells it `family` (documented 'Not supported and ignored'), and since "family" is not a prefix of "familiy", users typing the correct spelling get 'unused argument (family=...)'. robustboot is logical TRUE here but a string ("stratified"/"standard"/"residual") in imputeRobust and vimpute, so the same concept has different types across the three bootstrap-capable functions. Fix: write the docs (the details exist in imputeRobust's block to crib from); rename familiy->family keeping familiy as a deprecated alias for one release (if (!missing(familiy)) { warn; family <- familiy }); make robustboot a string with the vimpute vocabulary, mapping TRUE->"stratified"/FALSE->"standard" with a deprecation message.

**Evidence:** R/imputeRobustChain.R:2-17 (all placeholders incl. '@param familiy PARAM_DESCRIPTION'), :42-44 (formals familiy="Gaussian", robustboot=TRUE logical, value_back="matrix"); imputeRobust.R:8+45 (robustboot="stratified" string), :15 (family 'Not supported and ignored').

### P2.36 [api-consistency] imputeCellwise() dispatcher advertises "cellM" but unconditionally stop()s on it, and omits cellMCD/cellMM/cellReg from the family it claims to dispatch
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellwise.R*

imputeCellwise(data, method = c("cellIRMI", "cellM", "cellEM"), ...) lists cellM as a first-class choice in its signature, docs and match.arg, yet the switch branch is `cellM = stop("cellM requires a formula; use imputeCellM() directly")` (R/imputeCellwise.R:998) — a guaranteed error masquerading as an option (reproduced). The dispatcher also covers only 3 of the 6 cellwise methods; imputeCellMCD, imputeCellMM and imputeCellReg (all data-first, so trivially dispatchable) are missing, although project docs describe imputeCellwise() as 'dispatcher over the cellwise family'. Harmonisation: drop "cellM" from the choices (its formula-based single-response design doesn't fit a whole-data dispatcher) and add "cellMCD", "cellMM", "cellReg"; optionally accept method names without the redundant "cell" prefix ("irmi","em","mcd",...) since the function is already called imputeCellwise. Combined with the cellImp class (separate finding) this makes the dispatcher the natural single entry point for the 7.1.0 flagship family.

**Evidence:** R/imputeCellwise.R:994-1001: method = c("cellIRMI","cellM","cellEM"); switch(..., cellM = stop("cellM requires a formula; use imputeCellM() directly")). Reproduced: imputeCellwise(d, method="cellM") errors. cellMCD/cellMM/cellReg absent from choices despite data-first signatures.

### P2.37 [deps-arch] R/zzz.R globalVariables() is used as an R CMD check silencer: 11 of 13 declared symbols correspond to genuinely undefined functions/variables in imputeRobust(Chain)
*kind: refactor | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/zzz.R*

R/zzz.R:7-10 declares c('alpha','factors','ndata','pivotCoord','rn','robGAM','robust','supportedMethods','useGLMpoisson','useLogistic','x_reg','r','p'). These are not data.table NSE column names: pivotCoord, useLogistic, useGLMpoisson and robGAM are calls to functions that do not exist in the package (R/imputeRobustChain.R:126,236-237; R/imputeRobust.R:182); x_reg, ndata, robust, alpha, factors are undefined variables in the scopes that reference them (imputeRobustChain.R:236-237 and the 'lm' branch that errors on `alpha`). Declaring them in globalVariables converted what would have been loud 'no visible global function definition / no visible binding' NOTEs -- which would have flagged the P0/P1 bugs above before release -- into silence. Recommended hygiene rule for this package: globalVariables may only contain data.table/NSE column names; undefined-symbol NOTEs must be fixed in code. Concretely: purge the whole list, run R CMD check, fix each reappearing NOTE at its source (the codebase already has the better per-site idiom, e.g. `RandomVariableForImputationWithHotdeck <- NULL # Init for CRAN check` in R/hotdeck.R:126). Note data.table copy discipline itself is fine: vimpute copies via as.data.table(data)[, considered_variables, with=FALSE] before set() (R/vimpute.R:194,257 -- verified empirically that a user's data.table is not mutated by makeNA), hotdeck copies via data.table(data) (R/hotdeck.R:103), matchImpute explicitly handles the as.data.table-no-copy gotcha (R/matchImpute.R:57-61).

**Evidence:** R/zzz.R:7-10 vs. reproduced errors: 'konnte Funktion pivotCoord nicht finden', 'konnte Funktion robGAM nicht finden', 'Objekt alpha nicht gefunden' -- each masked symbol is in the globalVariables vector; grep shows useLogistic/useGLMpoisson/robGAM/pivotCoord have no definition anywhere under R/.

### P2.38 [deps-arch] Suggests guarding gaps: reactable (tableMiss), stringr (imputeRobust helpers), lgr (vimpute), plus dead enetLTS/robmixglm code
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/tableMiss.R*

Guarding is mostly correct (cellWise: imputeCellEM.R:1160 and imputeCellwise.R:207 guarded with fallbacks; crmReg: imputeCellReg.R guarded; mice: vimmi.R guarded; mgcv: 5 of 6 sites guarded; pdist: guarded where reachable). Gaps: (1) R/tableMiss.R:32-34 calls reactable::reactable/colDef unguarded -- the exported tableMiss() fails with a raw 'there is no package called reactable' instead of an informative message; (2) R/imputeRobust.R:269,279 use stringr::str_extract unguarded in getOrigName()/getTransformation() (also reached from imputeRobustChain) -- and the pattern '(?<=\\().*(?=\\))' is a one-liner in base R (regmatches/sub with perl=TRUE), so the stringr Suggest can be deleted outright; (3) R/vimpute.R:184 calls lgr::get_logger unguarded on the default verbose=FALSE path -- de facto safe because mlr3 (Imports) hard-depends on lgr, but per CRAN policy Suggests must be used conditionally; either guard it or move lgr to Imports with a comment; (4) R/imputeRobustChain.R:283-288: the enetLTS:: and robmixglm:: calls sit after stop('... not implemented yet') -- unreachable code; remove the calls and drop both packages from Suggests until implemented (enetLTS in particular has a heavy dependency tree of its own for test installs).

**Evidence:** Guard audit: grep counts uses vs requireNamespace guards -- reactable 2/0 (R/tableMiss.R:32,34), stringr 2/0 (R/imputeRobust.R:269,279), lgr 1/0 (R/vimpute.R:184), enetLTS 1/0 + robmixglm 1/0 behind stop() (R/imputeRobustChain.R:283-288); cellWise/crmReg/mice/pdist/mgcv guarded at cited sites.

### P2.41 [mice] where matrix: arbitrary imputation targets including overimputation of observed cells
*kind: method-gap (vs mice where argument + make.where) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Absent. vimpute imputes exactly the is.na cells (plus makeNA-matched values); no cell-level control.

PROPOSAL: Accept where logical matrix unioned into the internal NA mask (the makeNA_match plumbing at vimpute.R:197-202 is already cell-level, so the mask infrastructure exists). Also unlocks overimputation diagnostics (impute observed cells, compare to truth) feeding the P0 diagnostics plots.

REFERENCE: vimpute.R:196-202

**Verifier:** No where argument in formals(vimpute); impute_mask is is.na(data[[var]]) or, for makeNA-listed variables, only the matched coded values (vimpute.R:263-268 — note for those variables existing NAs are then NOT imputed, per docs vimpute.R:65-67). No overimputation of observed cells is possible. The makeNA_match plumbing at vimpute.R:196-202 is indeed cell-level mask infrastructure, as the proposal notes.
