### P2.47 [competitors] Bounds / valid-range constraints on imputed values
*kind: method-gap (vs Amelia bounds matrix + max.resample (draws until inside bounds; verified locally); Hmisc::aregImpute constraint argument (verified locally, 5.2.5)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: donorcond only restricts the donor/training pool (R/vimpute.R:204-236); nothing constrains predictions — regression/xgboost/gam can impute negative values for nonnegative variables or >100% percentages whenever PMM is off (inject_uncertainty adds unbounded noise, R/helper_vimpute.R:1779-1793)

PROPOSAL: Add bounds = list(var = c(lo, hi)): redraw (for stochastic uncert methods, Amelia-style max.resample) or clamp point predictions after inject_uncertainty; document PMM as the always-in-range alternative. Cheap and prevents embarrassing impossible values in applied work.

REFERENCE: args(Amelia::amelia) verified locally (bounds, max.resample); aregImpute constraint verified locally

**Verifier:** grep 'bounds' over R/*.R returns nothing; no argument in any imputation function constrains the range of imputed values. donorcond only filters the donor/training pool (R/vimpute.R:204-236; training data restricted via data[donor_mask[[target_col]]] at :560) — predictions themselves are unconstrained. inject_uncertainty adds unbounded noise: preds + rnorm(n, 0, scale) for 'normalerror' and preds + sample(residuals) for 'resid' (R/helper_vimpute.R:1779-1793), with no clamping or redraw. Empirically demonstrated on the installed build: a strictly positive variable imputed with method='robust', uncert='normalerror' produced a negative imputation (min imputed -0.0666, 1 of 80 values negative). Related win #5 (uncert menu none/normalerror/resid/pmm/midastouch) spot-checked and accurate: match.arg at R/helper_vimpute.R:1774, and midastouch_donors (:1679-1739) genuinely combines Mahalanobis covariate distance with score distance and weights donor draws by inverse distance — not inflated.

**Repro:** set.seed(99); d <- data.frame(x1=rnorm(400)); d$pos <- pmax(0.05, 0.1+0.05*d$x1+rnorm(400,0,0.2)); d$pos[sample(400,80)] <- NA; r <- vimpute(d, method='robust', uncert='normalerror', sequential=FALSE, imp_var=FALSE); min(r$pos[is.na(d$pos)]) # -0.0666

### P2.48 [competitors] Grouped / by-domain model-based imputation
*kind: method-gap (vs simputation: formula grammar y ~ x1 + x2 | group fits separate models per group in every impute_* verb) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: hotdeck() has domain_var (R/hotdeck.R:79) but the model-based path has nothing: vimpute/kNN have no by/domain argument

PROPOSAL: Add by = <vars> to vimpute: split the task per domain with automatic fallback to the pooled model when a domain has too few donors. Natural fit for official statistics (VIM's statistikat home turf: imputation within strata/NUTS regions is standard practice).

REFERENCE: VERIFY: simputation grouping syntax from documented knowledge (package not installed locally); van der Loo, simputation CRAN vignette

**Verifier:** vimpute() has no by/domain/group argument (formals verified on installed build; grep 'domain' over R/vimpute.R and R/helper_vimpute.R returns nothing), and kNN() has none either (signature at R/kNN.R:116-122). hotdeck() has domain_var as claimed (signature at R/hotdeck.R:79-81). One nuance the claim misses: matchImpute(data, variable, match_var, ...) (R/matchImpute.R:54) imputes within categories defined by match_var — but it is donor-based (sequential hotdeck-style), so the statement that the model-based path has nothing remains accurate.

### P2.49 [competitors] Low-rank / factorial imputation (iterative PCA, MCA, FAMD; matrix completion)
*kind: method-gap (vs missMDA (imputePCA regularized iterative PCA, estim_ncpPCA CV for ncp, MIPCA for MI, imputeMCA/imputeFAMD for categorical/mixed); softImpute (nuclear-norm ALS matrix completion, scales via Incomplete class)) | verdict: REFUTED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: No PCA/low-rank method anywhere in VIM; per-variable regression learners degrade when p >> n or predictor blocks are collinear; only 'regularized' (glmnet) partially covers the wide-data case

PROPOSAL: Add method = 'pca' (regularized iterative PCA with CV-chosen ncp) as a seventh built-in or a standalone imputePCA-style function. Fills the one methodological hole in the 'broadest methods' claim: questionnaire blocks, spectra, wide omics-style data.

REFERENCE: VERIFY: missMDA function set from documented knowledge (not installed); Josse & Husson, missMDA, JSS 70(1) 2016

**Verifier:** The vim_status 'No PCA/low-rank method anywhere in VIM' is false. VIM exports impPCA() (NAMESPACE:33; R/impPCA.R:59): iterative EM-PCA imputation with classical or robust MCD covariance (method='mcd' via robustbase::covMcd, R/impPCA.R:118-124), rank-k reconstruction, and residual-bootstrap multiple imputation (boot=TRUE, m draws, :146-206), citing Serneels & Verdonck (2008, CSDA) — and it has its own vignette (vignettes/impPCA.Rmd). The competitor scan even missed it in the wins list. What genuinely remains missing vs missMDA/softImpute: numeric-only (stop at R/impPCA.R:75), k is user-chosen with default ncol(x)-1 and no CV selection of ncp, no regularization in the Josse sense, no MCA/FAMD for categorical/mixed data, not available as a vimpute() method, and no scalable nuclear-norm matrix completion. So the narrower proposal (CV-chosen ncp, categorical support, vimpute integration) still has merit, but the gap as stated is wrong.

### P2.50 [competitors] Benchmark + evaluation infrastructure to substantiate the 'beats mice' claim
*kind: method-gap (vs mlim (markets itself entirely on benchmark plots vs mice/missRanger/missForest); mixgb (paper benchmarks); mice::ampute, missRanger::generateNA, mixgb::createNA (MCAR/MAR/MNAR generators)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: evaluation() is rudimentary: err_num sums squared differences over whole columns divided by missing count, unnormalized across variable scales, no per-variable breakdown (R/evaluation.R:36-48); VIM has no MAR/MNAR amputation generator (makeNA declares coded missings, different purpose); no benchmark vignette exists

PROPOSAL: Ship (1) an ampute-style MCAR/MAR/MNAR generator, (2) upgraded evaluation: per-variable NRMSE/PFC plus MI estimand metrics (CI coverage, bias, distributional distance), and (3) a reproducible benchmark vignette vs mice, missRanger, missForest, mixgb. Without this, the strategic claim is unverifiable marketing.

REFERENCE: R/evaluation.R:36-48; missRanger::generateNA verified locally (help index)

**Verifier:** evaluation() at R/evaluation.R:36-48 matches the description: err_num = sum((x-y)^2 over the whole numeric block)/sum(m) with no per-variable normalization or breakdown; nrmse/pfc (:53-67) require the true data. No MCAR/MAR/MNAR amputation generator exists (grep ampute/generateNA/createNA/MNAR over R/ and vignettes/: nothing; makeNA in kNN/hotdeck/vimpute only declares coded missings). No benchmark vignette: the 8 vignettes are donorImp, impPCA, irmi, modelImp, VIM, vimpute, VisualImp, xgboostImpute; the 'Performance' section of vimpute.Rmd (line 517ff) is a self-contained iris true-vs-imputed demo of vimpute itself with no comparison against mice/missRanger/missForest.

### P2.51 [competitors] Uniform formula interface: per-variable predictor selection for ML methods
*kind: method-gap (vs simputation (uniform impute_*(df, y + z ~ x1 + x2) grammar); missRanger (two-sided . ~ . formula: LHS = variables to impute, RHS = predictors, e.g. . ~ . - id; verified locally); Hmisc::aregImpute (single formula defines everything)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: vimpute formula works only for regularized/robust/gam/robgam, explicitly not for ranger/xgboost (R/vimpute.R:54-57); predictor selection for ML methods is only global via considered_variables (R/vimpute.R:8-9)

PROPOSAL: Support per-variable predictor subsets for ranger/xgboost via mlr3 task$select() (trivial), and consider a missRanger-style two-sided formula as sugar ('what to impute ~ what to use'). Removes an arbitrary inconsistency users will hit immediately.

REFERENCE: args(missRanger::missRanger) verified locally (formula = . ~ .)

**Verifier:** Within vimpute(): confirmed. Docs state formula is only for regularized/robust/gam/robgam (R/vimpute.R:54-57), enforced at R/helper_vimpute.R:1084-1094; empirically, vimpute(d, method='ranger', formula=list(y = y ~ a)) errors with 'A formula can only be used with the robust, regularized, gam, or robgam methods.' Predictor restriction for ranger/xgboost inside vimpute is only global via considered_variables (R/vimpute.R:8-9, :156, :194). Nuance the claim understates: since 7.1.0 the wrappers rangerImpute()/xgboostImpute()/regressionImp() delegate to vimpute() with a formula interface (LHS = variables to impute, RHS = predictors; R/rangerImpute.R:21-82, NEWS.md 7.1.0), and rangerImpute(y ~ a + b, data) was empirically verified to work — so formula-based predictor selection for ranger/xgboost exists at package level, but only one method per call with hardcoded sequential=FALSE, tune=FALSE, no MI, outside the unified interface. The inconsistency inside vimpute() itself is real.

### P2.52 [methodology-docs] No missingness-mechanism (MAR/MCAR/MNAR) statement anywhere in package docs
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

grep for MAR/MCAR/MNAR/'missing at random' across R/*.R roxygen and all vignettes returns zero hits. Model-based methods (vimpute, irmi, regressionImp, cellwise family) are valid under MAR; kNN/hotdeck need MCAR or MAR-with-informative-distance-variables; makeNA/donorcond explicitly target coded/implausible values (MNAR-adjacent territory). Best practice (Little & Rubin; van Buuren FIMD ch.1-2) is a per-method assumption statement plus a caution that no method fixes MNAR without extra assumptions. Minimum fix: one 'Assumptions' paragraph in the vimpute vignette + a sentence in vimpute.Rd, irmi.Rd, kNN.Rd Details.

**Evidence:** grep -rn 'MAR|MCAR|MNAR|missing at random' R/*.R vignettes/*.Rmd -> no output (verified). The 2011 CSDA and 2016 JSS papers state MAR; the docs never do.

### P2.53 [methodology-docs] Two references in new cellwise docs are materially wrong (verified against publishers)
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellEM.R*

(a) imputeCellEM.Rd/imputeCellMCD.Rd cite 'C. Raymaekers, P.J. Rousseeuw (2024) The cellwise minimum covariance determinant estimator. JASA, 119(545), 576-588' (R/imputeCellEM.R:114-116 and 959-961). Actual: J. (Jakob) Raymaekers — wrong initial — JASA 119(548), doi:10.1080/01621459.2023.2267777, T&F lists pages 2610-2621; issue 545 and pages 576-588 are wrong. (b) R/imputeCellEM.R:118-120 cites 'G. Zaccaria, L. Insolia, A. Farcomeni (2025) Robust model-based clustering with cellwise contamination. Technometrics, forthcoming' — the cellGMM paper is Zaccaria, García-Escudero, Greselin, Mayo-Íscar, 'Cellwise outlier detection in heterogeneous populations', Technometrics 67(4):643-654 (2025; arXiv 2409.07881): wrong co-authors, wrong title, stale 'forthcoming'. Violates the project's no-speculation-in-references rule; both look written from memory.

**Evidence:** Verified via https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.1080/01621459.2023.2267777 (title block: 'Vol 119, No 548') and https://arxiv.org/abs/2409.07881 (authors: Giorgia Zaccaria, Luis A. García-Escudero, Francesca Greselin, Agustín Mayo-Íscar; published Technometrics 67(4):643-654, 2025).

**Verifier:** Both sub-claims verified against the authoritative CrossRef registry (T&F page itself returns 403 to non-browser fetches, so CrossRef was used instead). (a) R/imputeCellEM.R:114-116 cites 'C. Raymaekers, P.J. Rousseeuw (2024) The cellwise minimum covariance determinant estimator. JASA, 119(545), 576--588' and R/imputeCellEM.R:959-961 (imputeCellMCD roxygen) repeats 'Raymaekers, C. and Rousseeuw, P.J. (2024) ... 119(545), 576--588'. CrossRef record for DOI 10.1080/01621459.2023.2267777: title 'The Cellwise Minimum Covariance Determinant Estimator', authors Jakob Raymaekers and Peter J. Rousseeuw, JASA Vol 119 Issue 548, pages 2610-2621, published 2024-10. So the VIM citation has the wrong author initial (C. vs J.), wrong issue (545 vs 548), and wrong pages (576-588 vs 2610-2621); year and journal are correct. Errors propagate to the generated man/imputeCellEM.Rd:162 and man/imputeCellMCD.Rd:100. (b) R/imputeCellEM.R:118-120 cites 'G. Zaccaria, L. Insolia, A. Farcomeni (2025) Robust model-based clustering with cellwise contamination. Technometrics, forthcoming'. A CrossRef bibliographic search for that exact title returns no such paper, and a web search finds no Zaccaria/Insolia/Farcomeni paper of that title. The paper evidently intended — the details section of the same help page says 'differs from cellGMM (Zaccaria et al., 2025)' (man/imputeCellEM.Rd:105) — is 'Cellwise Outlier Detection in Heterogeneous Populations' by Giorgia Zaccaria, Luis A. García-Escudero, Francesca Greselin, Agustín Mayo-Íscar, Technometrics 67(4), 643-654 (2025), DOI 10.1080/00401706.2025.2497822 (arXiv 2409.07881): wrong co-authors (2 of 3 named authors are not on the paper), wrong title, and stale 'forthcoming' for a published paper. This matches the claim exactly, including its diagnosis that both entries look written from memory, which violates the project's no-speculation-in-references rule.

**Repro:** curl -s https://api.crossref.org/works/10.1080/01621459.2023.2267777 | python3 -c 'import json,sys; d=json.load(sys.stdin)["message"]; print(d["title"][0], [(a["given"],a["family"]) for a in d["author"]], d["volume"], d["journal-issue"]["issue"], d["page"])'  # -> Jakob Raymaekers, Peter J. Rousseeuw, 119, 548, 2610-2621. curl -s https://api.crossref.org/works/10.1080/00401706.2025.2497822 | python3 ... # -> 'Cellwise Outlier Detection in Heterogeneous Populations', Zaccaria/García-Escudero/Greselin/Mayo-Íscar, Technometrics 67(4), 643-654. CrossRef query.bibliographic search for 'Robust model-based clustering with cellwise contamination' returns no matching Zaccaria/Insolia/Farcomeni paper. Compare with grep -n 'Raymaekers\|Zaccaria' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellEM.R (lines 114-120, 959-961).

### P2.54 [methodology-docs] Vignette sells regularization as 'robustness' — method-choice trap in a robust-statistics package
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

vimpute.Rmd:173: 'The key difference lies in flexibility (xgboost) versus robustness (regularization).' Elastic-net regularization controls variance/overfitting/multicollinearity; it provides no outlier robustness. VIM's own method="robust"/"robgam" (MM-estimation, robust GAM) are the robust options, so this sentence actively misdirects users with contaminated data toward glmnet. Replace 'robustness' with 'stability/shrinkage', and add one sentence pointing to method="robust" for outlier resistance. Same paragraph's claims about xgboost ('uneven ... may be less stable') are asserted, not shown by the plots.

**Evidence:** vimpute.Rmd:164-173 (side-by-side marginplots then the flexibility-vs-robustness sentence); contrast with the method list at lines 113-115 where 'robust' = lmrob MM-estimation.

### P2.55 [methodology-docs] irmi deprecation note overclaims vimpute ('more ... robust', 'more flexible') and uses 'Deprecated' without lifecycle
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/irmi.R*

R/irmi.R:12-15: 'Deprecated: irmi() is considered legacy functionality. ... please use vimpute() instead, which provides a more modern, flexible and robust imputation framework.' Problems: (a) 'robust' unqualified — vimpute's default is ranger; robustness requires method="robust"/"robgam", whereas robustness is irmi's core feature, so the unqualified claim inverts reality; (b) 'more flexible' ignores that vimpute has no equivalent of irmi's mixed/mixed.constant (semi-continuous) and count handling — a capability regression users must know about before migrating; (c) 'Deprecated' appears without .Deprecated(), and sibling classic methods (kNN.Rd) carry no such note, sending mixed lifecycle signals for a JSS-documented flagship. Suggest: 'legacy; superseded by vimpute() for model-based imputation (use method="robust" for robustness); irmi remains supported and is still required for semi-continuous/count variables.'

**Evidence:** R/irmi.R:12-15 (@note); irmi params mixed/mixed.constant/count at R/irmi.R:20-24; vimpute signature (R/vimpute.R:155-176) has no counterpart; no .Deprecated() call in irmi body; kNN.R roxygen has no legacy note.

### P2.56 [methodology-docs] uncert="pmm"/"midastouch" silently hard-code k=5 random-draw PMM, ignoring user pmm_k/pmm_k_method; midastouch is a variant of the cited method
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

The uncert path sets pmm_k=5L and pmm_k_method="random" unconditionally (R/helper_vimpute.R:2050-2052 for "pmm", 2065 for "midastouch"); the user's pmm_k/pmm_k_method arguments apply only to the separate pmm=TRUE path (defaults k=1/"mean", deterministic). Neither vimpute.Rd (@param uncert, R/vimpute.R:98-105) nor the vignette (lines 386-409) mentions that the two PMM paths use different, non-overridable defaults. Also, the doc string 'midastouch (covariate-distance-weighted PMM, Siddique & Belin 2008)' implies the published MIDAS procedure; the implementation (midastouch_donors, helper_vimpute.R:1679-1740) is a variant: 50/50 blend of range-normalized Mahalanobis covariate distance and prediction-score distance, donor sampled with prob ∝ 1/d among the k=5 nearest — Siddique & Belin use predictive distances with an ABB step. Say 'inspired by' and document the actual algorithm + fixed k.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:2050-2052 (`uncert_args$pmm_k <- 5L; uncert_args$pmm_k_method <- "random"`), 2065 (`uncert_args$pmm_k <- 5L`), 1679-1740 (Mahalanobis + score 0.5/0.5 blend, weights 1/(d+eps)); vimpute.R:104 cites Siddique & Belin 2008.

### P2.57 [usability] marginplot(..., delimiter="_imp") errors on vimpute()'s own data.table output
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/marginplot.R*

vimpute() returns a data.table, but marginplot's delimiter machinery uses data.frame indexing: tmp <- grep(delimiter, colnames(x)); imp_var <- x[, tmp, drop=FALSE] (marginplot.R:123-126). On a data.table, x[, tmp] looks up a column literally named 'tmp' and fails. So the natural post-imputation workflow — impute with vimpute, inspect imputed points with VIM's signature marginplot — breaks with a cryptic data.table error. Verified: imp <- vimpute(sleep, sequential=FALSE); marginplot(imp[, ..cols], delimiter="_imp") -> Error "j (the 2nd argument inside [...]) is a single symbol but column name 'tmp' is not found"; identical call after as.data.frame(imp) works. aggr(), matrixplot(), scattmatrixMiss() accept the data.table fine. Fix: coerce to data.frame at the top of marginplot (and audit other *Miss plots for the same idiom).

**Evidence:** marginplot.R:123-126. Commands: imp <- vimpute(sleep, sequential=FALSE); marginplot(imp[, c("Sleep","Dream","Sleep_imp","Dream_imp")], delimiter="_imp") -> ERROR; marginplot(as.data.frame(imp)[, cols], delimiter="_imp") -> OK; aggr/matrixplot/scattmatrixMiss on the same data.table -> OK.

**Verifier:** Confirmed by code reading and exact reproduction. vimpute() output has class c("data.table","data.frame") (verified live). /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/marginplot.R:123-126 uses data.frame idiom: tmp <- grep(delimiter, colnames(x)); imp_var <- x[, tmp, drop=FALSE]. On a data.table, j is evaluated as a symbol within the table's frame, so it looks for a column literally named 'tmp' and fails; the class check at marginplot.R:117 (inherits(x, c("data.frame","matrix"))) passes for data.table, so there is no early, friendly error. Reproduced: imp <- vimpute(sleep, sequential=FALSE); marginplot(imp[, ..cols], delimiter="_imp") with cols = c("Sleep","Dream","Sleep_imp","Dream_imp") -> Error "j (the 2nd argument inside [...]) is a single symbol but column name 'tmp' is not found. If you intended to select columns using a variable in calling scope, please try DT[, ..tmp]." — exactly the claimed cryptic data.table error. Same error with a with=FALSE column subset (still a data.table). The identical call after as.data.frame(imp) works (no error). aggr() on the same data.table works, confirming the inconsistency within VIM's own visualization functions (matrixplot was verified on a data.frame only; the claim's core assertion concerns marginplot and is fully demonstrated). The proposed fix (coerce to data.frame at the top of marginplot; audit other delimiter-using *Miss plots for the same x[, tmp] idiom) is appropriate.

**Repro:** Rscript <scratchpad>/claim3_marginplot.R -> TEST A (data.table + delimiter): ERROR "column name 'tmp' is not found"; TEST B (as.data.frame first): OK; TEST C (with=FALSE subset, still data.table): same ERROR; TEST D: aggr(imp) OK. Output in claim3_out.txt.

### P2.58 [usability] considered_variables silently drops all other columns from the returned dataset
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

The documented example z <- vimpute(sleep, considered_variables=c("Sleep","Dream","Span","BodyWgt"), sequential=FALSE) returns 62x7 (Sleep, Dream, Span, BodyWgt + 3 _imp cols) from a 62x10 input: BrainWgt, NonD, Gest, Pred, Exp, Danger are gone without any message. The @param doc says considered_variables 'exclud[es] irrelevant columns from the imputation process' — it never says the columns are removed from the output. mice keeps all columns. Users doing 'impute these, keep the rest' silently lose data and must cbind back manually (risky if row order assumptions break). Either return the full data with untouched columns, or add an explicit message + doc sentence stating columns are dropped.

**Evidence:** Command (verbatim ?vimpute example): z <- vimpute(data=sleep, considered_variables=c("Sleep","Dream","Span","BodyWgt"), sequential=FALSE); dim(z) -> 62 x 7; names(z) -> Sleep,Dream,Span,BodyWgt,Sleep_imp,Dream_imp,Span_imp. Doc: man/vimpute.Rd:35.

### P2.59 [usability] m=1 result (the default) is a bare data.table: no metadata, no print method, no progress feedback during the run
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

vimpute(sleep) runs ~4s in complete silence (default sequential=TRUE, nseq=10) and returns a plain data.table: attributes carry nothing beyond data.table defaults (verified: setdiff(names(attributes(imp)), c("names","row.names","class",".internal.selfref")) == character(0)). There is no record of which method imputed which variable (fatal in combination with the length-1 method-list bug), how many iterations ran, or whether eps convergence was reached; print() just dumps 132 lines of data. mice's mids prints methods and predictor matrix; VIM's own print.vimmi (m>1) is excellent — m=1 users deserve the same (store methods/iterations as attributes + a small print header, or return a lightweight class). Progress: mice prints iter/variable progress by default; vimpute's only option is verbose=TRUE which is developer debug spam in mixed German/English ('ITERATION 1 von 1', 'NAs in feature variables bearbeiten', '***** OHE'), ~14 lines per variable per iteration — not a progress report. On real-sized data the default is minutes of silence.

**Evidence:** Commands: system.time(vimpute(sleep)) -> 3.95s, zero output; attributes check -> character(0); print -> plain data.table. verbose=TRUE output captured in exp3 3.1 shows German/English debug lines. Contrast print.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:193) which shows m, boot, uncert, per-variable NA counts and methods.

### P2.60 [usability] Error-message quality is inconsistent; donorcond and method errors don't say what to do instead
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

Graded every misuse path. GOOD: all-NA column -> "Variable 'allna' contains only missing values. No model can be estimated. Please remove it from 'considered_variables' or impute it externally."; m>1 with no variability source -> actionable warning naming boot/uncert/pmm (vimpute.R:341-342); complete() action errors list valid options (vimmi.R:129-155). POOR: (a) vimpute(sleep, donorcond=list(Sleep="5")) -> "Invalid donor condition for 'Sleep': Objekt 'x5' nicht gefunden" — leaks the internal eval variable, half-German, gives no format hint (should say: conditions are comparison strings like ">5"); same for non-string donorcond=list(Sleep=5). (b) donorcond=list(Sleeep=">5") warns 'Unknown variable name(s) in donorcond: Sleeep' (vimpute.R:210-215) but then still evaluates it and dies with the unrelated "Condition ... must evaluate to a logical vector of length 62" — warn-then-crash with a misleading error; unknown vars should be skipped or the check made an error. (c) method="randomforest" -> "Unsupported method 'randomforest'." without listing the 6 supported methods (helper_vimpute.R:1020); the named-list variant is worse: "One or more unsupported methods found in 'method'." doesn't even name the offender (helper_vimpute.R:1046-1048). ?vimpute also never shows the donorcond string format, deferring to 'similar to kNN()'.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:209-232 (donorcond), helper_vimpute.R:1020,1046-1048 (method). Commands+outputs: donorcond=list(Sleep="5") -> Objekt 'x5' nicht gefunden; donorcond=list(Sleeep=">5") -> warning then 'logical vector of length 62' error; donorcond=list(">5") -> "'donorcond' must be a named list." (good); method="randomforest" -> "Unsupported method 'randomforest'."

### P2.61 [usability] ?vimpute contains invalid R in the method example, typos in the title, and misleading parameter docs
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/man/vimpute.Rd*

(1) The @param method example 'as.list(var1 = "xgboost", var2="robust")' is not valid R — running it errors 'Argument "x" fehlt (ohne Standardwert)'; must be list(var1=..., var2=...). A new user copying the doc's only per-variable syntax hits an R error unrelated to VIM. (2) Title: 'Impute missing values with prefered model, sequentially, with hyperparametertuning and with PMM (if wanted)' — 'prefered', 'hyperparametertuning', informal '(if wanted)' — this is the package's flagship function title on CRAN. (3) @param data says 'Provide as a data.table' but data.frame and tibble both work (verified) — needlessly scares off the majority of users. (4) First example's comment '# Single imputation (default)' annotates vimpute(sleep, sequential=FALSE) although the default is sequential=TRUE. (5) All examples are \dontrun so none are exercised by R CMD check; they do all run when executed manually (verified, exp6). 

**Evidence:** man/vimpute.Rd:5 (title, = R/vimpute.R:2), :41 (as.list example), :33 (data.table claim), :167-168 (default comment). Commands: as.list(var1="xgboost", var2="robust") -> Error 'Argument "x" fehlt'; vimpute(tibble::as_tibble(sleep), sequential=FALSE) -> OK; vimpute(sleep) on data.frame -> OK.

### P2.62 [framework-design] Per-variable specification is fragmented across 9 parallel arguments with ambiguous learner_params semantics — unify behind a spec object
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

To say 'ranger for x1, gam for x2 with formula, tuned, with PMM(k=5, median)' the user must coordinate up to nine parallel per-variable containers: method, pmm, pmm_k, pmm_k_method, learner_params, formula, tune, makeNA, donorcond (signature vimpute.R:154-176), each with its own recycling rules (map_pmm, map_pmm_k, map_pmm_k_method, map_tune, map_learner_params in helper_vimpute.R:552-880). learner_params is resolved three ways — per variable, per method, global — and a variable named 'ranger' or 'gam' makes the mapping ambiguous, guarded only by a warning (helper_vimpute.R:926-933). PMM is additionally specifiable two ways (pmm=TRUE and uncert="pmm") with a precedence warning (vimpute.R:332-337). This is objectively worse than mice's two-object model once >2 variables are customised. Proposed contract, both layers: (1) spec objects: `vimpute(data, spec = list(x1 = vs_ranger(num.trees=500, tune=TRUE, uncert="pmm", pmm_k=5), x2 = vs_gam(formula = ~ s(age)+region), x3 = vs_robust(donorcond = ">= 0")), default = vs_ranger())` where vs_*() constructors validate eagerly against the learner's param_set at call time (fail fast, not at iteration 7); (2) formula grammar à la simputation as sugar compiled to the same spec: `vimpute(data, x1 ~ hp + wt | ranger(tune = TRUE), x2 ~ . | gam())`. Keep the current flat arguments as a deprecated compatibility layer that compiles to specs internally.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:154-176 signature; helper_vimpute.R:806-880 map_learner_params 3-way resolution; helper_vimpute.R:926-933 reserved-name collision only warns; vimpute.R:332-337 pmm/uncert precedence warning

### P2.63 [framework-design] Tuning architecture: no caching across m imputations, flat one-shot design, machine-dependent random search — specify an AutoTuner-based design
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

What exists is real (per-learner search spaces scaled by n in build_vimpute_search_space helper_vimpute.R:2346-2413, CV via safe_cv_folds, budget via trm("evals"), tuned-vs-default comparison) but the architecture has four gaps. (1) No caching across m: the m>1 path recurses into vimpute() m times (vimpute.R:419-457) passing tune through, so tuning cost is m x (tuning + comparison CV) and each imputation may pick DIFFERENT hyperparameters — between-imputation variance then conflates missing-data uncertainty with tuner noise, which is statistically wrong for Rubin's rules. (2) One-shot at mid-sequence with within-loop cache only (hyperparameter_cache, vimpute.R:499) — never re-examined as imputed predictors stabilise. (3) tnr("random_search", batch_size = parallel::detectCores() - 1) (vimpute.R:1263-1264, 1354-1355) makes the evaluated-configuration sequence depend on the machine's core count: same seed, different laptop, different imputations. (4) future::plan("sequential") is unconditionally set after the first tuned variable (vimpute.R:1411), clobbering a user-chosen parallel plan for the rest of the run. Proposed design: tune ONCE on the observed cells before the m-loop, store per-variable tuned param_vals in a `tuning` object passed into each imputation run; expose `tune_control = vimpute_tune_control(resampling = rsmp("cv", 5), budget = 20, tuner = "random_search", batch_size = 1L, nested = FALSE)`; default batch_size fixed (1) for reproducibility; document that nested resampling is intentionally skipped because the goal is good imputations, not unbiased generalisation estimates. Export the search spaces (vimpute_search_space(learner_id)) so users can override them per variable via the spec object.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:2346-2413 build_vimpute_search_space; vimpute.R:419-457 m-loop recursion re-passing tune; vimpute.R:1263-1264 `batch <- max(1, parallel::detectCores() - 1)`; vimpute.R:1411 future::plan("sequential")

### P2.64 [framework-design] Adding a new imputation method requires ~12 coordinated edits across two files — define a register_vimpute_method() plugin contract
*kind: refactor | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Exact steps to add method 'newmeth' today: (1) write R6 Learner classes (regr+classif) + a register_newmeth_learners() (pattern: helper_vimpute.R:6-273, 2504+); (2) add to supported_methods (helper_vimpute.R:997); (3) add to reserved_methods (helper_vimpute.R:926); (4) add registration gating + learner_ids (vimpute.R:352-374); (5) extend learners_list in both the numeric and factor branches (vimpute.R:707-725); (6) add a per-method param-validation block (vimpute.R:921-1096 — six near-identical copies already); (7-9) extend THREE copy-pasted grepl/modifyList dispatch chains (vimpute.R:1105-1117, 1149-1179, 1864-1876); (10) add a search space (helper_vimpute.R:2346); (11) if formula-capable, edit two hard-coded allow-lists (vimpute.R:684, helper_vimpute.R:1091); (12) if boot/uncert-capable, extend extract_model_info (helper_vimpute.R:1503). Third parties cannot extend without patching VIM. Proposed contract: `register_vimpute_method(name, learner = list(regr = "regr.ranger", classif = "classif.ranger") | function(task_type, ...), search_space = function(task) ps(...), supports = c(formula = FALSE, missings = TRUE, boot = FALSE, uncert = c("pmm","resid")), fallback = "robust", validate = function(y_obs, data) NULL_or_reason)` writing into a package-env registry (`.vimpute_methods`). vimpute() then resolves everything from the registry: supported_methods <- names(.vimpute_methods), the three modifyList chains collapse to one registry lookup, formula allow-list becomes supports["formula"], precheck fallbacks call validate(). This also fixes the copy-paste drift risk (the three chains can already silently disagree) and makes mlr3extralearners (e.g. lightgbm, noted as TODO at vimpute.R:347-349) a one-liner for users.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1105-1117, 1149-1179, 1864-1876 three duplicated grepl-dispatch chains; helper_vimpute.R:997 supported_methods; vimpute.R:684 + helper_vimpute.R:1091 duplicated formula allow-lists

### P2.65 [framework-design] Keep vimmi over native mids, but harden the bridge: as.mids.vimmi is not a real S3 method, with() returns a bare list, and there are no chain diagnostics
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimmi.R*

Returning mice::mids natively is the wrong call: it would promote mice from Suggests to a hard structural dependency, force mice's memory layout, and drop vimmi's extra metadata (boot, uncert, per-variable method list). vimmi's compact storage (data once + imp values only, vimmi.R:74-89) is strictly better. But the bridge has three gaps. (1) as.mids.vimmi is exported as a plain function (NAMESPACE:15 `export(as.mids.vimmi)`) — there is no as.mids generic anywhere (mice::as.mids is not generic), so the '.vimmi' suffix is misleading dressing; users must know the full name. Either export it as `vim_as_mids()` or register it on a real generic. (2) with.vimmi returns an anonymous list (vimmi.R:178-186); mice::pool() accepts lists of fits in recent versions but summary()/D1()/anova() workflows expect mira — wrap the return as `structure(list(call=match.call(), call1=x$call, nmis=x$nmis, analyses=fits), class=c("mira","matrix"))`-style (mirror mice::as.mira) when mice is available. (3) vimmi stores no per-iteration chain statistics, so there is no equivalent of plot(mids) trace plots for FCS convergence — the data exists in-loop (convergence_data, check_convergence) but is discarded; add `chain = list(mean = array[nvar, nseq, m], var = ...)` to new_vimmi and a plot.vimmi() drawing mean/sd traces. Contract sketch: `new_vimmi(..., chain = chain_stats, seed = seed)` + `plot.vimmi(x, y = c("chains","density","strip"))`.

**Evidence:** NAMESPACE:15 export(as.mids.vimmi) — plain export, no S3method; vimmi.R:178-186 with.vimmi returns lapply() list; vimmi.R:74-89 constructor has no chain/seed slots

### P2.66 [framework-design] Defaults produce conditional-mean single imputation (uncert='none', pmm=FALSE) and the main model fit has no error fallback
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Two defensibility gaps in the out-of-the-box behaviour. (1) Defaults are method='ranger', pmm=FALSE, uncert='none' (vimpute.R:157-174): every numeric NA gets the ranger conditional mean. For any downstream analysis beyond point prediction this attenuates variance and distorts marginal distributions — exactly the failure mode mice's pmm default was designed to avoid; a reviewer comparing density plots of VIM-vs-mice defaults will show VIM losing. The m>1 warning (vimpute.R:340-343) is good but doesn't help m=1 users. Proposal: default `uncert = "pmm"` for numeric targets in single imputation (documented, with uncert="none" as explicit opt-in for prediction-oriented use), keeping current behaviour reachable. (2) Fallback chain is asymmetric: pre-checks fall back to 'robust' for glmnet/gam edge cases (helper_vimpute.R:1103-1189, vimpute.R:795-807, 872-884) and n_train==0 falls back to median/mode (vimpute.R:844-870), but the actual `learner$train(task)` at vimpute.R:1936 is bare — if ranger/xgboost errors (e.g. after OHE explosion, novel-level issues) the entire vimpute() run aborts, losing all completed variables and iterations. Proposal: wrap the train/predict of each variable in tryCatch with the declared per-method fallback chain (registry finding), ultimately median/mode + loud warning, so one pathological column cannot destroy the run — mice's behaviour (fail that variable, continue) is the bar.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:157-174 defaults pmm=FALSE, uncert='none'; vimpute.R:1936 `learner$train(task)` with no tryCatch (contrast bootstrap refit at 1964-1971 which IS wrapped); helper_vimpute.R:1103-1189 robust fallbacks exist only in precheck

### P2.67 [framework-design] Convergence criterion is an unscaled sum of raw per-variable MSEs — eps = 0.005 is meaningless across data scales, and no diagnostics are returned
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

check_convergence (helper_vimpute.R:2197-2233) computes total_diff = sum over numeric variables of mean squared change of imputed values (raw units) + sum over factors of disagreement rates, compared against a single eps (default 0.005). Consequences: a variable measured in thousands (e.g. BodyWgt in sleep) makes total_diff effectively never fall below eps (nseq always exhausted, silently costly), while standardized data 'converges' instantly; mixing one wide-scale numeric with factors means the categorical signal is invisible in the sum. The criterion is also undocumented in ?vimpute beyond 'predictions change less than this amount'. There is additionally dead/odd code in the convergence path: on the break branch, class probabilities are recomputed and sampled via apply(...) but the result is discarded (helper_vimpute.R:2245-2268). Proposed contract: per-variable scaled criterion `d_v = mean((new-old)^2)/var(observed_v)` for numerics and disagreement rate for factors, converged when max_v d_v < eps (max, not sum, so one variable can't mask another); return a `convergence` element (iterations x variables matrix of d_v) in the result and print it in verbose mode; document eps as 'relative change per variable'. This also feeds the vimmi chain-diagnostics finding.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:2207-2222 unscaled `d_var <- mean((new_vals - old_vals)^2)` summed across variables; helper_vimpute.R:2231 `if (total_diff >= eps)`; helper_vimpute.R:2265-2267 sampled predictions computed and discarded

### P2.68 [framework-design] Silent coercions and type-unstable return: ordered factors flattened, logicals numeric-ified, data.table-vs-list return depending on flags
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

Foot-gun cluster, all silent. (1) precheck coerces ordered factors to unordered (helper_vimpute.R:1203-1206, repeated in-loop at vimpute.R:817-820, 1624-1632) and logical to numeric (helper_vimpute.R:1213-1214): a logical column comes back as doubles, an ordered factor loses its ordering permanently in the output — no message in either case, and imputation of ordinals as nominals is also a methods-quality loss (mice has polr for this). (2) The return TYPE of vimpute() depends on flag settings: plain data.table normally, but a list(data=..., pred_history=..., tuning_log=...) when pred_history=TRUE or any tune is truthy (build_vimpute_result, helper_vimpute.R:1825-1847) — so adding tune=TRUE to working code breaks every downstream `result$column` access; empirically confirmed (class(res)[1] == 'list' with tune=TRUE). (3) data.frame in, data.table out (helper_vimpute.R:1828) — colnames-preserving but class-changing. Proposed contract: always return an object of class c("vimpute","data.table") (or match input class) with diagnostics as attributes accessed via pred_history(x), tuning_log(x), convergence(x); restore logical/ordered types in build_vimpute_result using the saved original_data types (round-trip: impute as numeric/factor internally, cast back on exit, as kNN does); message() once per coerced column.

**Evidence:** helper_vimpute.R:1203-1220 ordered->factor and logical->as.numeric coercions in precheck; helper_vimpute.R:1825-1847 build_vimpute_result returns data.table or list; confirmed empirically: class(res)[1]=='list' when tune=TRUE

### P2.69 [formulas] kNN weightDist=TRUE assumes distances in [0,1]; with methodStand="iqr" (or NA sentinels) weights become Inf and imputed values NaN
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/kNN.R*

The aggregation weights are computed as 1-dist with the comment '1-dist because dist is between 0 and 1' (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/kNN.R:424-426). That invariant only holds for methodStand="range" with complete distance variables and no mixed variables. With methodStand="iqr" (scaling by IQR, R/gowerD.R:102-107) per-variable contributions are unbounded; with NAs in distance variables contributions reach 2 (sentinel finding); with mixed variables they are unbounded. When all k nearest distances are >= 1, every 1-dist is <= 0 and the clamp pmax(min(x[x>0])/10, x) takes min over an empty set = Inf, so all aggregation weights are Inf and numFun returns NaN, which is written into the data. ?kNN documents weightDist simply as 'if the distances of the k nearest neighbours should be used as weights' with no restriction on methodStand (R/kNN.R:96-98). Fix: renormalise distances (e.g. divide by max or use exp(-d)) before 1-d, or clamp distances at 1, and guard the empty-positive-set case.

**Evidence:** Reproduced: dd <- data.frame(x=c(1,2,3,4,100), y=c(10,20,30,40,NA)); kNN(dd, variable="y", dist_var="x", k=2, numFun=function(x,weights) weighted.mean(x,weights), weightDist=TRUE, methodStand="iqr") imputes y[5]=NaN (range mode imputes 36). Clamp: R/kNN.R:425-426; IQR scaling: R/gowerD.R:102-107.

**Verifier:** Reproduced with the installed build: dd <- data.frame(x=c(1,2,3,4,100), y=c(10,20,30,40,NA)); kNN(dd, variable="y", dist_var="x", k=2, numFun=function(x,weights) weighted.mean(x,weights), weightDist=TRUE, methodStand="iqr") writes y[5]=NaN into the returned data (accompanied by the base-R warning 'no non-missing arguments to min; returning Inf'), while the identical call with methodStand="range" imputes 36. Mechanism verified step by step: under iqr the distance variable is scaled by IQR=2 (R/gowerD.R:102-107), so the recipient (x=100 -> 50) is at scaled distance 48 and 48.5 from its two nearest donors; the aggregation code at /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/kNN.R:424-426 computes weights as apply(1-mindi[[2]], 2, function(x) pmax(min(x[x>0])/10, x)) under the comment '1-dist because dist is between 0 and 1' — with all distances >=1, every 1-dist is <=0, x[x>0] is empty, min(empty)=Inf, pmax(Inf/10, x)=Inf for all weights, and weighted.mean(values, c(Inf,Inf))=Inf/Inf=NaN. The documentation at R/kNN.R:96-98 describes weightDist with no restriction on methodStand, so nothing warns the user off this combination. The claim's parenthetical about NA sentinels (per-variable contributions up to ~2 via the maxplus1 replacement at R/gowerD.R:121-127) and unbounded mixed contributions is consistent with the code but was not separately reproduced; the primary iqr path is fully demonstrated.

**Repro:** .libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); dd <- data.frame(x=c(1,2,3,4,100), y=c(10,20,30,40,NA)); kNN(dd, variable="y", dist_var="x", k=2, numFun=function(x,weights) weighted.mean(x,weights), weightDist=TRUE, methodStand="iqr", imp_var=FALSE)$y[5]  # -> NaN (warning: min over empty set returns Inf); same call with methodStand="range" -> 36

### P2.70 [formulas] Gower NA convention (sentinel max+1) makes d(NA,NA)=0 and d(NA,obs) up to 2: kNN prefers donors sharing the recipient's missingness pattern
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R*

gowerD replaces NAs in distance variables by max+1 of the pooled column AFTER scaling (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R:121-127, with the code's own comment 'TODO: find better way to handle missing in distance variables'). Consequences, all confirmed numerically: (a) two records missing the same variable get contribution 0 (identical sentinel) — maximally similar; (b) NA vs observed contributes |sentinel - value|, between 1 and 2 weight-shares for range-scaled numerics, i.e. the per-variable 'Gower' distance exceeds its nominal max of 1 and depends on the observed value's position in the range. Gower (1971)'s standard convention instead excludes non-comparable variables and renormalises the weight denominator. Net effect on imputation: a donor that shares the recipient's NA pattern deterministically beats donors identical to the recipient on all observed variables, so donor selection is biased toward records with matching missingness (under MAR this systematically selects unrepresentative donors). Neither ?gowerD nor ?kNN mentions any of this — ?kNN only says 'a variation of the Gower Distance'. Fix direction: implement omit-and-renormalise (track per-pair comparable weight sums in the C++ kernel), or at minimum document the sentinel behaviour prominently in ?kNN/?gowerD.

**Evidence:** Reproduced: gowerD(data.frame(v=c(0,1,NA,NA))) gives d(0,NA)=2, d(1,NA)=1, d(NA,NA)=0. End-to-end: data.frame(a=c(.1,.2,.3,.4,NA,NA), b=1, y=c(10,20,30,40,5000,NA)); kNN(variable="y", dist_var=c("a","b"), k=1) imputes 5000 — the donor whose a is also NA wins against four donors identical on the observed variable b. Sentinel code: R/gowerD.R:121-127; C++ sees sentinel as ordinary value: src/gowerD.cpp:21-26.

### P3.4 [check] CI R-CMD-check never runs on devel or feature branches where all development happens

.github/workflows/R-CMD-check.yaml restricts both push and pull_request triggers to [main, master] (lines 9 and 11). The entire vimpute/vimmi/cellwise modernization therefore gets no automated R CMD check (6-platform matrix incl. R-devel on Windows/Ubuntu) until merged into master -- exactly the work most likely to break checks. test-coverage.yaml has the same restriction pattern.
