### P3.5 [vimpute-core] Per-variable, per-iteration 5-fold CV of glmnet candidates plus shared R6 learner mutation
*kind: performance | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

When method='regularized' (numeric target) the learner_candidates list has two entries, so vimpute runs a full 5-fold CV comparison of regr.cv_glmnet vs regr.glmnet for EVERY variable in EVERY iteration (vimpute.R:1102-1135), never cached — with nseq=10 and 5 variables that is 100 CV resamplings before any actual model is fit. The lapply also mutates the shared R6 learner objects in `learners` via `lrn$param_set$values <- modifyList(...)` (vimpute.R:1106-1116), so variable A's glmnet params leak into variable B's candidate comparison (the final fit is protected because a fresh lrn() is created at vimpute.R:1142). Cache the winner per variable after iteration 1 and clone candidates before setting params.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1102-1135 resample() over candidates inside the var/iteration double loop; mutation of shared objects at vimpute.R:1106-1116

### P3.6 [vimpute-core] future::plan('sequential') forced after tuning; tuner parallelism is illusory
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

After the tuning block, vimpute.R:1411 unconditionally sets future::plan('sequential'), overriding any user-chosen parallel plan for the remainder of the call (only restored on exit via on.exit at vimpute.R:180). Meanwhile the tuner uses batch_size = detectCores()-1 (vimpute.R:1263-1264, 1354-1355) but no multisession plan is ever set, so random search evaluates sequentially anyway — the batch size buys nothing and misleads. Either set a documented plan around tuner$optimize() and restore the caller's plan immediately after, or drop the plan manipulation and the oversized batch_size.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1411 `future::plan("sequential")` unconditional; vimpute.R:1263 `batch <- max(1, parallel::detectCores() - 1)` with no multisession plan

**Verifier:** All three components verified. (1) R/vimpute.R:1411 executes future::plan("sequential") unconditionally at the end of each variable's first-time tuning block (entered at vimpute.R:1202 when i == round(nseq/2); line 1411 runs even on the skip/failed-tuning paths inside that branch), overriding any user-chosen plan for the remainder of the call; the caller's plan is only restored via on.exit at vimpute.R:179-180. Empirically demonstrated by tracing mlr3::benchmark (which executes the tuning batches) during vimpute(df, method='ranger', tune=TRUE, nseq=4) with two NA variables after the user set plan(multisession, workers=2): the active plan at successive tuning batches was 'tweaked', 'tweaked' (variable 1 — user's multisession honored), then 'sequential', 'sequential' (variable 2 — forced by line 1411), and the user's plan was restored only after vimpute returned. (2) vimpute itself never activates a parallel backend: grep shows the only active future::plan calls are the save/restore (179-180) and the forced 'sequential' (1411); future::plan('multisession') exists only commented out (vimpute.R:1473, 1583). Yet the tuner is built with batch_size = max(1, parallel::detectCores() - 1) (vimpute.R:1263-1264 and 1354-1355). In mlr3tuning/bbotk, batch evaluation parallelism comes solely from the active future backend — under the default sequential plan the core-sized batch buys nothing (and the trace confirms the plan, not batch_size, governs execution). So out of the box the tuning is fully sequential despite a cores-sized batch, and a user who sets a parallel plan gets it silently killed after the first tuned variable. Minor nuance on the claim's wording: the first tuned variable DOES parallelize if the user set a plan, which the claim itself acknowledges ('for the remainder of the call'). P3 severity is appropriate; the suggested fix (documented plan around tuner$optimize with immediate restore, or dropping the plan manipulation and oversized batch_size) is sound.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/test_claim3b.R — output: 'Active plan at each mlr3::benchmark call (tuning batches, in order): "tweaked" "tweaked" "sequential" "sequential"' with user multisession plan set before the call and restored after return.

### P3.7 [vimpute-core] Dead code and fragile state in the 2200-line vimpute(): commented tuning block, unused copies, lazily-saved undefined variable
*kind: refactor | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

Refactor targets: (a) ~165 lines of commented-out legacy tuning code (vimpute.R:1430-1594); (b) `data_before <- copy(data)` at vimpute.R:527 is never used but deep-copies the whole dataset per variable per iteration; (c) duplicate `learner <- list(classifier=..., regressor=...)` at vimpute.R:1851 immediately overwritten at 1854; (d) `stored_model_info` is only defined in the non-semicontinuous branch (vimpute.R:1939) yet passed to predict_imputations() for is_sc variables too (vimpute.R:2109) — it currently survives only because R's lazy evaluation never forces the promise on the is_sc path (verified: no error), a booby trap for any future change that touches stored_model_info when is_sc; (e) per-prediction `max(sapply(na.omit(data[[var]]), get_decimal_places))` scans all observed values on every call (helper_vimpute.R:2021). Extracting the per-variable body into a function with an explicit state object would remove this class of leakage.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:527, 1430-1594, 1851/1854, 1939 vs 2109; helper_vimpute.R:2021

### P3.8 [vimpute-core] m>1 recursion repeats candidate selection and tuning m times; no per-run RNG stream control
*kind: performance | verdict: unverified | confidence: medium | file: R/vimpute.R*

The m>1 path (vimpute.R:419-457) re-runs the full pipeline — including glmnet candidate CV and, if tune=TRUE, the complete random-search tuning per variable — independently for each of the m imputations, multiplying the most expensive steps by m although hyperparameters are conceptually shareable across imputations (mice tunes once). Reproducibility works only via a single ambient set.seed() before the call (verified identical results across two seeded runs); there is no seed argument and no per-imputation RNG streams (e.g. parallel-safe L'Ecuyer), so any future parallelization of the m loop will silently break reproducibility. Suggest: tune once, pass hyperparameter_cache into the m runs, and add a documented seed argument with per-run streams.

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:419-457 recursive vimpute(m=1) inside for-loop passing tune=tune; no 'seed' formal in vimpute() signature (vimpute.R:154-176); empirical: set.seed(42) twice gives identical vimmi$imp

### P3.9 [vimpute-helpers] Zero-count (unused) factor levels trigger spurious 'regularized' -> 'robust' fallback in precheck
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

The glmnet suitability check uses any(table(x_obs) <= 1) on predictors (R/helper_vimpute.R:1121) and any(table(y_obs) <= 1) on factor targets (line 1105) WITHOUT droplevels, so a factor with an unused level (count 0) always trips the check. Verified: y numeric with NAs, predictor f = factor(rep(c('a','b'),20), levels=c('a','b','c')) -> warning "Predictor 'f' unsuitable for glmnet. Falling back to 'robust' for 'y'" and method silently downgraded, although glmnet would fit fine after droplevels (which sanitize_model_features/one-hot encoding would do anyway). Fix: table(droplevels(x_obs)) in both checks. Also note the check runs over ALL predictors even for variables the user did not request 'regularized' for -- correct today because of the method[[var]] guard, but the y_obs computed at line 1101 for every variable is wasted work.

**Evidence:** Repro via VIM:::precheck(method='regularized') on data with an unused factor level -> method for 'y' becomes 'robust' with the misleading warning.

**Verifier:** Reproduced exactly as claimed on the installed build. VIM:::precheck (R/helper_vimpute.R:882) uses any(table(x_obs) <= 1) on factor predictors (line 1121) and any(table(y_obs) <= 1) on factor targets (line 1105) without droplevels, so a level with count 0 always trips the check. Repro: numeric y with 4 NAs, predictor f = factor(rep(c('a','b'),20), levels=c('a','b','c')) (table: a=20, b=20, c=0), method='regularized' -> warning "Predictor 'f' unsuitable for glmnet. Falling back to 'robust' for 'y'." and method[['y']] silently becomes 'robust'; the droplevels control run keeps 'regularized' with no warning. The target-side path is equally affected: factor target with levels u/v/w where w is unused (19/19/0) -> "Target 'y' has too few observations per class for 'regularized'" -> fallback, although both actual classes have 19 observations. The fallback is spurious: glmnet fits fine with an all-zero one-hot column (verified empirically), the glmnet pipeline one-hot encodes factors (po('encode', method='one-hot'), R/vimpute.R:762), and sanitize_model_features droplevels()s both target and factor features downstream (helper_vimpute.R:318, 335). Secondary notes also verified: the per-variable loop computes y_obs at line 1101 before the method guard at line 1103, so it is wasted work for non-regularized variables (trivial cost). Fix direction (table(droplevels(x_obs)) at lines 1105 and 1121) is correct.

**Repro:** Rscript /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/repro_claim3_precheck.R -> CASE 1 (unused predictor level): warning 'Predictor f unsuitable for glmnet. Falling back to robust for y.', method for y: robust; CASE 2 (droplevels control): no warnings, method stays regularized; CASE 3 (unused target level, 19/19/0): 'Target y has too few observations per class' -> robust; CASE 4: glmnet fit OK with an all-zero column.

### P3.10 [vimpute-helpers] Dropped-predictor warnings (1d12d04) fire once per variable per iteration -- noisy, and the precheck fallback is now inconsistent
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

Each custom learner's .train warns about constant/single-level predictors (R/helper_vimpute.R:70-75, 165-170, 2543-2548, 2632-2637, 2810-2815). Because the sequential loop retrains every learner each iteration, the identical warning repeats nseq x #variables times (and multiplies under m>1, boot, and tuning). Verified: one constant column, 2 NA variables, early convergence after 3 iterations -> 6 identical 'Dropping constant or single-level predictors' warnings wrapped in mlr3 PipeOp noise. Recommendation: detect and warn ONCE in precheck (which already scans predictors -- currently only single-level factors, lines 1156-1177, not numeric constants) and let the learners drop silently, or deduplicate per variable. Related inconsistency: precheck still downgrades gam/robgam to 'robust' whenever ANY single-level factor predictor exists (helper_vimpute.R:1170-1177), although since 1d12d04 the GAM learners handle exactly that case gracefully -- the fallback silently overrides the user's method choice for a solved problem.

**Evidence:** Test run: vimpute(method='gam') with constant numeric column produced 6 duplicate warnings (2 vars x 3 iterations); warning text 'Dropping constant or single-level predictors for 'y': konst / This happened in PipeOp regr.gam_imp's $train()'.

### P3.11 [vimpute-helpers] mlr3 clobbers self$state$feature_names after training: sanitized-feature bookkeeping in all five custom learners is dead
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

All custom learners store the post-sanitization feature set in self$state$feature_names during .train (R/helper_vimpute.R:67, 162, 2540, 2629, 2807) and subset newdata to it in .predict (lines 117, 220, 2575, 2739, 2904). But feature_names is a RESERVED state slot: after .train returns, mlr3's learner_train() overwrites learner$state$feature_names with the full task$feature_names. Verified on the installed build: after training regr.lm_rob on (y, x1, const) where const is dropped, lr$state$feature_names == c('const','x1'). So the predict-time restriction to sanitized features silently never happens; it currently works only because formula-based predict ignores extra columns. Fix: use a non-reserved slot (e.g. self$state$vim_feature_names); factor_levels survives because it is not reserved. Related non-idiomatic pattern: LearnerClassifGlmRob$.train returns invisible(TRUE) (line 205) and keeps models in state$models -- learner$model is then TRUE, breaking model introspection, marshaling and the usual mlr3 contract; return the model list from .train like the GAM learners do.

**Evidence:** Empirical: lrn('regr.lm_rob')$train(task with const col); state$feature_names == c('const','x1') although .train set it to 'x1'; state$factor_levels survives. mlr3 learner_train inserts feature_names=task$feature_names into state.

**Verifier:** Every element of the claim verified. (1) Code: .train stores the post-sanitization feature set in self$state$feature_names at R/helper_vimpute.R:67 (regr.lm_rob), 162 (classif.glm_rob), 2540 (regr.gam_imp), 2629 (classif.gam_imp), 2807 (regr.robgam_imp), and .predict subsets newdata to that slot at lines 117, 220, 2575, 2739, 2904 (reads at 103, 211, 2566, 2730, 2895). The count 'all five' is exact: the sixth custom learner classif.robgam_imp (line 2922ff) does not use the pattern. (2) Mechanism: deparse of mlr3:::learner_train in the installed mlr3 1.5.0 shows, after .train returns: learner$state = set_class(insert_named(learner$state, list(model = ..., task_hash = task$hash, feature_names = task$feature_names, ...))) — the reserved feature_names slot is unconditionally overwritten with the FULL task feature set; insert_named merges, so non-reserved keys survive. (3) Empirical repro on the pre-installed build: task with features (x1, const) where const is constant; calling private$.train directly sets state$feature_names == 'x1' (sanitized), but after lr$train(task) state$feature_names == c('const','x1') — clobbered — while state$factor_levels and state$used_fallback survive, exactly as claimed. Fitted model formula is y ~ x1 and lr$predict(task) succeeds, confirming the predict-time restriction is dead code that is currently masked because formula-based predict ignores extra columns (no user-visible misbehavior today; latent bug — P3 is a fair severity). (4) Secondary sub-claim also confirmed: LearnerClassifGlmRob$.train ends with invisible(TRUE) at R/helper_vimpute.R:205, and after training learner$model is TRUE (class logical) with the fitted models only in state$models — model introspection via learner$model is broken and the usual mlr3 contract (return the model from .train) is violated, though prediction remains functional since .predict reads state$models. The suggested fix (non-reserved slot such as state$vim_feature_names; return the model list from .train as the GAM learners do) is sound given insert_named's merge semantics.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(mlr3); library(VIM); VIM:::register_robust_learners(); set.seed(1); d <- data.frame(y = rnorm(40), x1 = rnorm(40), const = 1); task <- TaskRegr$new("t", d, target = "y"); lr2 <- lrn("regr.lm_rob"); invisible(suppressWarnings(environment(lr2$train)$private$.train(task))); cat("set by .train:", lr2$state$feature_names, "\n"); lr <- lrn("regr.lm_rob"); suppressWarnings(lr$train(task)); cat("after learner_train:", lr$state$feature_names, "| factor_levels NULL?", is.null(lr$state$factor_levels), "\n")'  # Output: 'set by .train: x1' vs 'after learner_train: const x1 | factor_levels NULL? FALSE'. Full script (incl. classif.glm_rob model==TRUE and mlr3:::learner_train source dump): /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/check_state.R

### P3.12 [vimpute-helpers] param_set gaps: dead ridge_lambda, classif.glm_rob has no hyperparameters, min_unique lower bound 2 guarantees failure
*kind: param-extension | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

(a) LearnerRegrRobustLM declares ridge_lambda (R/helper_vimpute.R:24, 49) and passes it into do.call(robustbase::lmrob.control, pv) (line 78); lmrob.control silently swallows it via '...' (verified: control builds, no warning) -- the parameter suggests ridge regularization that never happens and misleads tuning users. (b) LearnerClassifGlmRob (lines 133-146) defines NO param_set at all, so glmrob's method/tcc/maxit are unreachable and any learner_params supplied for robust classification of factor targets are discarded with 'Missing in Pipeline' warnings -- a direct hole in the per-variable hyperparameter-flexibility pillar (regression targets get 13 params, classification zero). (c) The GAM learners allow min_unique lower=2L (lines 2518, 2599, 2776, 2928) but build_gam_formula (lines 2432-2446) then emits s(x, k=3) for columns with only 2-3 unique values, which mgcv rejects ('fewer unique covariate combinations than df') and the WHOLE model falls back to lm/glm -- lower bound should be 3L (matching the tuning space at line 2400) and the doc comment 'mgcv needs at least k=3 knots' (line 2428).

**Evidence:** do.call(robustbase::lmrob.control, pv) with ridge_lambda returns a valid control silently (tested); glm_rob super$initialize has no param_set argument; ps lower=2L vs k=max(3L, n_unique-1L) mismatch.

### P3.13 [vimpute-helpers] Hidden global state: learners registered into the session-global mlr3 dictionary on every call, unprefixed, never cleaned up
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/helper_vimpute.R*

register_robust_learners()/register_gam_learners() run on every vimpute() call that needs them (R/vimpute.R:355-360, plus ensure_robust_learners at 377-384) and mutate the session-global mlr3::mlr_learners dictionary (R/helper_vimpute.R:131, 258, 2590, 2767, 2919, 3098). The generic ids (regr.lm_rob, classif.glm_rob, regr.gam_imp, ...) carry no VIM namespace, so any user- or third-party-registered learner with the same id is silently replaced, and VIM's learners remain globally visible after vimpute() returns (leaking package internals into the user's mlr3 session). The R6 class generators are also rebuilt from scratch inside the function body on each call. Recommendation: register once (memoised flag or mlr3 registration hook) under 'vim.'-prefixed ids (e.g. regr.vim_lmrob), or construct the learners directly from package-level R6 generators without touching the global dictionary at all -- vimpute() controls learner construction, so dictionary registration is not actually required.

**Evidence:** mlr3::mlr_learners$add calls at helper_vimpute.R:131, 258, 2590, 2767, 2919, 3098; per-call invocation at vimpute.R:355-360; ids persist in mlr_learners after the call.

### P3.14 [vimmi-mi] complete.vimmi/with.vimmi convention gaps vs mice, silent skip masking inconsistent objects, and undocumented imp_var suppression for m>1
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimmi.R*

Three smaller polish items on the mice-parity front. (1) complete.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:115-156) supports action = k/'all'/'long' but not mice's action=0 (original data), 'broad'/'repeated', or the include argument (long format with .imp=0 block, which is what mice::as.mids consumes — users hand-rolling the long path will trip on this); .imp/.id are appended as last columns whereas mice puts them first (cosmetic but breaks positional code ported from mice). (2) reconstruct_one silently skips a variable when ncol(imp_df) < mi (R/vimmi.R:122 'if (is.null(imp_df) || ncol(imp_df) < mi) next') — a malformed vimmi object then yields a completed dataset that still contains NAs with no error; this should stop() since it always indicates corruption. (3) For m>1 the recursion hardcodes imp_var=FALSE (R/vimpute.R:437), so a user's imp_var=TRUE is silently ignored and neither the vimmi object nor complete() carries the _imp indicator columns; either document this in @param imp_var/@param m or reconstruct indicators in complete.vimmi from the where matrix (trivial, since where is stored). Positive note recorded during verification: with.vimmi's eval(call_expr, envir=d, enclos=parent.frame()) respects the with() contract, and mice::pool accepts its plain-list output — pooled results were numerically identical to the with(mids,...) path.

**Evidence:** R/vimmi.R:115-156 (action handling, no include/0), R/vimmi.R:122 (silent skip), R/vimmi.R:148-149 (.imp/.id appended last), R/vimpute.R:437 (imp_var=FALSE hardcoded in m>1 recursion). t2_mids.R verified pool-path equivalence.

### P3.15 [cellwise] Engine documentation overclaims: shooting-s is a heuristic, not the cited Oellerer et al. (2016) algorithm; imputeCellMM's 'S-step on unweighted data' actually passes weights into lmrob
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: medium | file: R/imputeCellReg.R*

R/imputeCellReg.R:36-38 documents engine 'shooting-s' as 'Shooting S-estimator (Oellerer et al. 2016). Iterates between cellwise detection and S-estimation. Implemented from the published algorithm.' The implementation (.engine_shooting_s, :328-402) is instead a single global lmrob.S fit followed by at most 5 rounds of an ad-hoc flagging rule (|contribution|/sigma > 3 AND |r|/sigma > 2), zeroing flagged cells and refitting — there is no coordinate-descent ('shooting') structure of per-coordinate S-regressions as in the cited paper. For a methods package this claim should be softened to 'heuristic inspired by' or the published algorithm implemented. Similarly, imputeCellMM's docs promise 'S-step on unweighted data (high breakdown), M-step with cell weights' (R/imputeCellMM.R:3-6, echoed in the comment at :86-88), but the code passes cell-derived row weights into robustbase::lmrob for the whole MM fit (weights = w_row at :99), so the S-step is not unweighted and the stated breakdown-preservation argument does not hold as described. Either implement the documented two-stage scheme (unweighted lmrob.S init, weighted M-refinement — the machinery exists in cellIRWLS) or fix the docs.

**Evidence:** Code structure at R/imputeCellReg.R:350-402 (global lmrob.S + threshold flags u_k>3 & |r/sigma|>2, max_shooting=5); weights passed to lmrob at R/imputeCellMM.R:99 despite 'unweighted' claim at :86-88.

### P3.16 [classic-integration] kNN(weights="auto"): wrong subset when dist_var is a list - target can enter its own importance model
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: medium | file: R/kNN.R*

R/kNN.R:327 in the weights="auto" branch reads regressors <- dist_var[[i]][dist_var!=variable[i]] - it compares the whole LIST dist_var (element-wise as.character of each vector) against the target name instead of dist_var[[i]]. The correct pattern is used two lines below for the vector case (:330, dist_var[dist_var!=variable[i]]). Consequence: when dist_var is a list whose i-th element contains variable[i] (natural when reusing one predictor set), the comparison is TRUE for every list element, the logical index recycles over dist_var[[i]], the target survives into regressors, and ranger fits y ~ y + ... - its importance for y dominates, so the 'auto' Gower weights are driven by the target itself (and the target column is added to dist_var_new for distance computation). Runs without any error (verified), i.e. silently wrong weights. Fix: dist_var[[i]][dist_var[[i]]!=variable[i]]. Note recycling can also error when lengths mismatch non-multiply.

**Evidence:** Code contrast kNN.R:327 vs :330; verified kNN(sleep, variable=c("NonD","Dream"), dist_var=list(c("NonD","BodyWgt","BrainWgt"), c("BodyWgt","Span")), weights="auto") completes without error (silent path).

**Verifier:** Verified by code reading and empirical reproduction against the pre-installed build. R/kNN.R:327 (weights=="auto" AND is.list(dist_var) branch) reads `regressors <- dist_var[[i]][dist_var!=variable[i]]`. The RHS index compares the WHOLE list `dist_var` (not `dist_var[[i]]`) to the scalar target name; R coerces each list element to its deparsed string (e.g. 'c("NonD", "BodyWgt", "BrainWgt")'), which never equals the plain name 'NonD', so `dist_var != variable[i]` returns c(TRUE, TRUE). That all-TRUE logical is silently recycled over the length-3 vector `dist_var[[i]]`, selecting EVERY element including the target. Verified: `dist_var[[1]][dist_var != "NonD"]` = c("NonD","BodyWgt","BrainWgt") whereas the intended `dist_var[[1]][dist_var[[1]] != "NonD"]` = c("BodyWgt","BrainWgt"). Consequently ranger (kNN.R:334-337) fits `NonD ~ NonD + BodyWgt + BrainWgt`; the target's own impurity importance dominates (0.52 of total on the sleep data, ~0.70 on a 300-row synthetic set) and becomes the 'auto' Gower weight, while kNN.R:336 (`dist_var_new[[i]] <- regressors`) also adds the target column itself as a distance variable for imputing itself. The vector branch two lines below (kNN.R:330, `dist_var[dist_var!=variable[i]]`) uses the correct pattern, confirming line 327 is a copy/paste omission of the `[[i]]` subscript. The path is silent (no error/warning) and untested (no tinytest references weights="auto"). Impact demonstrated: applying the one-token fix (`dist_var[[i]][dist_var[[i]] != variable[i]]`) changes ALL 30 imputed NonD cells (max abs diff 4.27 on a target with residual SD ~1) - materially wrong output, not cosmetic. Trigger is narrow (needs weights="auto" AND dist_var passed as a list AND the i-th list element containing variable[i], natural when reusing one predictor set), consistent with the P3/medium rating; vector dist_var and the default (vector) dist_var are unaffected.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); dv <- list(c("NonD","BodyWgt","BrainWgt"), c("BodyWgt","Span")); print(dv[[1]][dv != "NonD"]); print(dv[[1]][dv[[1]] != "NonD"])'  # -> buggy selects c("NonD","BodyWgt","BrainWgt") (target NonD included), intended selects c("BodyWgt","BrainWgt"). Full run kNN(sleep, variable=c("NonD","Dream"), dist_var=dv, weights="auto") completes silently; ranger formula becomes NonD ~ NonD + BodyWgt + BrainWgt with importance(NonD)/sum = 0.52. Patching line 327 flips all 30 imputed NonD cells (max abs diff 4.27) on a synthetic MCAR set. Scripts: /private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/verify_knn_auto.R and verify_knn_fix2.R

### P3.17 [classic-integration] imp_var/imp_suffix bookkeeping diverges across the eight functions - extract one shared helper
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/kNN.R*

Five different semantics coexist: (1) kNN updates existing <var>_<suffix> columns cumulatively (converts to logical, ORs new TRUEs, warns; R/kNN.R:170-188) and creates flag columns for every requested variable; (2) hotdeck creates flags unconditionally with no existing-column check (hotdeck.R:115-122) - rerunning on already-flagged data appends the name a second time via setnames, and prior status is reset; (3) irmi adds flags only for variables that HAD missings (irmi.R:216-221) with no collision handling; (4) the new wrappers rangerImpute/xgboostImpute/regressionImp overwrite any pre-existing flag with vimpute's fresh one, losing prior TRUEs despite emitting kNN's 'will be updated' warning (rangerImpute.R:87-98, xgboostImpute.R:90-98, regressionImp.R:133-142); (5) imputeRobust/imputeRobustChain have no imp_var support at all, and vimpute() hardcodes suffix "_imp" with no imp_suffix argument (vimpute.R:78-79), which is why every wrapper needs the fragile <var>_imp -> <var>_<suffix> rename dance. Proposal: a single internal helper update_imp_flags(data, targets, na_index, imp_suffix, cumulative=TRUE) used by all functions, plus an imp_suffix parameter on vimpute() for parity.

**Evidence:** Cited line ranges in all six files; verified hotdeck(hotdeck(sleep, variable="NonD"), variable="NonD") silently resets/duplicates flag handling while kNN warns and ORs.

### P3.18 [classic-integration] rangerImpute/xgboostImpute dropped all hyperparameter passthrough; xgboostImpute docs contradict behavior
*kind: param-extension | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/rangerImpute.R*

rangerImpute now warns 'Additional ranger arguments are ignored' for any ... (verified with num.trees=500; R/rangerImpute.R:30-33), and xgboostImpute ignores nrounds, objective and ... (xgboostImpute.R:43-46) while its roxygen still claims 'argument passed to [xgboost::xgboost()]' for nrounds/objective/... (:9-16) and the title still says 'based on a random forest model'. This is a needless functionality regression: vimpute() already accepts exactly these via learner_params per method and validates them against the mlr3 param_set (vimpute.R:921-983). Fix is ~5 lines per wrapper: learner_params = list(ranger = c(list(predict_median = median), dots)) and list(xgboost = c(list(nrounds = nrounds, objective = objective), dots)); then update the docs. Also cosmetic: both wrappers use cat() for the 'No missings in X.' notice (rangerImpute.R:43, xgboostImpute.R:52) where every other VIM function uses message() - cat cannot be suppressed.

**Evidence:** Verified warning: rangerImpute(Dream~BodyWgt+BrainWgt, sleep, num.trees=500) -> 'Additional ranger arguments are ignored'; xgboostImpute.R doc lines 13-16 vs warning at 44-46; vimpute.R:951-978 shows ranger_params merging from learner_params.

### P3.19 [tests] Tautological assertion in test_cellwise.R all-NA-column test cannot fail; behavior for all-NA columns is unpinned across the package
*kind: test-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/inst/tinytest/test_cellwise.R*

test_cellwise.R:243-248 wraps imputeCellIRMI in tryCatch(..., error=function(e) e) and then asserts expect_true(inherits(res_allna,"list") || inherits(res_allna,"error")) — tryCatch can only ever yield the list result or the error object, so the assertion is always TRUE and the package's all-NA-column contract is untested everywhere (vimpute has no all-NA test either). Related quality skim: test_cellwise.R:207 uses a loose mse<5 bound where the true relation is noise-free (sigma of normalerror is small; <1 would still be safe); test_vimpute.R retains commented-out testthat scaffolding from mechanical conversion (e.g. lines 3, 12), so tinytest reports assertions without test names — cosmetic but hampers triage. PROPOSED TEST 9: replace the tautology by pinning actual behavior — run imputeCellIRMI(df_allna, maxit=3, trace=FALSE) once, decide the contract, then either expect_error(..., <message>) or expect_false(any(is.na(res$data_imputed))) unconditionally; add the twin for vimpute: d$dead <- NA_real_; expect_error(vimpute(d, method="ranger", sequential=FALSE), <informative message>) so users get a clear error, not an mlr3 traceback.

**Evidence:** inst/tinytest/test_cellwise.R:243-254 (res_allna is necessarily list-or-error; both branches accepted), :207 (mse < 5 tolerance); inst/tinytest/test_vimpute.R:3,12 (testthat remnants); grep shows no all-NA-column test for vimpute

### P3.20 [tests] vimpute() degenerate-input matrix untested: zero-variance column, n<p regularized, single missing cell, unseen factor level
*kind: test-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

None of the classic breakage inputs for an mlr3-backed pipeline is tested, so failures surface as cryptic learner errors instead of clear VIM errors (directly against the USABILITY pillar). PROPOSED TEST 10 (one file, four cases): (a) zero variance: d$const <- 1; d$y[3] <- NA; vimpute(d, method="regularized", ...) — pin either success or an informative error mentioning the column; (b) n<p: 8 rows x 12 numeric cols with a few NAs, method="regularized" (cv.glmnet needs enough folds — expect informative error or fallback, not a glmnet traceback); (c) single missing cell in one column with pmm=TRUE (donor pool edge, k>n_donors); (d) unseen factor level: factor predictor where level "C" occurs only in the rows whose target is NA — train set never sees "C"; assert no crash and imputed values valid (this is the classic mlr3 'new levels' failure mode; issue-98 test covers missing-target construction but not unseen levels). Each case should assert the error MESSAGE is VIM's own (expect_error(..., "VIM|vimpute|column")) rather than merely expect_error(...), so wrapping regressions are caught.

**Evidence:** grep over inst/tinytest/test_vimpute*.R shows no zero-variance/const column, no n<p fixture (all fixtures are sleep with n=62 or n>=40 frames), no single-missing-cell case, no unseen-level construction; error tests present are only arg-validation (test_vimpute.R:95-112, :164-183)

### P3.22 [api-consistency] Surface conventions split by era: verbose vs trace (impPCA defaults verbose=TRUE, wrappers cat() unconditionally), x vs data first-arg, variable vs considered_variables, and vimpute hardcodes the _imp suffix
*kind: refactor | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/impPCA.R*

Progress control: `trace` in kNN, irmi, imputeRobustChain and all imputeCell* vs `verbose` in vimpute, rangerImpute, xgboostImpute and impPCA — and impPCA alone defaults verbose=TRUE (R/impPCA.R:61), while rangerImpute/xgboostImpute print 'No missings in X.' via cat() regardless of verbose (R/rangerImpute.R:44, R/xgboostImpute.R:52), which is neither suppressible nor sink-safe; use message() gated on verbose. First arg is `data` everywhere except irmi/impPCA/prepare/initialise (`x`). Variable selection is `variable` (kNN default colnames(data), hotdeck default NULL meaning all — two different idioms for 'all') vs vimpute's verbose `considered_variables`. vimpute exposes imp_var but not imp_suffix — the indicator name is hardcoded paste0(var, "_imp") (R/vimpute.R:862), so kNN(imp_suffix="flag") code cannot migrate. Function-name style (kNN/hotdeck/irmi vs rangerImpute vs regressionImp vs imputeCell* vs vimpute) is not worth renaming exports over; instead position vimpute() as the documented front door (irmi already warns 'deprecated, use vimpute()', R/irmi.R:123 with lifecycle note at :13) and align its surface: accept `variables` (with considered_variables as alias), add imp_suffix="imp", standardise on verbose (accept trace as alias in legacy functions), and flip impPCA's default to FALSE at the next minor release with a NEWS entry.

**Evidence:** Formals across installed build: trace in 8 functions, verbose in 4; impPCA verbose=TRUE (R/impPCA.R:61); unconditional cat() at R/rangerImpute.R:44 and R/xgboostImpute.R:52; x-first in irmi/impPCA/prepare/initialise; vimpute(considered_variables=names(data)) vs kNN(variable=colnames(data)) vs hotdeck(variable=NULL); hardcoded imp_col <- paste0(var, "_imp") at R/vimpute.R:862 with no imp_suffix formal.

### P3.26 [mice] Count-data imputation (Poisson/NB)
*kind: method-gap (vs countimp (mice extension); mice itself lacks it too) | verdict: REFUTED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Counts treated as generic regression targets.

PROPOSAL: Extend the existing LearnerRegrGlmRob to family = poisson (robustbase::glmrob supports it) → robust Poisson imputation, which NOBODY else offers — turns a shared gap into a differentiator.

REFERENCE: helper_vimpute.R:138-258

**Verifier:** VIM already has count-data imputation, including the robust Poisson variant the proposal presents as new: irmi() takes a count argument (R/irmi.R:24, 110) and imputes count responses via useGLMcount (R/irmi.R:847-869), which fits robustbase::glmrob(form, family=poisson) when robust=TRUE (irmi.R:865) and glm(family=poisson) otherwise (irmi.R:869), with digit-preserving rounding (irmi.R:284-306). Functionally verified: irmi(d, count='y') imputes integer-consistent values. So 'robust Poisson imputation, which NOBODY else offers' already exists inside VIM. Caveats making the underlying improvement still sensible: vimpute() does treat counts as generic regression targets (no count method there), and irmi() is deprecated in 7.1.0 (warning at irmi.R:123) — porting count support to vimpute (e.g. via LearnerRegrGlmRob family=poisson) would preserve a capability that otherwise dies with irmi. But the claim 'Counts treated as generic regression targets' is false at package level.

**Repro:** Rscript: d <- data.frame(y=rpois(150,3), x1=rnorm(150), x2=rnorm(150)); d$y[1:20] <- NA; r <- irmi(d, count='y'); all(r$y == round(r$y))  # TRUE; sed -n '847,869p' R/irmi.R

### P3.30 [methodology-docs] Nonexistent journal name 'Journal of Computational Statistics and Data Analysis' in 5 man pages
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: R/irmi.R*

The 2011 IRMI paper is in Computational Statistics & Data Analysis 55(10):2793-2806, but five roxygen blocks cite '*Journal of Computational Statistics and Data Analysis*': R/irmi.R:62-63, R/evaluation.R:15-16, R/imputeCellEM.R:122-124, R/imputeCellwise.R:557-558 (imputeCellM), R/VIM-package.R:630-631. R/imputeCellwise.R:86-87 (imputeCellIRMI) cites it correctly, so the package is internally inconsistent about its own flagship reference. One-line fix in each block, then devtools::document().

**Evidence:** grep output: five files with 'Journal of\nComputational Statistics and Data Analysis'; correct form at R/imputeCellwise.R:86 '\emph{Computational Statistics & Data Analysis}, \strong{55}(10), 2793--2806'.

**Verifier:** All five claimed source locations verified verbatim in the working tree: R/irmi.R:62-63, R/evaluation.R:15-16, R/imputeCellEM.R:123-124, R/imputeCellwise.R:557-558 (imputeCellM block), and R/VIM-package.R:630-631 all cite the 2011 IRMI paper as '*Journal of Computational Statistics and Data Analysis*' (markdown) or '\emph{Journal of Computational Statistics and Data Analysis}' (Rd markup), line-wrapped after 'Journal of' (which is why a single-line grep misses it). The error propagates to exactly five built man pages: man/irmi.Rd:152-153, man/evaluation.Rd:54-55, man/imputeCellEM.Rd:171-172, man/imputeCellM.Rd:98-99, man/VIM-package.Rd:53-54. No journal of that name exists: the paper (Templ, Kowarik, Filzmoser 2011, 'Iterative stepwise regression imputation using standard and robust methods') appeared in Computational Statistics & Data Analysis (CSDA, Elsevier), 55(10), 2793-2806, DOI 10.1016/j.csda.2011.04.012 (the 'csda' journal code in the DOI confirms the venue). Internal inconsistency confirmed: R/imputeCellwise.R:84-87 (imputeCellIRMI) cites the same paper correctly as '\emph{Computational Statistics & Data Analysis}, \strong{55}(10), 2793--2806', and R/impPCA.R:19 also cites CSDA without the spurious prefix. The claim's scope is precise — the other two 'Journal of' line-break hits (R/kNN.R, R/hotdeck.R, plus the second hit in R/irmi.R) are 'Journal of Statistical Software', which is a real journal correctly cited. Side observation for whoever fixes this (same error class, beyond this claim's scope): '*Journal of Advances in Data Analysis and Classification*' appears in 19 R files (e.g. R/aggr.R:70-72, R/bgmap.R:24-26, R/VIM-package.R:625-627); the actual Springer journal is 'Advances in Data Analysis and Classification' (ADAC) with no 'Journal of' prefix, so a fix pass should correct both patterns, then run devtools::document().

**Repro:** grep -rn -A1 'Journal of$' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/*.R | grep -B1 'Computational Statistics and Data Analysis'  # shows the 5 source locations; grep -rn -A1 'Journal of$' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/man/ | grep -B1 'Computational Statistics and Data Analysis'  # shows the 5 built Rd files; sed -n '82,90p' /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/imputeCellwise.R  # shows the correct 'Computational Statistics & Data Analysis' form in the imputeCellIRMI block

### P3.31 [methodology-docs] imputeCellEM.Rd contradicts itself: pseudo-likelihood called 'the observed-data log-likelihood' in Details step 4
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/imputeCellEM.R*

Details step 4 (R/imputeCellEM.R:77-79) says 'The observed-data log-likelihood (sum of per-variable conditional mixture log-likelihoods) is tracked for diagnostics', while the @return entry for pseudo_loglik (lines 35-39) and the later Details paragraph (lines 86-90) correctly and explicitly state this quantity is a composite (pseudo) log-likelihood and 'not the proper observed-data joint log-likelihood'. Same Rd, opposite claims — a reader deciding whether AIC/BIC or likelihood-ascent checks are legitimate gets both answers. Fix step 4 to 'composite pseudo-log-likelihood' (and the example comment '# Log-likelihood trace' at line 142). The convergence-by-stability design itself is documented correctly and is not at issue.

**Evidence:** R/imputeCellEM.R:77-79 vs 35-39 and 86-90 (quoted in both directions); example lines 142-144 mix 'Log-likelihood trace' comment with ylab 'Pseudo log-likelihood'.

*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

(b) Line 445: 'only possible if seq = TRUE' — the argument is `sequential`; moreover with sequential=FALSE, nseq is forced to 1 (R/vimpute.R:326-329) and tuning triggers at i == round(nseq/2) = 0 (vimpute.R:1202), i.e. tune is silently skipped with no warning — docs should state it is ignored (or code should warn). (c) Line 64: 'there are 9 rows wich contain a missing in both NonD and Dream' — 9 is the count of the exact pattern {NonD, Dream} only; rows with both missing number 12 (verified); the sentence conflates the aggr pattern count with the joint missing count. ### P3.33 [methodology-docs] 'Performance' section: displayed missingness differs from the data actually imputed; 'validate' overstated with no error metric
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

The visible NA-generation chunk (vimpute.Rmd:527-532) uses col=sample(ncol(iris)-1) (numeric columns only, Species never NA) and its aggr plot + sapply NA counts are shown; but the hidden chunk that actually produces the results tables (lines 556-560) regenerates NAs with col=sample(ncol(df)) (Species included), so the displayed missingness summary describes a different dataset than the one imputed. Also 'In order to validate the performance of vimpute()' is overstated: output is just the first 5 true-vs-imputed pairs per variable, with no error metric — although VIM ships nrmse/msecor etc. in R/evaluation.R — no repetition over seeds, and no benchmark (kNN/irmi/mice). A statistician's fix: use evaluation metrics, note that point-recovery of true values is not the criterion for MI validity (distributional/inferential validity is), and either align the two chunks or drop the hidden one.

**Evidence:** vimpute.Rmd:529-530 `col=sample(ncol(iris)-1,...)` (visible) vs 557-558 `col = sample(ncol(df), ...)` (hidden, include=FALSE, actually imputed); section header 'Performance' line 517; R/evaluation.R provides nrmse/msecor but is unused in the vignette.

### P3.34 [usability] tune=TRUE silently changes the return type to an unclassed list, and the tuning log records nothing useful
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

tres <- vimpute(sleep, tune=TRUE) returns class 'list' with names data, tuning_log (16.2s, no progress output). Any code written for the normal case (a data.table) breaks when the user toggles tune; there is no class, no print method, and printing dumps everything. Worse, the tuning log is content-free: each entry is only list(variable=<name>, tuned_better=<logical>) (vimpute.R:1425-1428) — the tuned hyperparameter values and the CV scores that were computed (vimpute.R:1278-1279) are discarded, so the user cannot learn what tuning chose or how much it helped. Since tuning is the headline differentiator vs mice, the log should contain chosen params + default-vs-tuned scores, and the result should keep the normal return shape (log as attribute or in a proper result class).

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:1425-1428, :1278-1279. Commands: tres <- vimpute(sleep, tune=TRUE) -> class list, names data,tuning_log; str(tres$tuning_log) -> each element 'List of 2: $variable chr, $tuned_better logi' only.

### P3.35 [usability] Post-imputation diagnostics exist and work but are undiscoverable from ?vimpute/?vimmi
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/man/vimpute.Rd*

What a user can actually do after vimpute(): aggr(imp, delimiter="_imp") and matrixplot(imp, delimiter="_imp") work on the output (verified); mice::densityplot(as.mids.vimmi(res)) gives MI density diagnostics (verified, returns trellis); evaluation()/nrmse()/msecor()/pfc() are exported for simulation studies. None of this is reachable from the docs a new user reads: ?vimpute's See Also (man/vimpute.Rd:197-217) lists only the other imputation functions, no plotting/evaluation function, and never mentions the _imp/delimiter convention that VIM's whole visualization suite keys on; ?vimmi advertises as.mids.vimmi for pooling but not for mice's plot diagnostics; methods(class="vimmi") is only complete/print/summary/with (no plot method). mice's ?mice points to plot.mids/densityplot/stripplot. One @seealso block + one example line ('aggr(imp, delimiter="_imp")') would close most of the gap; a plot.vimmi wrapping the as.mids bridge would close it fully.

**Evidence:** man/vimpute.Rd:197-217 (See Also = imputation methods only). Commands verified working but undocumented: aggr(imp, delimiter="_imp") OK; matrixplot(imp, delimiter="_imp") OK; mice::densityplot(as.mids.vimmi(res5)) -> trellis; getNamespaceExports grep -> msecor, evaluation, nrmse, pfc; methods(class="vimmi") -> complete, print, summary, with.

### P3.36 [usability] A single all-NA column degrades every other variable to 'simple fallback imputation' and the fatal error only fires late
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimpute.R*

sl2 <- sleep; sl2$allna <- NA_real_; vimpute(sl2, sequential=FALSE) first emits 'No observed values for target 'NonD'/'Dream'/'Sleep'/'Span'/'Gest' after donor filtering. Using simple fallback imputation.' for ALL five normal variables, then errors on allna. Two problems: (1) training data is complete-case (na.omit(data[donor_mask[[target]]]), vimpute.R:560), so one all-NA column empties every variable's donor pool — the misleading warnings blame 'donor filtering' though the user set no donorcond; (2) the (excellently worded) all-NA error is raised only when that variable's turn comes, after computation on all preceding variables is wasted — it should be an upfront validation check before iteration starts. Also 'simple fallback imputation' is documented nowhere, so users can't know what values they got (same fallback fires on over-restrictive donorcond, e.g. donorcond=list(Sleep=">1000"), where the warning itself is reasonable).

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:843-858 (fallback + late stop), :560 (na.omit donor pool). Command: sl2$allna <- NA_real_; vimpute(sl2, sequential=FALSE) -> 5x 'No observed values for target ... Using simple fallback imputation.' warnings + error "Variable 'allna' contains only missing values. No model can be estimated. Please remove it from 'considered_variables' or impute it externally."

### P3.37 [framework-design] No seed argument and machine-dependent knobs undermine MI reproducibility claims; regularized re-runs candidate CV every iteration
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: medium | file: R/vimpute.R*

Same-seed same-machine runs are reproducible (verified for untuned ranger), but the framework has no `seed` argument (mice(seed=)) — MI users must know to set.seed() externally, and nothing records the seed in the vimmi object for provenance. Cross-machine reproducibility is broken by two detectCores()-derived values: tuner batch_size (vimpute.R:1263, 1354) changes the random-search evaluation stream, and optimal_threads (vimpute.R:900-907) feeds xgboost nthread, whose results can differ across thread counts. Separately, a performance wart with statistical side-effects: for method='regularized' with numeric targets, learner_candidates has 2 entries (cv_glmnet, glmnet; vimpute.R:708-715), so a full 5-fold CV comparison of both learners runs for EVERY variable in EVERY iteration in EVERY of the m imputations (vimpute.R:1101-1135) — the winner can flip between iterations, and the cost is nseq x m x 2 CV runs that a once-per-variable decision would avoid. Proposed contract: `vimpute(..., seed = NULL)` doing withr-style RNG scoping and storing seed in the result/vimmi; fixed batch_size = 1L default; cache the candidate-selection verdict per variable in the same cache as hyperparameters (it already exists: hyperparameter_cache, vimpute.R:499).

**Evidence:** vimpute.R:154-176 no seed parameter; vimpute.R:1263 `batch <- max(1, parallel::detectCores() - 1)`; vimpute.R:1101-1135 candidate CV inside the `for (i in seq_len(nseq))` x `for (var in variables_NA)` loops; verified same-seed same-machine identical

### P3.38 [formulas] maxCat/sampleCat weighted aggregation uses count x sum(weights), not the weighted mode / weighted probabilities
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: medium | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/maxCat.R*

In the weighted branch, both functions score each level as s = tmpTab$prob * tmpTab$x = (level count) x (sum of weights in that level) (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/maxCat.R:18-22; /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/sampleCat.R:18-22). The standard distance-weighted mode is argmax over the sum of weights per level; multiplying by the count again double-counts frequency (score = count^2 x mean weight), so a level carried by many low-weight (distant) donors beats a level carried by fewer high-weight (near) donors. This contradicts the contract implied by ?kNN's weightDist ('distances ... used as weights in the aggregation step', R/kNN.R:96-97), and is inconsistent with the ordinal path, which correctly uses laeken::weightedMedian (R/medianSamp.R:19). Neither ?maxCat ('chooses the level with the most occurrences', maxCat.R:3-4) nor ?sampleCat documents the weighted formula. Fix: score by per-level weight sums alone (s <- tapply(weights, x, sum)) and document; keep random tie-break.

**Evidence:** Reproduced: maxCat(factor(c("A","A","A","B")), weights=c(.1,.1,.1,.8)) returned "A" in 200/200 draws (scores A: 3x0.3=0.9, B: 1x0.8=0.8) although the weighted mode is B (0.8 > 0.3). Formula: R/maxCat.R:19-21 and R/sampleCat.R:19-21.

**Verifier:** Code reading confirms the formula: R/maxCat.R:19-21 and R/sampleCat.R:19-21 build tmpTab by merging aggregate(weights,list(x),sum) (per-level weight sum, column 'x') with the summary counts (column 'prob'), then score s <- tmpTab$prob*tmpTab$x = count x sum(weights) per level. Empirical repro on the installed 7.1.0 build: maxCat(factor(c('A','A','A','B')), weights=c(.1,.1,.1,.8)) returned 'A' in 500/500 draws (scores A=3x0.3=0.9, B=1x0.8=0.8) although the standard weighted mode is B (weight sums 0.8 > 0.3); sampleCat over 50,000 draws gave empirical probs A=0.5283/B=0.4717, matching the count-x-weightsum prediction (0.5294/0.4706) and far from weight-proportional sampling (0.2727/0.7273). This is the live kNN path: a probe catFun confirmed kNN(..., weightDist=TRUE) passes per-donor 1-dist weights to catFun (R/kNN.R:425-429), so a level carried by many distant donors beats one carried by fewer near donors, contradicting the plain reading of ?kNN weightDist ('distances ... used as weights in the aggregation step', R/kNN.R:96-97). Refutation attempts failed: ?maxCat documents only 'chooses the level with the most occurrences' (no weighted formula anywhere); the tinytest fixture (inst/tinytest/test_aggFunctions.R:20) cannot discriminate the formulas (level F wins under both count-x-weightsum and weight-sum scoring, verified by hand); the ordinal counterpart medianSamp uses the proper laeken::weightedMedian (R/medianSamp.R:19); git history (ac9ff96/b1519e6, split from kNNFaster.R in 2020) gives no rationale. Supporting detail: if aggregate had used mean instead of sum, prob*x would equal exactly the per-level weight sum (the correct weighted mode), consistent with an implementation slip. Severity is correctly rated P3: it only biases weighted categorical aggregation toward majority levels; the proposed fix (score by tapply(weights,x,sum), keep random tie-break, document) is sound.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); x <- factor(c("A","A","A","B")); w <- c(.1,.1,.1,.8); print(table(replicate(500, maxCat(x, w)))); set.seed(42); print(prop.table(table(replicate(50000, sampleCat(x, w)))))' -> maxCat: A 500/500 (weighted mode is B); sampleCat: A 0.5283 / B 0.4717 == count*weightsum prediction (0.5294/0.4706), not weight-proportional (0.2727/0.7273).

### P3.39 [formulas] msecov/msecor: undocumented denominator (divides by p, not p^2) and NA exactly when imputation is worst (constant column)
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R*

msecov and msecor compute sum((cov(x)-cov(y))^2)/ncol(x) and sum((cor(x)-cor(y))^2)/ncol(x) (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/evaluation.R:77-86). The names say 'mean squared error' but the sum runs over all p^2 matrix entries (diagonal included, off-diagonals double-counted) and is divided by p only — neither the sum, nor the mean over p^2 entries, nor the mean over the p(p-1)/2 unique correlations. No formula is documented anywhere in the Rd, so users cannot know which convention applies (the cited Templ/Kowarik/Filzmoser 2011 CSDA paper is not specific enough a pointer). Additionally cor()/cov() are called with the default use="everything": if an imputation collapses a variable to a constant (e.g. mode/median filling), cor() returns NA and msecor returns NA instead of a large error — the metric fails exactly on the worst imputations; any residual NA in x or y also yields NA. Fix: document the formula, divide by the number of compared entries (or restrict to upper triangle), and handle constant columns explicitly (e.g. define the correlation error contribution as maximal or drop with a warning).

**Evidence:** Reproduced: a <- matrix(rnorm(40), ncol=2); b <- a; b[,2] <- 5; msecor(a,b) returns NA (with cor() zero-sd warning suppressed). Code: R/evaluation.R:77-86; Rd gives no formulas (R/evaluation.R:1-32).

### P3.40 [formulas] ?gowerD documents weights as per-observation; code treats them as per-variable
*kind: bug | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R*

The roxygen for gowerD says '@param weights numeric vector providing weights for the observations in x' (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/gowerD.R:8), but the default is rep(1, ncol(data.x)) (line 38), the vector is reordered with the variable permutation weightind (line 92, order(match(colnames(data.x), ...))) and consumed per-variable in the C++ kernel with weightsum = sum over variables (src/gowerD.cpp:46-57). A user following the man page and passing nrow(data.x) weights gets silently wrong distances (the first ncol elements are subset in permuted order, no length check). The ?kNN doc for the same concept is correct ('weights for the variables for distance calculation', R/kNN.R:68). Likely a copy-paste from maxCat/sampleCat/medianSamp where 'weights for the observations' is correct. Fix: correct the @param text and add a length==ncol(data.x) check in gowerD().

**Evidence:** Doc: R/gowerD.R:8 vs default rep(1, ncol(data.x)) at R/gowerD.R:38, per-variable use at R/gowerD.R:92,130-132 and src/gowerD.cpp:46-57 (weightsum accumulated over the weight vector, one weight(k) per column).

**Verifier:** Doc-code mismatch verified at every cited location: R/gowerD.R:8 (and generated man/gowerD.Rd:28) reads '@param weights numeric vector providing weights for the observations in x', but the default is rep(1, ncol(data.x)) (R/gowerD.R:38, per-variable length), the vector is permuted by the variable ordering weightind <- order(match(colnames(data.x), c(numerical,factors,orders,mixed))) (R/gowerD.R:92) and passed as weights[weightind] into the C++ kernel (R/gowerD.R:130,140), which consumes exactly one weight per column with weightsum = accumulate(weight.begin(), weight.end(), 0.0) summed over variables (src/gowerD.cpp:46-57). Empirical repro on the installed build: on a 3-row, 2-column frame, gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0)) vs weights=c(0,1) yield different distance matrices keyed to variable a vs variable b (per-variable semantics demonstrated); passing per-observation-length weights as the man page suggests — gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0,999)) and even weights=c(1,0,-1e6) — raises no error or warning and returns output identical(TRUE) to gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0)), i.e. the extra elements are silently dropped by the weights[weightind] subset, so a doc-following user gets silently wrong distances with no length check. The same concept is documented correctly for kNN ('weights for the variables for distance calculation', R/kNN.R:68), and kNN itself validates length against dist_var (R/kNN.R:344-345) while gowerD has no such check — consistent with the claim that the gowerD @param text was copy-pasted from the aggregation helpers (maxCat/sampleCat/medianSamp all use the identical 'weights for the observations in x' wording, where it is correct). Proposed fix (correct @param text, add length==ncol(data.x) check) is appropriate.

**Repro:** Rscript -e '.libPaths(c("/private/tmp/claude-503/-Users-matthias-workspace-VIM/1cfe2c5c-cdbf-42a1-98c3-9d8450b466d1/scratchpad/Rlib", .libPaths())); library(VIM); d3 <- data.frame(a=c(0,1,2), b=c(0,10,0)); print(gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0))); print(gowerD(d3, weights=c(0,1))); print(identical(gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0,-1e6)), gowerD(d3, weights=c(1,0))))' -> the two 2-element weight vectors give variable-keyed distance matrices; the 3-element (per-observation-length) vector runs without error and is identical(TRUE) to the truncated 2-element call.
