### P4.7 [methodology-docs] Terminology drift: method/model/learner used interchangeably; formula documented as 'named list' though names are ignored
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: vignettes/vimpute.Rmd*

Across the vignette and man pages the same object is a 'method' (arg name, method list), a 'model' (section headings 'Imputation with Default Model', 'different Models for each Variable'), and a 'learner' (learner_params; mlr3 term). Pick one primary term (mlr3 'learner' or 'method') and state the equivalence once. Related API-doc mismatch: vimpute.Rd @param formula says 'Provide as a named list' (R/vimpute.R:58) but names are never used — select_formula (R/helper_vimpute.R:534-546) matches purely on the formula LHS, and the vignette's own example (lines 310-315) passes an unnamed list while another (line 346) passes a named one. Document LHS-matching as the mechanism so users don't assume names control targeting.

**Evidence:** vimpute.Rmd:93 ('Default Model'), 147 ('different Models'), 33/245 (learner_params 'learner-specific'); R/vimpute.R:58 'Provide as a named list' vs helper_vimpute.R:534-546 (Filter on deparse(f[[2]]) — names ignored); unnamed list example vimpute.Rmd:310-315.

### P4.8 [usability] as.mids bridge has an awkward calling convention: as.mids(res) fails two different ways
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimmi.R*

as.mids.vimmi is exported as a plain function (NAMESPACE:15 'export(as.mids.vimmi)') because mice::as.mids is not a generic. The S3-style name invites the natural call as.mids(res), which fails with 'konnte Funktion "as.mids" nicht finden' when mice is not attached, and with mice attached fails inside mice::as.mids with the cryptic 'Imputation index `.imp` not found'. The documented direct call as.mids.vimmi(res) works and returns a proper mids (verified; pooling and densityplot then work). Low-cost fixes: mention explicitly in ?vimmi/?vimpute that as.mids(res) will NOT work, and/or catch vimmi objects earlier (e.g. also export an unambiguous name like vimmi2mids())

**Evidence:** NAMESPACE:15; R/vimmi.R:264-283. Commands: as.mids(res) without mice -> 'konnte Funktion "as.mids" nicht finden'; library(mice); as.mids(res) -> 'Imputation index `.imp` not found'; as.mids.vimmi(res) -> class mids, then mice::pool(with(res, lm(Sleep~Dream+Span))) works.

### P4.9 [formulas] cellIRWLS doc/code mismatches: 'damping' damps psi-weights (not cell weights) and only for method="tukey"; cellWeightsMCD's covMcd alpha=0.75 and fallbacks undocumented
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/cellwise_utils.R*

Three doc/code misalignments in /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/cellwise_utils.R (the weight formulas themselves — Huber 1.345, Tukey 4.685, MAD/IQR-1.349 scale, Schur-complement conditional mean/variance — are all correct): (1) @param damping says 'the cell-weight update is adaptively damped across iterations' (lines 308-309), but the code damps the psi (residual/row) weights — w_cell is a fixed input — and only when method=="tukey" (line 421: if (damping && method == "tukey")); with method="huber" the argument is silently ignored. (2) The Algorithm section says the S-estimator init is used when 'n > 2p' (line 271-272) while the code requires n > 2*(p+1) (line 375: n > 2 * p_int). (3) The exported cellWeightsMCD() hard-codes the MCD subset fraction covMcd(..., alpha = 0.75) (line 175) — undocumented and confusingly named against the function's own `alpha` argument, which is the psi tuning constant — and silently falls back to univariate median/MAD weights when p < 2 || n < 2p (lines 154-164) or when covMcd errors (lines 179-189), and median-imputes NAs before estimating the MCD and the conditional residuals (lines 166-171, 220); none of this is in the man page. Fix: reword the damping doc (psi-weights, tukey-only or extend to huber), align the n>2p condition, and document the MCD fraction, fallbacks and NA pre-imputation in ?cellWeightsMCD.

**Evidence:** Damping doc R/cellwise_utils.R:308-309 vs code 421-424; init doc 271-272 vs code 375; covMcd alpha=0.75 at 175; univariate/error fallbacks 154-164, 179-189; NA median pre-imputation 166-171 with u_j reset at 220-222.

### P4.10 [formulas] kNN silently rounds aggregated values for integer target columns (undocumented, banker's rounding)
*kind: doc-gap | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/kNN.R*

For integer target variables kNN applies round() to the numFun aggregate: round(apply(kNNs,2,numFun)) resp. the weighted analogue (/Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/kNN.R:432-433 and 441-442). ?kNN documents numFun only as 'function for aggregating the k Nearest Neighbours in the case of a numerical variable' (R/kNN.R:71-72) and never mentions that integer columns are treated specially. Consequences a user cannot anticipate from the docs: (a) the imputed value can equal none of the donor values and differ from what numFun returned (median of an even k gives .5 values); (b) R's round() uses round-half-to-even, so e.g. donor medians 2.5 and 3.5 impute 2 and 4; (c) a user-supplied numFun that deliberately returns non-integers (e.g. weighted mean) is silently overridden. Fix: one sentence in ?kNN (and consider type-preserving as.integer(round(...)) documentation), or make the rounding optional.

**Evidence:** Rounding branches at R/kNN.R:432-433 (weighted) and 441-442 (unweighted: data[...] <- round(apply(kNNs,2,numFun))); ?kNN numFun/weightDist docs at R/kNN.R:71-72,96-98 say nothing about integer targets or rounding.


## P5 (1 items)

### P5.1 [usability] Positive baseline worth preserving: first success, vimmi UX, MI guard-rail warning, and one-call flexibility all verified
*kind: usability | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/R/vimmi.R*

For calibration of the roadmap, these passed the new-user test and should be protected by tests: (1) vimpute(sleep) one-liner on a data.frame works, ~4s, imputes everything (total time-to-first-success ~5s incl. 0.96s load; mice load 0.95s — parity). (2) print.vimmi/summary.vimmi are self-explanatory (m, boot, uncert, per-variable NA counts+methods; summary adds between-imputation variance) — arguably nicer than mice's mids print. (3) complete() misuse errors are exemplary: complete(res,10) -> 'action must be between 1 and 5 (m).'; complete(res,'broad') -> "action must be an integer (1..m), 'all', or 'long'."; 'long' format is mice-compatible (.imp/.id) and mice::pool(with(res, lm(...))) works end-to-end. (4) vimpute(sleep, method='gam', m=5) with defaults warns 'm > 1 without boot/uncert/pmm: all imputations will be identical...' — exactly the right guard (minor nit: for stochastic learners like ranger/robust the imputations actually differ slightly, so the wording overstates; and pooling then silently proceeds with b=0). (5) The flagship flexibility claim holds in one call: vimpute(sleep, method=list(NonD='ranger',Dream='xgboost',Sleep='robust',Span='gam',Gest='ranger'), learner_params=list(ranger=list(num.trees=200)), sequential=FALSE) runs in 0.6s; partial method lists warn per unlisted variable and default sensibly; mice has no per-variable hyperparameters and no tuning.

**Evidence:** All commands run in exp1/exp4/exp5/exp6: timings 0.96s load/3.95s impute; print(res) vimmi header; complete() error strings verbatim; vimpute.R:340-342 warning fired for gam (b=0 verified via mice::pool: b column all 0) but ranger/robust m=5 defaults gave non-identical completions (identical(complete(res,1),complete(res,2))==FALSE).


## IDEA (5 items)

### IDEA.1 [deps-arch] IDEA: split-package architecture (VIM core + VIMlearn companion) -- measured verdict: keep mlr3 in Imports, diet the legacy deps instead
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: /Users/matthias/workspace/VIM/DESCRIPTION*

Measured cost of the mlr3 stack in Imports (mlr3, mlr3pipelines, mlr3tuning, mlr3learners, paradox, R6, future = 7 of 24 Imports): joint marginal 24 of 105 recursive deps (23%); 17 of the 50 namespaces loaded by library(VIM); total attach time 0.87 s elapsed on this machine -- real but modest. Split option: VIM keeps visualization + classic methods (kNN, hotdeck, irmi, cellwise family: zero mlr3 need), a companion (VIMlearn/VIMtune) gets vimpute/vimmi. Pros: light core for the large viz-only userbase and downstream reverse dependencies; isolates VIM's CRAN status from mlr3-ecosystem churn (the Batch-class rename is a live example); faster CI; per-package version pinning. Cons -- and why I recommend against: the strategic aim is that VIM-the-brand beats mice, and 'install VIM, call vimpute()' is the whole usability pitch -- a companion package reintroduces exactly the friction mice does not have; cross-package S3 (complete/with/as.mids on vimmi) and shared internals (helper_vimpute learners) create a maintenance seam; two CRAN release trains for one feature. The degrade-gracefully alternative (mlr3 stack to Suggests, requireNamespace inside vimpute) is worse still: it turns the flagship into an optional extra and load-time importFrom of six packages would have to become brittle runtime lookups. Recommended architecture: mlr3 stack stays in Imports with version pins (see pin finding); reclaim the footprint from the legacy side instead -- car (-55) + e1071 (-3) + sp/laeken (-2) takes the recursive tree from 105 to ~45 and the message becomes 'lighter than before 7.0 despite gaining an AutoML imputer'.

**Evidence:** Measurements on installed build: library(VIM) = 0.87 s, +50 namespaces; recursive hard deps 105 (excl base); mlr3-stack joint marginal 24 vs car alone 55; direct Depends+Imports = 26 (DESCRIPTION:15-41).

### IDEA.2 [mice] quadratic and ri (random-indicator) niche methods
*kind: method-gap (vs mice.impute.quadratic, mice.impute.ri) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Absent; both are rarely used and quadratic relationships are handled natively by ranger/xgboost/gam learners.

PROPOSAL: No action — document that nonlinearities are captured by the ML/GAM learners; revisit only if reviewers ask.

**Verifier:** Absent (grep zero hits for quadratic/random-indicator in R/ and NEWS.md). The no-action rationale is sound: nonlinearities are covered by ranger/xgboost/gam learners (vimpute.R:15-21). Note on the three spot-checked wins: (1) the robust-family win is accurate — robustboot standard/stratified/residual are genuinely implemented (helper_vimpute.R:1414-1480; 'psi'/'quantile' disabled with fallback warning) and robust learners registered — though it cites irmi(), which is deprecated in this very release (irmi.R:123); (2) the per-variable-tuning win is real (active TuningInstanceBatchSingleCrit code, vimpute.R:1201-1411, per-variable tune list) but inflated at the margins: tuning only fires when i == round(nseq/2) (vimpute.R:1201), so with sequential=FALSE or nseq=1 it silently never runs; (3) the convergence-early-stopping win is solid — check_convergence (helper_vimpute.R:2189-2244) breaks after two consecutive iterations with summed change < eps, wired at vimpute.R:2164-2183, and mice indeed has no stopping rule.

**Repro:** grep -rniE 'quadratic|random.indicator' R/ NEWS.md  # no hits

### IDEA.3 [competitors] Time-series / cross-section (longitudinal) imputation structure
*kind: method-gap (vs Amelia: ts/cs arguments, polytime/splinetime trends, lags/leads, intercs per-unit trends (verified locally, 1.8.3)) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: No time-aware imputation anywhere in VIM; users must hand-engineer lag features before calling vimpute

PROPOSAL: Do not build a TSCS engine; add a small helper that auto-generates lag/lead/trend features per unit as extra predictors for vimpute, and document the boundary (point users to Amelia/imputeTS for genuinely temporal problems).

REFERENCE: args(Amelia::amelia) verified locally

**Verifier:** No time-aware structure anywhere: grep for lag/lead/polytime/splinetime/longitudinal/time-series over R/*.R returns only unrelated matches ('Flag' in R/imputeCellReg.R:382, 'Zero-Flag' in R/vimpute.R:1667). No ts/cs arguments in any imputation function. Users must hand-engineer lag features as ordinary predictor columns before calling vimpute, as claimed.

### IDEA.4 [competitors] Deep-learning multiple imputation (denoising autoencoders)
*kind: method-gap (vs rMIDAS: MIDAS denoising-autoencoder MI, scales to very wide/large data, overimputation-based training diagnostic; Python/TensorFlow backend via reticulate) | verdict: CONFIRMED | confidence: -*

STATUS IN VIM: Nothing neural in VIM; all learners are classical ML/statistical

PROPOSAL: Do not chase this: the Python dependency contradicts VIM's dependency-light CRAN positioning. Revisit only if an R-native torch implementation becomes cheap; meanwhile position VIM's ranger/xgboost + tuning as the pragmatic high-dimensional answer.

REFERENCE: VERIFY: rMIDAS details from documented knowledge (Lall & Robinson, Political Analysis 2022); not installed

**Verifier:** Nothing neural in the package: grep for neural/autoencoder/torch/keras/tensorflow over R/ finds only a bibliographic reference string in a dataset help page (R/VIM-package.R:391, citing a feedforward-NN paper for the chorizonDL data). All learners are classical ML/statistical. The claim's own recommendation (do not chase this) is consistent with VIM's Suggests-guarded dependency posture.

### IDEA.5 [framework-design] IDEA: two-layer spec grammar — vs_*() constructors compiled from simputation-style formulas — as the public face of the mlr3 backend
*kind: design | verdict: unverified | confidence: high | file: R/vimpute.R*

The strategic pitch ('per-variable methods AND tuning via mlr3') deserves an interface that demos in three lines. Sketch of the full grammar unifying findings on spec fragmentation, predictors, and tuning: `imp <- vimpute(dat, Sleep ~ Dream + Span | ranger(num.trees = 500, tune = TRUE), Dream ~ . - NonD | gam(uncert = "pmm", pmm_k = 5), NonD ~ . | robust(donorcond = ">= 0"), .default = ranger(), m = 20, seed = 1)`. Compilation rules: LHS = target; RHS before `|` = predictor set (supports `.`, `-`, transformations for formula-capable methods; for ranger/xgboost it lowers to task$select(), giving predictorMatrix power to ML methods for free); after `|` = a vs_* spec constructor whose arguments are validated against the mlr3 param_set at call time. Each vs_*() returns list(method, params, tune, tune_space, uncert, pmm_k, formula_rhs, donorcond, makeNA) — the same structure register_vimpute_method() plugins register, so user-registered methods immediately participate in the grammar. This is the single change that would make vimpute visibly more ergonomic than mice's method + predictorMatrix + formulas + blocks in papers and teaching material; effort is contained because it is a pure front-end compiling to the existing per-variable containers.

**Evidence:** Builds on vimpute.R:154-176 (current 9-argument surface), helper_vimpute.R:552-880 (mapping helpers the grammar would compile into), vignettes/vimpute.Rmd:137-160 (current verbose setNames(as.list(rep(...))) idiom the grammar replaces)


## Verified wins (VIM ahead today)

- **[mice]** Robust imputation family: irmi(), imputeRobust(Chain)(), vimpute method='robust'/'robgam' (lmrob/glmrob/robust GAM learners, helper_vimpute.R:138-258) plus robust bootstrap strategies robustboot='stratified'/'residual' (vimpute.R:93-97) — mice 3.19 has zero robust methods
- **[mice]** Cellwise-robust family (imputeCellEM/MCD/IRMI/M/MM/Reg + imputeCellwise dispatcher, new 7.1.0) — no counterpart in mice or its ecosystem; unique selling point
- **[mice]** Per-variable hyperparameter tuning via mlr3tuning (vimpute tune=TRUE, globally or per variable, vimpute.R:82-86) — mice's rf/cart run with fixed defaults, no tuning anywhere
- **[mice]** Learner breadth in one call: ranger, xgboost, glmnet, robust lm/glm, GAM, robust GAM (vimpute.R:15-21) — mice needs external packages (mixgb) for xgboost and has no GAM method
- **[mice]** kNN() and hotdeck() with Gower distance (src/gowerD.cpp) for mixed numeric/categorical/ordinal data, donor conditions and weighted donors — mice has no distance-based donor methods at all (mice.impute.sample is a random draw)
- **[mice]** Missingness visualization suite: aggr, matrixplot, marginplot/marginmatrix, scattmatrixMiss, mosaicMiss, parcoordMiss, histMiss/spineMiss/barMiss, colormapMiss (~20 functions) vs mice's md.pattern + fluxplot
- **[mice]** Imputation-quality metrics built in: evaluation(), nrmse(), pfc(), msecor(), msecov() (R/evaluation.R) — mice ships no quality metrics
- **[mice]** Per-variable granularity for everything: method, pmm, pmm_k, pmm_k_method, learner_params (per-variable, per-method, or global), tune (vimpute.R:10-53) — finer than mice's method vector + blots
- **[mice]** Convergence-based early stopping of FCS iterations (eps threshold, vimpute.R:76-77) — mice always runs fixed maxit with no stopping rule
- **[mice]** Memory-efficient vimmi container (original data stored once + imputed values only, R/vimmi.R:11-16) with verified loss-free bridge to mice pooling via as.mids.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:264)
- **[mice]** makeNA parameter: declare coded values (e.g. -9, 'missing') as imputable per variable inside the imputation call (vimpute.R:63-67) — mice requires manual pre-recoding
- **[mice]** Richer PMM: k-donor aggregation via mean/median/random or arbitrary user function (pmm_k_method, vimpute.R:35-47) on top of mice-style single-draw PMM and midastouch
- **[mice]** Diagnostic raw material: imp_var indicator columns and pred_history full prediction traces across iterations (vimpute.R:78-81) — mice only stores chainMean/chainVar
- **[competitors]** Robust model-based imputation family is unmatched: irmi(), imputeRobust(), and 'robust'/'robgam' vimpute learners (R/helper_vimpute.R:997; R/irmi.R) — across all 13 scanned competitors only simputation::impute_rlm offers anything robust, and only as a single-model verb.
- **[competitors]** Cellwise-robust family (imputeCellEM/MCD/IRMI/M/MM/Reg + imputeCellwise dispatcher, new in 7.1.0) is unique in the entire R imputation landscape — no scanned competitor handles cellwise outliers during imputation at all.
- **[competitors]** Per-variable granularity beyond any rival: method, pmm, pmm_k, pmm_k_method, learner_params (per-variable/per-method/global), and tune can all be set per variable (R/vimpute.R:10-53,82-86); mice offers only a method vector, missForest/missRanger/mixgb fit one global model class.
- **[competitors]** Real per-variable hyperparameter tuning with a tuned-vs-default guardrail (keeps defaults if tuning doesn't beat them, R/vimpute.R:1264-1301) and data-size-adaptive search spaces (R/helper_vimpute.R:2346-2413) — only mlim attempts this, and it drags in h2o/Java.
- **[competitors]** Broadest MI uncertainty menu: uncert = none/normalerror/resid/pmm/midastouch (covariate-distance-weighted PMM), R/helper_vimpute.R:1774-1815 — missRanger has PMM only, missForest nothing, mixgb PMM variants only.
- **[competitors]** Robust bootstrap for MI: robustboot = standard/stratified/residual (R/vimpute.R:89-97) — no competitor offers outlier-aware resampling for between-imputation variability.
- **[competitors]** vimmi is a memory-efficient MI container (stores only imputed cells, not m full copies) with complete()/with()/as.mids.vimmi() -> mice::pool() verified working end-to-end this audit (R/vimmi.R:115-186,264-283).
- **[competitors]** 16+ imputation-aware visualization functions (aggr, marginplot, matrixplot, mosaicMiss, parcoordMiss, ... with delimiter-based highlighting of imputed cells) — the richest pre/post-imputation visual toolkit in the scan; no competitor comes close for single-dataset diagnostics.
- **[competitors]** Donor-based classics with unique control: kNN() with Gower distance for mixed types, per-variable weights, custom aggregation and donorcond; hotdeck() with ord_var/domain_var within-domain donor search (R/hotdeck.R:79).
- **[competitors]** makeNA + donorcond in vimpute (R/vimpute.R:63-71,196-259) let users declare coded missings and donor-eligibility conditions — only Hmisc::aregImpute's constraint argument is comparable (verified in Hmisc 5.2.5).
- **[competitors]** Good MI UX guardrail: explicit warning when m>1 is requested with no source of between-imputation variability (boot/uncert/pmm all off), R/vimpute.R:340-343.
- **[competitors]** GAM + robust GAM learners with automatic smooth-term construction (R/helper_vimpute.R:2419ff) give aregImpute-class spline flexibility plus robustness aregImpute lacks.
- **[competitors]** Measured wall-clock parity with the fastest rival: vimpute ranger nseq=3 took 79.6s vs missRanger 2.6.1 default-convergence 82.8s at n=3000, p=15, 10% MCAR (this audit) — the mlr3 overhead is only visible on tiny data (4.5s vs 1.4s at n=1000, p=4).

## Parity

- **[mice]** PMM and midastouch: vimpute pmm=TRUE / uncert='pmm'/'midastouch' (vimpute.R:98-105) matches mice.impute.pmm/midastouch
- **[mice]** Random-forest imputation: rangerImpute / vimpute method='ranger' vs mice.impute.rf (VIM adds tuning — see wins)
- **[mice]** Regularized (lasso) imputation: method='regularized' (glmnet, regression + classification) vs mice.impute.lasso.norm/lasso.logreg/lasso.select.*
- **[mice]** Bootstrap MI: boot=TRUE ≈ mice norm.boot/logreg.boot parameter-uncertainty mechanism
- **[mice]** Stochastic draws: uncert='normalerror'/'resid' ≈ norm.nob-style noise; uncert='none' ≈ norm.predict (deterministic); neither package makes fully Bayesian draws mandatory
- **[mice]** Categorical imputation (binary and multiclass) via classif learners (ranger/xgboost/glmnet/glm_rob) ≈ logreg/polyreg/lda — except ordinal, see gaps
- **[mice]** Chained FCS iteration: sequential=TRUE, nseq ≈ mice maxit loop (VIM adds eps early stop)
- **[mice]** complete() with integer/'all'/'long' actions (R/vimmi.R:96-156) matches mice::complete semantics
- **[mice]** with() across imputations: with.vimmi returns a plain list that mice::pool() accepts (verified: pooled lm estimates OK) ≈ with.mids/mira workflow
- **[mice]** Formula-based model specification per variable (vimpute formula list, vimpute.R:54-62) ≈ mice formulas interface — but only for regularized/robust/gam/robgam methods
- **[competitors]** PMM on ML predictions: vimpute pmm=TRUE / uncert='pmm' (k donors, random draw, default k=5 for uncert path; R/helper_vimpute.R:1769-1803) is functionally equivalent to missRanger pmm.k (verified 2.6.1), mixgb pmm.type/pmm.k, and miceRanger meanMatch.
- **[competitors]** Iterative chained imputation with convergence stopping (sequential/nseq/eps, R/vimpute.R:72-77,505) matches mice maxit and missForest/missRanger early-stopping loops.
- **[competitors]** Bootstrap-based MI: vimpute boot=TRUE per imputation parallels Amelia's EMB bootstrap (verified 1.8.3) and mixgb's bootstrap flag — VIM applies it to any of its 6 learners rather than a multivariate-normal model.
- **[competitors]** Random-forest imputation accuracy: vimpute/rangerImpute use the same ranger backend as missForest (ranger backend option, verified 1.6.1) and missRanger; measured NRMSE in the same ballpark once PMM noise injection is accounted for.
- **[competitors]** XGBoost imputation core: xgboostImpute()/vimpute 'xgboost' matches mixgb's single-dataset engine; mixgb is ahead only on MI ergonomics (m, save.models, GPU) — covered in gaps.
- **[competitors]** Rubin pooling: VIM delegates to mice via as.mids.vimmi (R/vimmi.R:264-283) exactly as miceRanger and mixgb delegate pooling to mice — verified working with mice 3.19.0.
- **[competitors]** Regularized regression imputation: vimpute 'regularized' (glmnet/cv_glmnet with tuned alpha/lambda, R/helper_vimpute.R:2350-2365) matches simputation::impute_en and the ELNET core of mlim.
